### ISSUE #2023 [OPEN] — Tiered decomposition as the architecture: sparse_dict linear bulk (Tier 1, K~10⁴) + evidence-K curved atoms (Tier 2) on the whitened residual, with a residual-factor ↔ linear ↔ curved migration ledger replacing PC reseeding
Author: SauersML   Created: 2026-07-01T22:56:25Z   Labels: 
Comments: 18
------------------------------------------------------------------------
BODY:
## Thesis
Make the tier split the architecture rather than a rescue path. Four measured facts point at the same design:
- #1893: the co-collapse *recovery* reseeds from ~p principal components, guaranteeing re-collapse at K≫p — data rows are unlimited but PCs cap at p, so the recovery mechanism is the failure mechanism.
- #1995: the joint arrow-Schur at ~130 s/iter (K=128) is the wrong tool for large K; external TopK trains K=2,000 in the time this fits 128.
- #1801 Bug B: the JumpReLU optimization band keeps all K atoms in the compact block — per-token cost O(K), not O(k_active), which breaks the invariant any large-K claim rests on.
- The EV-vs-K analysis already concluded the hybrid is the end state; today it is bolted on inside one joint solver where linear atoms are curved atoms with zero curvature, which is why K=2,000 is unreachable.

Also a statistical point, not just a performance one: ~2,000 distinct *certified* 1-manifolds in p≈48 dimensions with ~40k tokens is not an evidence-supportable object. Curved K should be **discovered** (birth/death), not preset.

## Architecture
- **Tier 0**: mean + the rogue high-norm directions (measured carrying 85–99% of raw variance) as fixed linear atoms / preprocessing.
- **Tier 1**: the `sparse_dict` collapsed-linear lane — already built and GPU-routed — promoted from collapse-rescue to the *primary* bulk model at K ~ 10⁴, trained by the classical fast machinery.
- **Tier 2**: curved atoms at evidence-chosen K (tens), fit by the certified REML machinery on the Tier-1 residual.

**Coupling (the unification with #2021)**: initialize/couple the structured-residual Λ to Tier 1's active subspace — the linear dictionary *is* the interference model for the curved fit. Alternate tiers to joint stationarity. The joint arrow-Schur becomes terminal polish + certificate over the small curved block; the workhorse is block-coordinate per-atom exact REML on assigned rows' sufficient statistics — embarrassingly parallel, O(K) per sweep. (Hypothesis to measure, not assume: with Tier 1 + Λ absorbing shared variance, curved atoms' effective co-assignment overlap drops enough that block-coordinate is near-exact; report the polish step's correction size as the check.)

## Migration ledger (replaces reseeding)
One three-state ledger with evidence-adjudicated moves: **residual factor ↔ linear atom ↔ curved atom**.
- Promotion: run the d=1 chart fit on a persistent Λ factor or an Ising community of Tier-1 atoms; promote if evidence prefers the curve.
- Demotion: the existing hybrid-split Θ→0 verdict, applied at the tier boundary instead of inside the joint solver.
- Death: back into Λ. Dead-atom resampling draws from high-residual data rows (k-SVD replacement rule, objective non-increasing) — never from PCs.

## Invariant to enforce while in there
Compact-block sizing uses the hard gate so per-token cost tracks k_active (fixes #1801 Bug B as a structural invariant, not a patch); the wide band prices only value-consistent prior terms.

## Acceptance
- K=2,000 on the #1893 benchmark: Tier 1 alone ties the external TopK baseline **by construction** (same algorithm class), Tier 2 adds EV on top — the parity criterion met with margin, and the interesting deltas move to the #1942 disentanglement/dose metrics where curved atoms actually differentiate.
- Wall-clock: end-to-end fit at K_linear=10⁴, K_curved≈20 in less time than today's K=128 joint solve.
- No PC reseed events in the log; migration ledger accounts for every birth/death.

Related: #1893 (this is the structural form of its fix plan), #1995, #1801, #1911, #2021 (Λ coupling), #2022 (quotient makes per-atom evidence comparable), #2011 (routing-stack Rust ports feed Tier-1/T2 alternation).

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-02T20:40:12Z ---
2026-07-02: a large slice of this architecture shipped and is measured.

**Landed on main:**
- Tier-1 block-sparse dictionary lane: `sparse_dict/block.rs` (blocks of b atoms, column-orthonormal Grassmann frames via the existing `GrassmannFrame::polar_update`, block-TopK on ‖z_g‖₂, signed codes, gate/amplitude decoupled, AuxK revival from worst-residual ROWS) — `a6f2c0e28`/`097b1c1de`/`a830fab3a`; 17/17 tests green including a gauge-invariance test with negative control.
- Streaming surface `block_stream.rs` (`f820166c8`): partial_fit over bf16 residual shards → same fixed point as one-shot; the node driver `examples/stream_block_t1.py` consumes the 42M-token qwen3_32b_fineweb harvest format directly.
- The Tier-1→Tier-2 seam: per-block seed manifests (basis + in-block coords + firing/utilization stats), `compose_tiers.py --t1-mode block` → one K=1 curved chart per block → additive composition (`5bc705aef`, `ddf620afa`).

**Measured (Manifold-SAE/experiments/block_nursery/, held-out, review-validated):** unsupervised block discovery ≈ oracle at n=480 (EV 0.834 vs 0.833), 3/3 planted planes found, 3/3 rings reconstructed 0.89–0.93 EV; joint torch K=3 got EV 0.756 recovering 1/3. Inside a block: one curved coordinate = 0.94 of a circle's variance vs 0.52 for one linear coordinate. Discovery is sample-sensitive below n≈480 (mis-segments at n=210) — tracked in Manifold-SAE#3.

**Convergence note:** the same sequential-deflation principle now also fixes the joint fit's cold start (7a93b1d06) — the "migration ledger replacing PC reseeding" direction this issue proposes is corroborated from two sides.

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-03T04:02:29Z ---
**Empirical result: the stagewise/joint curved tier co-collapses; the scalable primitive is per-block K=1. Data + proposed path.**

Ran a stagewise scaling sweep on a fresh HEAD wheel (0.1.247 @ 2c7fec4e, includes the pca_seed rank-collapse fix 3254a3e0a), narrow p=16, 6 planted circles (circle_subspace_ev=0.986, all real), to isolate distinctness from the O(p³) width cost:

| K | k_fit | ev | μ̂_max | n_distinct | n_collapsed_pairs | factors_recovered |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 2 | 3 | 0.577 | 0.656 | 3 | 0 | 2 |
| 4 | 5 | 0.593 | 0.912 | 4 | 1 | 2 |
| 6 | 7 | 0.593 | 0.99997 | 4 | 6 | 2 |
| 8 | 9 | 0.594 | 0.99999 | 4 | 15 | 2 |
| 12 | 13 | 0.594 | 0.99999 | 4 | 45 | 2 |

**Stagewise growth does NOT scale**: it recovers only 2 of 6 factors no matter how many atoms are born; μ̂_max → 1.0 by K=6; collapsed pairs explode O(K²); most atoms degenerate to rank-1 dead lines. EV stays a deceptive 0.59 throughout (co-collapse is EV-invisible, per #2082 — reporting EV alone would call this a success). The pca_seed fix corrected the *joint cold-start* but did not transfer to stagewise residual-births.

**Architecture findings:**
- `compose_tiers` is only an example script (`examples/compose_tiers.py`), not a library API. It composes T1 (linear `sparse_dictionary_fit`, scales fine) + T2 = one small curved `sae_manifold_fit` on the residual — i.e. T2 is the same joint curved fit that co-collapses. The current tiered design just relocates co-collapse into T2.
- `merge_tiers` IS real Rust (`construction.rs:158`) — the assembly primitive works; it's the T2 *fitting* that's broken.

**Proposed principled path to K=32k** (testing now): a single K=1 curved atom converges fast (62s) and cannot co-collapse with itself. So instead of fitting K curved atoms in a shared/full residual space, fit **K independent K=1 curved atoms, each confined to its own small discovered block** (project residual onto the block's 2–8-dim basis, fit K=1 curved there, lift the decoder back, `merge_tiers` to assemble). Distinctness becomes structural (different blocks can't merge), width cost is bounded per atom, and it's embarrassingly parallel — so K=32k = "T1 discovers 32k small blocks + 32k parallel K=1 curved fits + merge." Running the oracle-block validation now; if per-block K=1 keeps μ̂ low and recovers all factors, this is the scaling primitive and the joint/stagewise curved fit can be retired for scale-out. **Infra ask if it validates:** expose a real `fit_per_block_curved_tier` + `merge_tiers` Python surface (the K=1-per-block orchestration currently lives only in an example).

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-08T01:25:50Z ---
## Update: the tiered joint co-fit primitive landed (`391583459`, `crates/gam-sae/src/sparse_dict/cofit.rs`)

The Jul-3 finding here was that the stagewise/joint curved tier co-collapses because the curved charts are fit to an LS residual **orthogonal to the structure they seek** (residual-orthogonality trap). That specific mechanism now has a direct implementation:

`feat(sae): tiered linear+curved joint co-fit (two-block coordinate descent closing the residual-orthogonality trap)` — commit **`391583459`**, +813 lines in `crates/gam-sae/src/sparse_dict/cofit.rs` (plus `outer_objective.rs` +303, `description_length.rs` +128, FFI + Python plumbing). The linear bulk tier (Tier 1) and curved chart tier (Tier 2) now descend **one penalised joint objective `J(codes, charts)` with monotone alternation** instead of the sequential residual-factor path — exactly the "shared objective, not orthogonal residual" fix this issue called for.

Related supporting landings on the same architecture: `f46b1bccf` (Jeffreys −½logdet F anti-collapse barrier — the co-collapse penalty this tier needs), matched description-length surface `86c588684`/`a06cbd36e` (the curved-vs-flat migration ledger in bits), and stratum-local stagewise births `15de9f3d3`.

**Not closing** — this is the architecture epic; the migration ledger (residual-factor ↔ linear ↔ curved) and the K~10⁴ Tier-1 scaling arm are still in progress, and the co-fit path has not yet been CI-measured against the planted-circle co-collapse sweep (last full Rust CI `c22d838fb` predates `391583459`). Next: validate the co-fit lane clears the co-collapse the stagewise path could not (the residual-notes-below-linear-PCA-floor observation in #2132).

## Component status matrix vs live HEAD (`f645cbe97`)

Audited each architecture component the issue defines against the source (read-only, no compile). Verdict up front: **Tier-0 and Tier-1 are real and strong; the defining unification — a production path that runs Tier-1 then fits curved atoms on the Tier-1 residual, adjudicated by a migration ledger that replaces PC reseeding — is NOT wired end-to-end. The T1→T2 handoff is a defined-but-unconstructed type, the only curved-on-residual fitter (`cofit`) has no caller, and PC reseeding still cold-starts the curved fit.**

| component (as the issue defines it) | status | evidence |
|---|---|---|
| **Tier 0** — shared mean + rogue high-norm directions as fixed atoms/preprocessing | **LANDED** | `tiered::Tier0Mean`, `PerContextMean`, `Tier05SinkAtom` (attention-sink, peeled pre-charting) in `crates/gam-sae/src/tiered/mod.rs`; manifold-tier analogue wired at `manifold/term.rs:724`, `construction.rs:1026`. ⚠️ regression test `tests_tier0_shared_mean_2023::tier0_makes_dc_zombie_ev_invisible_six_circles` is **red** in the latest CI (`04a117dab`). |
| **Tier 1** — `sparse_dict` collapsed-linear bulk at K~10⁴, GPU-routed, primary model | **LANDED (strongest component)** | `sparse_dict/block.rs` (Grassmann-frame blocks, block-TopK, signed codes), `block_stream.rs` streaming partial_fit; TopK hard-support build mode (`15fd89c17`/`fdcb95bc1`/`2692ba663`); measured block discovery ≈ oracle (EV 0.834 vs 0.833). Dead-atom revival draws from **worst-residual rows** (not PCs) — reseeding retired *in this lane*. |
| **Tier 2** — curved atoms at evidence-K on the Tier-1 residual | **PARTIAL / not wired** | Two realizations, neither production-reachable: **(a) sequential handoff** — `WhitenedResidualHandoff` struct is **defined but never constructed** (no producer) and **never consumed** (no Tier-2 code reads it); `prechart_residual` only does Tier-0/0.5, stopping before T1/T2; `compose_tiers.py` is an example script, not a library API. **(b) joint co-fit** — `cofit_block_and_curved` (`sparse_dict/cofit.rs`, `391583459`) implements the two-block coordinate descent, but its **only references are the module re-export and its own file — zero callers**, and it is **not FFI-exposed**. |
| **Coupling with #2021** — init/couple structured-residual Λ to Tier-1's active subspace; fit T2 on the whitened residual | **PARTIAL** | `interference_subspace()` computes Tier-1's active subspace `Q` — but is **DIAGNOSTIC ONLY** (the code explicitly forbids `Q⊥`-weighting the T2 residual as a proven design error; T2 is meant to fit the RAW residual). #2021 whitening is engaged for the joint SAE fit, but there is no tiered driver that installs Λ from Tier-1 and hands a residual to a curved tier. |
| **Migration ledger** — three-state residual-factor ↔ linear ↔ curved, evidence-adjudicated, accounts for every birth/death | **PARTIAL / scattered** | The *pieces* exist: `structure_harvest::BirthSeed::ResidualFactor` + `born_atom`/`apply_structure_move` (promotion residual-factor→curved), matched description-length in bits (`description_length.rs`, the migration currency), `hybrid_split` Θ→0 (demotion). But there is **no unified three-state ledger object**, and these moves operate **inside the joint solver**, not at the tier boundary as the issue specifies. |
| **PC-reseed retirement** — no PC reseed events; deaths resample from high-residual rows | **PARTIAL — not retired for the curved fit** | Retired in the T1 block lane (worst-residual-row AuxK revival). But `sae_pca_seed_initial_coords[_with_pc_offset]` **still cold-starts the curved manifold fit** (`manifold/fit_drivers.rs:2891,3445`, `seed_cold_start_disjoint_charts`). The `3254a3e0a` pca_seed rank-collapse fix improved it; it did not remove it. |
| **#1801 Bug B invariant** — compact-block sizing tracks k_active via the hard gate | **LANDED (adjacent)** | `front_door::admit_topk_manifold` routes K>P to `SaeFitLane::CurvedStreaming` with a `SaeTopKCurvedBudget` memory ledger; the **silent `SparseDictionaryFit` demotion at K>P is retired** (`6f21d761f` "kill the silent linear substitution", 2026-07-08). (This is a *budget* ledger, not the *migration* ledger above.) |

### Acceptance criteria
| criterion | status |
|---|---|
| K=2,000 on #1893: Tier-1 ties external TopK by construction, Tier-2 adds EV | **Tier-1 half plausible-by-construction** (same algorithm class, TopK build landed); **no end-to-end tiered K=2,000 number** because no T1→T2 driver exists. Measured curved tier at scale still **co-collapses** (stagewise sweep: 2 of 6 factors recovered regardless of K; `cofit` not yet CI-measured against that sweep). |
| Wall-clock: K_linear=10⁴ + K_curved≈20 < today's K=128 joint | **NOT MEASURED** (nothing orchestrates it). |
| No PC reseed events; ledger accounts every birth/death | **NOT MET** (pca_seed still present; no unified ledger). |

### Biggest missing piece
The **end-to-end tiered orchestration driver**, exposed to production/Python: fit Tier-1 → construct the `WhitenedResidualHandoff` → run Tier-2 curved birth/death on that residual → adjudicate via a real migration ledger. Today the handoff is an unwired stub type, the joint curved fitter (`cofit`) has no caller and no FFI, and the curved fit still PCA-seeds. **Where it plugs in:** a `fit_tiered(...)` in `tiered/mod.rs` that (1) calls the existing `sparse_dict` Tier-1, (2) builds the already-defined `WhitenedResidualHandoff`, (3) drives `cofit_block_and_curved` (or a per-block K=1 curved fit) on `handoff.residual`, (4) records moves in a three-state ledger replacing `sae_pca_seed_*` at the curved cold-start — then FFI-expose it.

### How real vs aspirational
- **Real (~50%):** Tier-0 preprocessing, the Tier-1 linear-bulk lane (the load-bearing scaling win), the co-fit *primitive*, the interference-subspace diagnostic, and the K>P silent-demotion retirement.
- **Aspirational / stub (~50%):** the tiered *composition itself* — T1→T2-on-residual as a wired production path, the unified migration ledger, and PC-reseed retirement for the curved tier. The architecture's central claim ("make the tier split the architecture, not a rescue path") is **not yet realized in a runnable end-to-end path**; the components are built but not assembled. **Keep open.**


--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-08T16:34:26Z ---
## Landed: the end-to-end `fit_tiered` orchestration + FFI (the gap this issue tracked)

Following the component matrix above, the missing assembly is now built and committed on local `main` (no push; MSI-verified by the lead).

### What landed
**Increment 1 — the driver** (`crates/gam-sae/src/tiered/fit.rs`, `fit_tiered`):
- **Tier-0**: `Tier0Mean` peel, `R0 = z − μ`.
- **Tier-1**: `fit_block_sparse_dictionary` on `R0` (the block lane, so the routing is exactly what the co-fit consumes).
- **Tier-2**: `cofit_block_and_curved(R0, tier1.decoder/blocks/codes/gamma)` — its round 0 **is** curved-on-linear-residual and its A/B alternation drives the joint objective to stationarity. This is the "run Tier-1 then fit curved atoms on the Tier-1 residual" path the matrix reported did not exist.
- **Migration ledger** (`MigrationLedger` + `TieredMoveKind{Promotion,Demotion,Death}`): promotions/demotions are read from the co-fit's per-round `n_accepted_charts` deltas with the matched-DL `curved_charge` currency; deaths from `tier1.block_utilization == 0`. **`pc_reseed_events` is pinned `0` by construction** — the curved tier seeds from the Tier-1 routing/residual, never principal components, so the "no PC reseed events" acceptance bar holds structurally.

**Increment 2 — production consumer + Python surface** (commit `0b183f671`):
- `sae_manifold_fit_tiered` pyfunction (`latent/sae_spectral_ffi.rs`, registered in `manifold/geometry_ffi.rs`), thin marshalling over `gam::terms::sae::tiered::fit_tiered`; returns composed EV, Tier-0 mean, Tier-1 decoder/blocks/utilization/EV, Tier-2 co-fit EV + round/chart counts, and the ledger as columnar arrays (move-kind legend `0/1/2`, `dl_bits`, `pc_reseed_events`).
- Thin gamfit facade `sae_manifold_fit_tiered` + `TieredFitResult` (`_sae_spectral.py`), re-exported from `__init__.py`.
- **Acceptance test** `tiered_beats_linear_on_six_circle_mixture_and_records_a_promotion`: a 6-circle + linear-bulk synthetic where the tiered fit must beat the pure-linear Tier-1 EV **and** the ledger must record ≥1 curved promotion.

### Design note — why the `WhitenedResidualHandoff` stays unused
`cofit_block_and_curved` already implements the residual protocol (round 0 fits curved on the linear residual; the RAW-residual, evidence-priced anti-rechasing this issue's `InterferenceSubspace` doc mandates). Hand-constructing `WhitenedResidualHandoff` and a separate curved driver would duplicate that engine, so the co-fit is wired as the Tier-2 engine directly. The handoff struct remains available for a future streaming/out-of-sample split.

### Held: increment 3 (retire the curved cold-start's PC seed)
Replacing `sae_pca_seed_initial_coords` (`fit_drivers.rs:2891,3445`) with `BirthSeed::ResidualFactor` promotion for the tiered path is scoped but **held**: `fit_drivers.rs`/`construction.rs` carry active foreign hunks, and the direct curved path must stay untouched to avoid colliding with live lanes. The tiered driver already never PC-reseeds (it routes through the block lane + co-fit), so this increment only affects the *manifold-term* curved cold-start, which is orthogonal to the tiered path's guarantee.

### Read on the red `tier0_makes_dc_zombie_ev_invisible_six_circles`
**Distinct defect, not explained or fixed by this orchestration work.** It exercises the *manifold-term* Tier-0 (`SaeManifoldTerm::fit_tier0_mean` + `per_atom_loao_explained_variance`, `construction.rs:3432`), not the `sparse_dict` block lane / co-fit the driver uses. Its sibling `tier0_fit_demeans_and_reconstruction_adds_mean_back` passes, so `fit_tier0_mean`'s de-meaning is correct; the failure is in the leave-one-atom-out EV assertion — most likely the LOAO reconstruction's Tier-0 mean add-back is inconsistent between the full and drop-one reconstructions, so the DC zombie's ΔEV does not collapse to ≤1e-6 with Tier-0 on. It lives in `construction.rs`, which currently carries foreign hunks, so I am **not** folding a fix here. The test's own `eprintln` prints the off/on ΔEV — the MSI run will pinpoint which assertion trips; recommend routing this defect to a construction.rs owner once the tree is clean.

## Close-audit verification (read-only, HEAD `a6dbd67a7`) — not closing, one prior claim is now stale

Verified `0b183f671` ("FFI-expose the tiered fit + planted 6-circle acceptance test") is an ancestor of HEAD and its diff matches the claim: it added `sae_manifold_fit_tiered` to `crates/gam-pyffi/src/latent/sae_spectral_ffi.rs`, registered it in `manifold/geometry_ffi.rs`, and added the `gamfit._sae_spectral.TieredFitResult` facade.

**But that public surface no longer exists at HEAD.** A later commit, `b53bd1357` ("feat(sae #2232): remove public tiered surface; tiered = seed policy + alternation cadence (Increment 4)"), explicitly deletes it:
- the FFI `sae_manifold_fit_tiered` pyfunction + its `geometry_ffi.rs` registration,
- the `gamfit._sae_spectral.TieredFitResult` dataclass + wrapper + legend constants + the two `gamfit.__init__` re-exports.

Confirmed by grep on current HEAD: `sae_manifold_fit_tiered` has zero references anywhere under `crates/gam-pyffi/` or `gamfit/`. `crates/gam-sae/src/tiered/fit.rs::fit_tiered` still exists but is now doc-marked **internal (in-crate) only**; per `b53bd1357`'s message, the tiered flow's one public expression is `examples/compose_tiers.py` (linear warm-start via `sparse_dictionary_fit` then curved alternation via `sae_manifold_fit`) — which is exactly the "compose_tiers.py is only an example script, not a library API" gap this issue originally identified, now true again after a round-trip through FFI-exposed-then-removed.

Additionally, per the thread's own account: **Increment 3 (retiring `sae_pca_seed_initial_coords` as the curved cold-start for the direct manifold-term path) is explicitly held**, and the regression test `tests_tier0_shared_mean_2023::tier0_makes_dc_zombie_ev_invisible_six_circles` was reported red and its fix was not folded in (cannot confirm current pass/fail red-only from source reading).

Against this issue's own acceptance bar: no end-to-end K=2,000 wall-clock/tie-by-construction measurement exists (only a synthetic 6-circle acceptance test), and "no PC reseed events" holds only for the tiered path's *internal* orchestrator, not for the direct curved-fit cold start generally.

**Not closing.** Residual: (1) the tiered fit has no Python-reachable production entry point at current HEAD (removed by `b53bd1357` for an unrelated unification reason — Increment 5 of #2232 is expected to fold `cofit_block_and_curved` into `sae_manifold_fit`'s own inner driver, at which point this issue's architecture becomes literally true without a separate surface, but that fold has not landed), (2) Increment 3 (PC-reseed retirement for the direct path) is held, (3) no measured K=2,000 wall-clock/tie acceptance number exists.


--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-11T04:10:25Z ---
## K=2,000 acceptance measurement + tier0 gate status (MSI, pinned 8eb0b88c6)

### K=2,000 Tier-1 linear-bulk measurement — the acceptance number this issue asked for

Ran `examples/tiered_gpu_scale` (the composed `fit_tiered` spine that drives the block-sparse Tier-1 at high K) on MSI, 32-core CPU router, `--gpu off`. Device admission is `minibatch·K`-gated and below break-even here (`1,024,000 < 1,048,576`), so the CPU oracle is the honest portable baseline; the routing lane is byte-identical to the device path. Deterministic planted corpus: **N=32,768, P=64**, 8 shared linear directions + per-row wobble.

**K=2,000, block-size b=1 (== TopK by construction), block-TopK k=16:**

| epochs | wall (32 cores) | Tier-1 EV | frame-projector residual | fixed-point certified? |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| 3  | **16 s** | **0.8541** | 1.000 | no |
| 10 | 33 s | 0.8281 | 1.000 | no |
| 30 | 99 s | 0.7653 | 1.000 | no |

Comparison at the **same K=2,000, b=4** (500 blocks × 4), 30 epochs: EV 0.8272, frame residual 0.967, 77 s — also uncertified.

**Tie-by-construction: confirmed (algebraic).** At b=1 each block is a singleton, so the block gate `‖z_g‖₂` over a one-element slot is exactly `|z|` and block-TopK collapses to scalar TopK on the codes (`sparse_dict::block::stored_code_gate`). The K=2,000 b=1 run *is* a TopK SAE by construction, no approximation.

**Honest certificate caveat — a real, documentable finding.** The block lane's fixed-point certificate does **not** close at K=2,000 on this corpus, and EV *degrades* with epochs (0.854 → 0.765). Root: the corpus has intrinsic rank ≈ 8 but K=2,000 atoms, so ~1,984 atoms are spurious and perpetually under-utilised → dead-block AuxK revival reseeds a block's Grassmann frame onto worst-residual rows every epoch, flipping it orthogonally → the frame-projector fixed-point residual is pinned at ~1.0 (exactly 1.0 at b=1) and never reaches the 1e-6 tolerance, and the revival churn erodes EV. This is the **K ≫ intrinsic-rank / K ≫ active-budget** class (#2134-adjacent): the certificate is well-posed only when K is commensurate with recoverable structure. EV = 0.854 at 3 epochs is the best fixed point; further epochs churn rather than converge. The headline is **EV 0.854 at K=2,000, b=1, 16 s** with the certificate open for the stated structural reason.

**Tier-2 adds EV — not separately measurable on this corpus.** `fit_tiered` runs Tier-1 to a certified fixed point before handing its residual to the Tier-2 curved co-fit; since Tier-1 does not certify at K=2,000 here, Tier-2 never runs (the `--tier2` run reports the same Tier-1 error, 97 s). Independently, the example's planted data is purely **linear** (8 shared directions), so a curved Tier-2 has no curved structure to add on this corpus by design. A clean Tier-2-adds-EV measurement needs (a) a K commensurate with structure so Tier-1 certifies and (b) planted curved factors — flagging as the remaining measurement.

### Tier-0 gate (3 red tests) — roots found; all three are TEST-side, fixes landed

Exact status at 8eb0b88c6 (`--no-fail-fast`): `tier0_fit_demeans_and_reconstruction_adds_mean_back` **passes**; the other three fail. Both roots are test-side, not the deep convergence work.

**(1,2) `primary_entry_installs_tier0_mean_on_raw_target` + `primary_entry_tier0_is_a_noop_on_centered_target`.** These fit a K=1 Periodic atom to a clean 8-point circle, which reconstructs `[cosθ, sinθ]` to machine precision → pass-0 residual ≈ 0. The always-on **structured-residual outer pass** (`fit_entry.rs:555`, gated only on `structured_passes>0 && metric_provenance=="Euclidean"` — **not** on the tests' `run_outer_rho_search:false` / `run_structure_search:false`) then fits a residual-covariance model on ~0 residual: its idiosyncratic diagonal collapses to the denormal floor, whitening by ~1/D is near-singular, and the whitened REML over the 3 smoothing ρ has no interior stationary point → the outer optimizer **correctly refuses** to certify (`projected gradient 1.647e-1` vs `bound 5.018e-4`; confirmed by a direct gradient probe). Genuinely non-identifiable config, correct refusal — do not weaken the cert.

Fix (`dafd515d6`, test-config only): give the two fixtures real above-floor residual energy — a denser 64-point circle + small deterministic iid noise (σ = 0.05) — so the structured pass is well-posed. μ stays the exact column mean; the μ≈OFFSET / μ≈0 tolerances are widened to the noise's finite-sample band (std σ/√N ≈ 6e-3).

**(3) `tier0_makes_dc_zombie_ev_invisible_six_circles`.** The Tier-0 **headline property passes** (`DC-zombie ΔEV: off = 50.57 survivor, on = 0.0000 invisible`). The failure was a secondary check: each genuine circle's leave-one-atom-out ΔEV came out ≈ −0.14 (fixture expects ≈ +0.16). Root: the hand-built fixture loaded the periodic basis rows **swapped** — `PeriodicHarmonicEvaluator`'s column order is `[1, sin 2πt, cos 2πt]` (basis.rs:300), but the decoder put sin into the cos output dim and cos into the sin dim, so each circle reconstructed a swapped `(sinθ, cosθ)` circle uncorrelated with the target `(cosθ, sinθ)` → spuriously negative ΔEV. A test-fixture bug, **not** the `per_atom_loao_explained_variance` production defect previously suspected. Fix (`bc817f642`, test-fixture only): swap the two decoder rows.

MSI verification of all three at the combined HEAD is in flight; both fixes are landed on `main`.

### Production robustness bug surfaced (separate from #2023, worth a ticket)
The structured-residual pass runs on **every** SAE fit (magic-by-default) with **no absolute residual-energy floor** — so any real fit that explains its target near-exactly hits the same non-certification. Principled guard: `sae_structured_residual_model` returns `None` when total residual energy is below an absolute precision/noise floor (nothing to whiten → degrade to the pass-0 iid fit), or an absolute floor on the idiosyncratic diagonal in `residual_factor.rs`. Owner TBD (fit-driver surface).

### Residual mechanical gap: sparse_dict has no CPU small-block baseline path

From the wide-p feasibility deep-dive (#2134 closed its p/N-scaling and top_k>1 walls; this one is the honest remainder):

`route_minibatch_required` (`crates/gam-sae/src/sparse_dict/scoring_gpu.rs:568,606`) **refuses any block with `m·k < DEVICE_SCORE_BLOCK_MIN_ELEMS = 1048576`** (`scoring_gpu.rs:435`). The guard lives in *routing*, so `score_mode="off"` does not lift it. Net effect: a small-K CPU baseline cannot run through the transform lane (the Python default `required` overrides the flipped FFI default), which blocks small-K CPU A/B comparisons against the frontier.

A `score_block_cpu` path already exists (`crates/gam-sae/src/sparse_dict/mod.rs:79`), so the fix is either:
- a documented minimum-K contract, or
- route small blocks (`< DEVICE_SCORE_BLOCK_MIN_ELEMS`) to `score_block_cpu` instead of fail-closed.

CPU-verifiable, low-risk — but it changes a **deliberate GPU fail-closed device contract**, so it wants an explicit decision rather than a silent flip.

For contrast, the wide-p **cubic-in-width cost is already retired**: Grassmann frames (`ensure_decoder_frames_active_for_current_decoder`, engaged on all three drivers) make the arrow-Schur border p-independent — p=4096 measured border 32768→64, cov 8.59 GB→32 KB (MSI job 12943297). The remaining wide-p cost is iteration *count*, not width (see #2080).

## Landed: the Tier-1 K>small seed entry (the named remaining Tier-1 gap)

The tiered orchestration (`fit_tiered`), the block-sparse Tier-1 lane, and the Tier-2 curved co-fit are all wired. The one remaining Tier-1 gap was the **seeding wall**: the one-shot Tier-1 (`fit_block_sparse_dictionary`) unconditionally ran the data-aware farthest-point `seed_frames` pass — `O(N·P·G·b) = O(N·P·K)`, serial — which at the #2023 target width (`K≈1e4`) *dominates the whole fit* and is unrelated to routing. The streaming lane already had an escape hatch (`BlockSparseStreamState::new_with_decoder` + a cheap coordinate seed, used at `K≈1e4` in `examples/scale_k.rs`); the one-shot lane the tiered spine calls had none, so a `K≈1e4` tiered fit was not tractable end to end.

### What landed (committed on `main`, checkpoint `37103c094`)

**`sparse_dict::block`:**
- `BlockSeedPolicy { FarthestPoint, CoordinatePartition }` — the seed is only the starting frames; the alternation is seed-agnostic and reaches the same fixed point.
- `coordinate_partition_frames(G, b, P)` — a real library seeder (promoted from the `scale_k` example): `G` blocks of `b` distinct signed unit coordinate axes from a fixed splitmix64 stream, `O(K·b)`, no corpus pass. A valid `St(b,P)` block dictionary (within-block rows orthonormal by construction).
- `fit_block_sparse_dictionary_with_seed(x, config, policy)` — the caller-supplied seed hook. `fit_block_sparse_dictionary` is now its thin `FarthestPoint` delegate (**byte-identical** to the old behaviour — pinned by a test).

**`tiered::fit`:**
- `TieredSeedPolicy { Auto, FarthestPoint, CoordinatePartition }` on `TieredFitConfig` (default `Auto`). `Auto` resolves against the farthest-point budget `N·P·G·b` vs `FARTHEST_POINT_SEED_MAX_OPS = 1e9`: below it keeps the coherent data-aware seed, above it (as at `K≈1e4`) switches to the coordinate seed. **Magic-by-default: no caller flag, no env var, no feature gate** — a `K≈1e4` tiered fit now runs end to end with zero call-site change.

### Why the cheap seed is the *right* choice at large K (not a shortcut)
At `K ≫ intrinsic-rank` most atoms are structurally spurious; the farthest-point seed's value (block-coherence so unrelated subspaces don't share a block) matters near the intrinsic rank, not at `K≈1e4`. There, dead-block AuxK revival reseeds frames from **worst-residual rows** during the epochs — recovery is carried by revival, not the seed. The streaming lane's measured "same fixed point as one-shot" corroborates this. So `Auto` keeps the data-aware seed exactly where it pays and drops it exactly where it only costs.

### Tests (call the production path)
- `coordinate_partition_frames_are_orthonormal_and_data_independent` — the seed is a valid St(b,P) dictionary and never reads `x`.
- `farthest_point_seeded_entry_matches_default_byte_for_byte` — the default entry == FarthestPoint seeded entry (decoder, EV, epochs).
- `coordinate_partition_seed_fits_end_to_end` — the cheap seed carries a real block fit to non-trivial EV.
- `auto_seed_switches_at_the_farthest_point_budget` — `Auto` picks FarthestPoint at small K, CoordinatePartition at the #2023 `N=1e5,K=1e4` width, and honours explicit overrides.
- `coordinate_seed_carries_a_full_tiered_fit` — a full Tier-0→Tier-1(cheap seed)→Tier-2 fit: finite composed EV, `pc_reseed_events == 0`, Tier-2 runs.

Also updated `examples/tiered_gpu_scale`'s seeding note: the serial seed is no longer the scaling wall, so `--rows` can be raised toward the `N=1e5` target and the GPU route dominates the wall time.

**MSI verification in flight** (job 13026297, chained behind the shared-target queue at `37103c094`); I'll post the green `test result:` lines when it lands.

**Still open on the epic** (unchanged by this): the measured K=2,000 certificate-open-at-K≫rank finding, a clean Tier-2-adds-EV number on a curved-structure corpus at a K where Tier-1 certifies, and Increment 5 (folding `cofit` into `sae_manifold_fit`'s inner driver). This closes the *Tier-1 large-K entry* specifically.

## Follow-up: MSI verification round 1 + a convergence-cost datum worth recording

The first MSI run of the seed-entry tests (`cargo nextest run -E 'test(...)'`, 7 tests) came back **4 passed / 3 failed**, and the split is informative:

- **Passed** — `farthest_point_seeded_entry_matches_default_byte_for_byte` (the delegate is byte-identical to the old entry, so the seed refactor is exonerated), `coordinate_partition_frames_are_orthonormal_and_data_independent`, `coordinate_partition_seed_fits_end_to_end` (the block lane **converges** at `aux_k=3` / `max_epochs=120`), and `auto_seed_switches_at_the_farthest_point_budget`.
- **Failed** — the three end-to-end tests that actually run `fit_tiered`, all with the *same* shape: Tier-1 returned `Err(NonConvergence)` because the block **frame-projector fixed point did not reach the 1e-6 tolerance within the fixtures' epoch budgets**. Measured frame residuals at the budget cutoff: **0.036** (`tiered_driver_runs`, 8 epochs), **0.43** (`tiered_beats_linear` linear arm, 20 epochs), **0.44** (`coordinate_seed_carries`, 20 epochs) — with the EVs already high (0.99 / 0.86 / 0.86).

The fix was to make those fixtures well-posed (`aux_k=3` + `max_epochs=200`, the budget the passing block test certifies at); the EV / promotion / `pc_reseed_events` assertions are unchanged. But **the reason a bigger budget was suddenly needed is worth recording, not just absorbing**: two of the three (`tiered_driver_runs`, `tiered_beats_linear`) are pre-existing fixtures that certified under their old tight budgets, and the concurrent **pairwise-determinism reduction rework** (the deterministic `par_pairwise_sum` / block-fold doctrine) changed the exact fixed-point trajectory enough to leave those residuals (0.036 / 0.43) short of the tolerance at the old epoch counts. The frame fixed point is unchanged in *value* (EV is identical to ~2 digits); what shifted is the **per-epoch approach rate** — the deterministic reduction ordering converges the frame projector a little slower per epoch than the old work-stealing order did. That is a real (small) cost of the determinism guarantee, now on the record with the numbers rather than silently paid in larger default budgets.

Re-verification of the fix is in flight (job 13030916, pinned at the fix commit on the healed base). I'll post the green `tests run:` line when it lands.


--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-12T14:04:44Z ---
## Increment 5 design — fold `cofit_block_and_curved` into `sae_manifold_fit`'s inner arrow-Schur driver

Design only (implementation is a next-session lane unless 5a turns out small). The thesis (#2232): there is ONE model — an intercept plus a sparse dictionary of complexity-priced atoms, where a linear atom is the rank-1 / `b₂=0` special case of the curved atom. Today the linear+curved *joint* is descended by **two** engines: `sparse_dict::cofit::cofit_block_and_curved` (block-coordinate A/B alternation) and `manifold::fit_drivers::run_joint_fit_arrow_schur_with_termination_policy` (the unified inner solve). Increment 5 removes the duplicate by expressing cofit's alternation as a schedule over the one inner driver.

### What the unified driver looks like
cofit is already a two-block coordinate descent on the joint objective `J(codes, charts)`:
- **Block A** — `refit_linear_tier`: exact per-row block minimisation of `‖(target − C) − L‖²` over chart-*unowned* active slots. This is precisely the degenerate arrow-Schur inner solve for read-only gates on linear atoms (projection, no ridge pair) — the `d=b` block fast kernel the block lane already documents as the `run_linear_fast_kernel` sibling.
- **Block B** — `compose_block_coordinate_charts` + guarded commit: fit curved charts on `target − L`, accept iff `J` improves within `monotone_slack`. This is the curved atoms' birth/accept, which the joint solve *already* performs via `born_atom` / `apply_structure_move` under the matched description-length charge.

So the fold is: **a linear atom and a curved atom are two atoms of one arrow-Schur assembly, differing only in `d_atom` / `SaeAtomBasisKind`; cofit's A/B is the block-coordinate sweep of that single solve, and its "round 0 = curved-on-linear-residual" is the #2023 seed policy (seed curved atoms from the Tier-1 residual), not a separate pass.** `fit_tiered` collapses to what tiered/mod.rs already claims it is — a seed policy + alternation cadence over `sae_manifold_fit`, with no second engine.

### What dies
- `cofit_block_and_curved`, `CofitConfig`, `CofitReport`, `CofitRound`, and cofit's private `joint_objective` / `assert_monotone` / `refit_linear_tier` / `curved_correction` (they become the arrow-Schur assembly's block pieces, not a parallel copy).
- `tiered::fit::fit_tiered`'s `cofit_block_and_curved` call → a `sae_manifold_fit` invocation with `atom_topology` mixed linear+curved, seeded from the Tier-1 block fit.
- The `record_cofit_moves` translation layer (the migration ledger is written natively by the joint solve).

### Migration risks (ranked)
1. **Dense-state blowup — the load-bearing risk.** The arrow-Schur inner state is `N×K` in TWO places (`SaeAssignment` logits `N×K` and per-atom coords `K×(N×d)`). cofit sidesteps this with block-sparse support state; the joint solve's dense logits path is why `admit_sae_fit` caps the dense engine at `K ≤ P`. Folding cofit into the driver MUST route through the **support-sparse / TopK massive-K assembly** (indices `N×k`, no dense logits), or the fold silently regresses the entire `K ≫ P` scalability the tiered architecture exists for. Non-negotiable gate: peak memory `O(N·k·(1+d))` at `K=1e4`, verified.
2. **#2275 open-certificate must survive.** The block lane emits the typed open certificate (`convergence.certified` + residuals) when the frame fixed point doesn't close at `K ≫ rank`. The arrow-Schur driver has its own termination policy (Newton-decrement / KKT band). The fold must reconcile these into ONE certificate that still distinguishes "certified" from "best-effort, open by this residual" — with no silent tolerance softening (the #2275 contract).
3. **Residual-orthogonality trap.** cofit fits curved on the RAW linear residual; `interference_subspace` is diagnostic-only and `Q⊥`-weighting is a proven design error (the `qperp_weight_is_blind_to_in_plane_curvature` regression). A naive arrow-Schur whitening step could reintroduce it — the fold must keep the raw-residual protocol and price anti-rechasing only via the evidence criterion.
4. **Monotonicity + determinism.** cofit asserts strict per-block descent (`assert_monotone`, slack-bounded); the driver uses Newton-decrement acceptance + EFS. The fold must preserve strict-decrease and the pairwise-determinism doctrine (run-twice bit-identity per backend). Note the already-measured cost: the determinism reductions slowed the frame-projector per-epoch approach rate (residuals 0.036/0.43 short of tol at the old budgets) — the fold must not compound it.
5. **Guarded curved commit ↔ ledger.** cofit's guarded chart commit must map exactly onto `born_atom` / `apply_structure_move` under the matched-DL currency so the migration ledger accounts births/refusals identically (the ledger is the #2023 currency, not an afterthought).

### Verification gate
- **Behaviour parity:** `tiered_beats_linear_on_six_circle_mixture`, `tiered_returns_best_effort_open_certificate_at_k_gg_rank_2275`, `tiered_driver_runs_and_never_pc_reseeds`, and the block co-fit tests pass through the folded path with composed EV **match-or-beat** the cofit path (never weaker).
- **K=2000 measurement** (this issue's acceptance harness, `examples/tiered_k2000_measure`): certificate contents, held-out Tier-1 EV, and Tier-2-adds-EV do not regress.
- **Scale gate:** `O(N·k·(1+d))` peak memory at `K=1e4` (no dense `N×K`), measured on the A100 box.
- **Determinism gate:** run-twice bit-identity per backend on the folded solve.
- **Unify-deletes-legacy grep gate:** zero references to `cofit_block_and_curved` / `CofitReport` after the fold.

### Suggested staging
- **5a (behaviour-preserving):** route cofit's A/B blocks through the arrow-Schur block sweep *behind the existing cofit signature* — same inputs/outputs, same tests green, so the risky engine swap is isolated and measurable.
- **5b (delete):** once 5a is parity-green and the scale/determinism gates hold, repoint `fit_tiered` at `sae_manifold_fit` directly and delete the cofit surface. 5b is the small commit; 5a is the real work and should be its own session.


--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-12T16:09:27Z ---
## Increment 5a — Stage 2 engine seam spec (for the engine lane / e1; gated on the collapse fix)

Stage 1 (landed `7e3996f23`, `sparse_dict::cofit_arrow::cofit_linear_via_arrow`) routes the co-fit's linear tier through `SaeManifoldTerm::run_joint_fit_arrow_schur_for_quasi_laplace` using a **dense** `SaeAssignment` (`N×K` logits). That is correct for the moderate-K parity fixtures (dense in-core is acceptable there), but it violates risk #1 (no dense `N×K` state) for **production** routing at `K ≈ 1e4`. Stage 2 needs an engine seam I cannot build without touching the driver — speccing it here.

### What exists
- `SaeAssignmentState::from_topk_support(...)` (`assignment_state.rs:143`) already holds the support-sparse state: support indices `N×k` + per-atom coords, `O(N·k)`, no dense `N×K` logits. It is what `admit_topk_manifold`'s CurvedStreaming lane consumes.
- The joint solver `run_joint_fit_arrow_schur*` (`fit_drivers.rs:5301/5336/5396`) consumes a **dense** `SaeAssignment` — not `SaeAssignmentState`. So the in-core joint solve is only reachable with the dense `N×K` logit matrix.
- The fully-streaming lane (`SaeManifoldTerm::fit_topk_curved_streaming` + `seed_cold_start_disjoint_charts_streaming`) exists, but it is the OUT-OF-CORE seed/fit path; it is not the in-core joint arrow-Schur solve the co-fit fold wants for a resident-seed `K>P` fit.

### The seam requested
An **in-core, support-sparse** entry with the SAME contract as `run_joint_fit_arrow_schur_for_quasi_laplace`, consuming a support-sparse assignment instead of a dense one:

```
impl SaeManifoldTerm {
    // Same 7 numeric/target args + certificate return as the dense entry, but the
    // term is constructed from a SaeAssignmentState (from_topk_support) and the
    // arrow-Schur assembly is built over the k active atoms per row WITHOUT ever
    // materializing a dense N×K logit matrix.
    pub(crate) fn run_joint_fit_arrow_schur_support_sparse_for_quasi_laplace(
        &mut self,
        target: ArrayView2<'_, f64>,
        rho: &mut SaeManifoldRho,
        analytic_penalties: Option<&AnalyticPenaltyRegistry>,
        max_iter: usize, step_size: f64, ridge_ext_coord: f64, ridge_beta: f64,
    ) -> Result<EvidenceJointFitOutcome, String>;
}
```

Requirements:
1. **No dense `N×K`.** Peak `O(N·k·(1+d))` for the assignment/coords + `O(K·M·r)` framed decoders. The reduced-Schur inner solve is already per-row over the ACTIVE set; under TopK the logits are read-only (`assignment_coord_dim()==0`, no logit Newton params), so the support IS the state — the assembly just needs to iterate the `k` active atoms per row from the support indices instead of scanning `K` dense logits.
2. **Same certificate.** Returns `EvidenceJointFitOutcome { loss, fixed_point }` so the #2275 open-certificate reconciliation is identical to Stage 1 (`certified == fixed_point`).
3. **Parity with the dense path** at moderate K (both entries must agree to solver tolerance on the same routing) — that equivalence test is the seam's acceptance gate, and the dense Stage-1 path is the oracle for it.

### How Stage 1 consumes it
`cofit_arrow` swaps `SaeAssignment::from_blocks_with_mode(dense_logits, …, top_k_support)` for `SaeAssignmentState::from_topk_support(support_indices, coords, k)` and calls the new entry — one construction line + one call site change, no re-derivation. Then 5b (repoint `fit_tiered` at the unified solver, delete `cofit_block_and_curved`) becomes memory-safe at `K=1e4`, closing the fold.

This is the ONE engine change the fold needs; everything else (the linear-atom adapter, the certificate mapping, the parity harness, the K=2000 measurement) is on the caller side and already landed or staged. Tagging for the engine lane per the coordination rule (I call the solver, I don't modify it).


--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-13T00:29:54Z ---
Correctness prerequisite landed in `6de3d0e9a` + `2b68735dd`: Tier-2 no longer mints an open/uncertified cofit. The legacy cofit now requires a deterministic full A/B transition to recur bit-for-bit and errors on exhaustion; curved-state changes commit only on strict objective improvement. The Arrow entry likewise requires the underlying evidence joint fit's `fixed_point`, removes the public `certified=false` report state, and rejects `max_iter=0` because that outcome is a checkpoint freeze rather than a fresh fit.

This closes the immediate SPEC violation (returning a non-fixed-point fit), but not this issue. --- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-13T04:55:31Z ---
Current-main architecture audit confirms #2023 remains open and localizes the next breaking cutover.

The public TopK route is still dense despite its admission label:

- `SaeManifoldTerm` owns dense `SaeAssignment`; `SaeAssignmentState` has no production consumer.
- Arrow assembly builds K-wide gates, N×K prior gradient/diagonal arrays, and K-wide row scratch before its compact row solve.
- atom caches retain N×M basis values and N×M×d jets.
- `admit_topk_manifold` can select `CurvedStreaming`, but `admit_sae_fit_shape` discards that lane and `build_sae_fit_seed` still requires dense N×K logits/bases/coordinates.
- `fit_topk_curved_streaming` has no production caller.

The duplicate tiered/cofit engine is also not an acceptable destination: it optimizes SSE plus coefficient ridge instead of a final-function penalty chosen by REML/LAML. Its translated ledger loses atom identities, records count decreases as refusals, cannot represent the full residual↔linear↔curved lifecycle, and passes a nats-valued charge to a bits constructor (ln(2) unit error).

Therefore the smallest principled increment is not another adapter: make a heterogeneous `SaeAssignmentState` canonical, make public admission operational, assemble TopK Arrow rows directly from active supports with no N×K state, and cut the public TopK entry over with no dense fallback. After fixed-point/parity/O(Nk) gates pass, fold Tier1 scheduling into that single REML driver and delete `cofit.rs`, `cofit_arrow.rs`, their translation tests, and production PCA reseeding.

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-03T03:19:49Z ---
**Triangulation probe (MSI 12437107) — the "wide-p hang" is the K≥2 co-collapse surfacing at the OUTER solver. Full mechanism below.** All arms on the verified fresh 0.1.247 wheel, planted product-of-circles, n=480.

**p=16, K=1 → CONVERGES in 61.6s** (n_atoms=1). So the canned "hangs even at K=1" note was FALSE — single-atom is fine. That desync is the fingerprint of the analytic logdet/adjoint derivative bugs being tracked in #2087 (red-tree localized 5 of them) — the fitter's own optimality self-audit is flagging the same wrong gradient.

**p=16, K=3 → FATAL in ~7 min** with `RemlConvergenceError` (not a plain hang). The mechanism, from the live log:
- The structural coherence detector fires on **every** atom pair — (0,1),(0,2),(1,2) all decode a **shared output subspace, μ̂=1.0000** (derived random-subspace null far below) — i.e. textbook co-collapse.
- Critically this happens at **healthy EV=0.9468** — the collapse is EV-invisible, exactly as #2082 established.
- The collapsed configuration is a degenerate outer geometry, so BFGS can't find a feasible step: `[OUTER] probe-refusal non-termination guard fired after 25 consecutive infeasible cost probes with no accepted gradient step (nan_seed=true)` → escalates to Fatal. Startup validation then reports all seeds `rejected_by_objective`.

**So #2080 ("wide-p REML hang") and the K≥2 co-collapse are the same problem seen at the outer-REML level.** The wide-p timeout is the co-collapsed, degenerate optimization thrashing infeasible probes until the wall cap; at p=16 it aborts fast, at p=96 it runs out the 40-min clock. The cold-start chart-deflation fix (`7a93b1d06`) is NOT preventing it in this joint `sae_manifold_fit(K=3, n_iter=40, random_state=0)` path — the seeds fail outer startup validation before/despite the deflation seeding, `nan_seed=true`. p96_K1 arm still running (isolates pure width from K).

Two concrete workstreams fall out: (1) the analytic derivative bugs (#2087) are not cosmetic — they desync the gradient the outer solver trusts, visible even in the converging K=1 case; (2) the cold-start disjoint-chart seeding needs to actually engage (or the outer startup-validation needs to accept it) in the joint multi-atom path, not just the tests_cocollapse_2027 entry path.

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-03T03:42:26Z ---
**Triangulation complete — TWO independent failure modes, not one. Full table (fresh 0.1.247 wheel, planted circles, n=480):**

| | K=1 | K=3 |
|---|---|---|
| **p=16** | CONVERGES 61.6s | FATAL ~7min (co-collapse: all pairs μ̂=1.0, 25 infeasible outer probes) |
| **p=96** | TIMEOUT (600s cap) | TIMEOUT (900s cap) |

The load-bearing new datum is **p96_K1 timing out**. A single atom cannot co-collapse with itself, so this is NOT the co-collapse surface — it's a pure **width-scaling** cost in the outer REML / inner solve. 62s at p=16 → does not return in 600s at p=96 (6× width). The REML criterion's dense p×p logdet/Hessian work scales ~O(p³), so this is cubic-in-ambient-width. At real-data width (d=2048) a direct curved fit is intractable by orders of magnitude, independent of any co-collapse.

**So #2080 decomposes into two separable problems:**
1. **Co-collapse** (multi-atom) — degenerate shared-subspace geometry kills the outer solver even at narrow p. Owned by the disjoint-seeding-engagement work.
2. **Cubic width cost** (per-atom) — even K=1 is intractable at wide ambient p.

**Architectural consequence for scaling (K=32k):** curved atoms must NEVER be fit in the full ambient space. They must operate on **small per-block subspaces (d≈2–8)** — which is exactly the tiered design (block-sparse Tier-1 reduces dimensionality; curved Tier-2 refines within each small block). The tiered architecture isn't just elegant, it's *required* by the cubic width cost — a single curved atom in 2048-dim ambient is already too slow, let alone 32k of them. Both failure modes are dissolved by keeping curved fits low-ambient-dimensional and growing atoms stagewise rather than jointly.

Even the converging p16_K1 case emits `CERTIFICATE warning: GRADIENT-OBJECTIVE DESYNC` (the #2087 analytic-derivative fingerprint), which likely worsens the width-scaling thrash — wrong gradients make the outer solver take tiny/infeasible steps that compound as p grows.

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-03T04:07:59Z ---
**Correction to the "cold-start disjoint seeding does NOT engage in the joint path" claim — it DOES engage; the real mechanism is entanglement-specific.**

I built a faithful K=3-circle repro through the REAL `OuterProblem` (`seed_budget=1, max_seeds=1`, exactly as `sae_manifold_fit_minimal` drives it — confirmed the FFI entry passes a COLD zero-init decoder + PCA seed coords, ffi line ~6782), instrumented the entry gate in `run_joint_fit_arrow_schur` (`max_decoder_norm==0 ⇒ cold-seed fires`), and measured structural distinctness (per-atom decoder norms + `structural_coherence_collapse_detected`), not EV. Findings at HEAD `2c7fec4ef`:

1. **The cold-start `seed_cold_start_disjoint_charts` DOES fire in the real outer path.** On the FIRST ρ probe `max_decoder_norm==0`, so entry seeding runs and places disjoint decoders (norms e.g. `[18, 25, 11]`). It is NOT rejected at startup validation before deflation. The earlier "seeds rejected before disjoint deflation / nan_seed before it engages" reading was wrong.

2. **It fires exactly ONCE per fit.** Every subsequent ρ probe sees the warm decoder (`fired=false`), so there is no re-seeding across the ρ-search — no recovery if an atom later drifts toward collapse.

3. **On DISJOINT-subspace planted circles (what `tests_cocollapse_disjoint_2027` uses), atoms separate and converge at every scale I could run** — direct `run_joint_fit_arrow_schur` gives `coherence=None` with all atoms carrying material norm up to `(n=480, p=16)` and `(n=240, p=96)`; the full outer path converges `Ok` at n=45 (EV=0.478, separated). The co-collapse is **not reproduced by disjoint circles at all**.

4. **The differentiator is DATA STRUCTURE, not the seeding wiring.** This issue's data is a *product-of-circles* — an ENTANGLED / overlapping-frame manifold. With overlapping frames, the seed's sequential PCA-**residual** deflation (atom 0 = dominant factor of the target, atom 1 = dominant of the residual, …) cannot cleanly peel one circle at a time, so later atoms get degenerate seeds. Measured: with entangled/overlapping-frame data the weakest-to-strongest decoder-norm ratio collapses from **~0.42 (disjoint)** to **~0.13 (entangled p=16)** / **~0.16 (entangled p=48)**, EV 0.49→0.35 — the onset of co-collapse (the 3rd atom is squeezed out).

**Root diagnosis.** The disjoint-chart seed's separation ASSUMES the planted factors are peelable in disjoint subspaces — true for the test fixture, FALSE for an entangled product manifold — AND it fires once at entry with no mid-ρ-search re-engagement (the `structural_coherence_collapse_detected` detector that would catch drift is telemetry-only per #2082 because it false-positives on healthy correlated atoms).

**Honest limitation.** I could NOT reproduce the full `μ̂=1.0` / EV=0.9468 collapse at `(n=480, p=96)` on the laptop — a ~30s wall-clock reaper SIGKILLs fits that large. The entangled-data trend points straight at it; full-scale confirmation (and a rigorous T³-product generator; mine is a coupled multi-phase curve on overlapping frames) needs MSI, which the red-tree lane is set up to run.

**Implication.** Joint K≥2 curved genuinely WORKS for disjoint/peelable factors and degrades on entangled structure. This favors the tiered + STAGEWISE route (peel one factor → deflate → repeat, and/or per-block K=1) over joint fitting for entangled manifolds. The open question the per-block experiment answers: does confining each atom to its own small block subspace RESCUE the entangled case, or does the entanglement contaminate the projected block too?

Self-contained Rust repro (disjoint + entangled generators, direct-vs-outer paths, entry-gate instrumentation) available for the MSI full-scale run.
---

**Correction (framing, thanks to the red-tree lane).** Scratch "favors the STAGEWISE route for entangled" above — that's wrong. Red-tree's data shows **stagewise peel-deflate births ALSO co-collapse on the entangled product-of-circles** (2/6 factors, μ̂→1.0). That's expected in hindsight: stagewise is the SAME peel-and-deflate mechanism as the joint-entry disjoint seeding, just sequenced across births — so it inherits the same failure, deflating one factor from an entangled manifold leaves a residual that still entangles the rest. So the accurate statement is: **peel-and-deflate (joint-entry seeding OR stagewise) works for DISJOINT factors and degrades on ENTANGLED**, independent of sequencing. The open rescue for entangled is therefore NOT stagewise — it's **structural per-block CONFINEMENT** (project onto a small block subspace, fit K=1 there) or a **non-disjoint (whitened joint-diagonalization / ICA-like) seed** that doesn't assume peelability. The per-block-K=1-on-entangled experiment (red-tree, MSI) decides which.


--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-03T04:54:47Z ---
**Cross-ref from #2089** — a concrete, actionable measurement of the intra-fit time sink, and where the fast-refuse belongs.

While closing the #2089 process-kill (memory-safety part fixed by `7a93b1d06`; a strictly-gated defense-in-depth bail landed in `0f1efbeff`), I profiled *where* a totally-co-collapsed K≥2 fit spends its wall time. It is **not** the outer ρ-search retrying many probes — for the tiny repro (n=120, p=32, K=6, `ibp_map`/circle) the death is **intra-probe**: each co-collapse reseed cycle inside a single `run_joint_fit_arrow_schur` call spends **~10–13 s** in the inner `(t, β)` solve thrashing on the near-degenerate / non-PD co-collapsed system — the "`[#1026] restoring inner-fit reconstruction incumbent after EV degraded …`" churn — so the 3-reseed multi-start budget isn't exhausted for ~35 s.

That contradicts the inner solve's own contract: the `probe_outer_criterion_value` / `is_recoverable_value_probe_refusal` comments state an infeasible/degenerate ρ should "return the typed refusal after a single diagnostic pass" (defect-2 in the #2080 notes). Empirically, on a *provably* degenerate co-collapsed inner system it does **not** single-pass-refuse — it grinds the damped LM / proximal-ridge Newton to the iteration cap while the reduced Schur stays indefinite (the `schur_pd_floor` engages but the loop still crawls).

Actionable, SPEC-18-clean fix for this lane (convergence-gated, not a timer): detect the *provably* non-PD / rank-deficient inner `(t, β)` system up front (the reduced-Schur indefiniteness is already computed) and return the typed infeasible-ρ refusal in **one** diagnostic pass, instead of letting the LM loop inflate ρ_β over thousands of tiny steps. The whitened-metric + anchor-birth prevention work (#2023) should also shrink how often this path is hit. Once the per-cycle cost drops from ~10 s to a single pass, the #2089 defense-in-depth bail reaches reseed-exhaustion quickly and raises its diagnostic, and this wide-p outer hang shortens correspondingly.

Not fixing it here (out of the #2089 bail-out scope) — flagging with the measurement so the co-collapse-solver lane can pick it up.

A *globally-infeasible seed neighbourhood* where the seed is nonetheless a valid dictionary (ev>0.15, only its REML neighbourhood is undefined) should **ship the incumbent** (`converged=false`) rather than reject-and-abort.

**Why not landed:** this is the *generic* gam-solve outer engine shared by every REML path; the probe-refusal and cost-stall guards interact subtly and existing tests assert the current reject/halt semantics (`run_plan_tests.rs:1552,1751`, `tests_startup_validation_1782.rs`). ## Root cause resolved into two architectural mechanisms — routing the close to #2087 + #2023

Diagnosis against current `main`. **The original non-termination ("hang") is gone.** Every loop this issue could hang on is now bounded:

- **Seed budget** capped — `rho_optimizer/run_plan.rs` `effective_seed_budget`; `sae_manifold_fit` drives `seed_budget=1`/`max_seeds=1`. No combinatorial seed blowup at wide p.

The stated acceptance `wide_p_outer_reml_terminates_within_probe_budget_2080` (K=2, p≈96) is **GREEN** (ev≈0.909, `criterion_calls=6`, `mutating_value_probes=0`).

**What remains is bounded-but-slow / fast-abort, decomposing into two roots — both architectural, neither closable in this lane:**

**1. Cubic width cost (per-atom, hits even K=1).** p16/K1 converges in 62s → p96/K1 does not return in 600s. This is *not* a memory mis-route (`streaming_plan.rs` admits the direct path because p=96 fits RAM); it is dense O(p³)-ish logdet/Hessian arithmetic per REML eval × many inner Newton iterations. It is **amplified by the #2087 gradient–objective desync**: the converging K1 case *still* emits `CERTIFICATE warning: GRADIENT-OBJECTIVE DESYNC` (the analytic logdet/adjoint derivative-bug fingerprint). A wrong outer gradient → BFGS takes tiny/infeasible steps → many more full REML solves → the width cost compounds. **Fix owned by #2087** (correct gradient ⇒ far fewer evals) + structurally by **#2023** (per-block d≈2–8 confinement so a curved atom is never fit in full ambient — mandatory at d=2048/K=32k regardless).

**2. Co-collapse (K≥2).** The product-of-circles target is an **entangled** manifold. The disjoint-chart seed's sequential PCA-residual deflation assumes *peelable* factors (true for the `tests_cocollapse_disjoint_2027` fixture, **false** here), so later atoms get degenerate seeds → all pairs decode a shared subspace (μ̂=1.0) → degenerate outer geometry → 25 infeasible probes → `Fatal`. EV-invisible (0.9468). Stagewise inherits the same peel-and-deflate failure. **Fix owned by #2023**: a non-disjoint (whitened joint-diagonalization / ICA-like) seed that does not assume peelability, or per-block confinement.

**Disposition.**
- Keep this issue **OPEN**; it closes when **#2087** (gradient/logdet-adjoint) + **#2023** (non-disjoint seed / per-block tiering) land.
- `wide_p_outer_reml_terminates_k3_heavy_2080` stays **RED** — it is a correct failing regression pinning the open co-collapse defect, **not** an XFAIL to suppress.
- The #2089 up-front provably-non-PD single-pass refuse is a real perf win but only shortens the abort; it does not make K≥2 converge, so it is not the root and is deferred.

Retitling to reflect the current state (bounded-but-slow at wide p / entangled co-collapse), not "hang."

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-09T01:15:47Z ---
## Wide-p per-eval cost: where it actually is, and a desync-safe sub-quadratic construction

Follow-up to the four-lever train (50aae88fb) — the hang is fixed, so what remains is the per-eval cost that makes #2230's phases run for hours (~5 min/criterion-eval at p=7168). This comment pins the cost to the right term and derives the construction that removes it without re-opening the objective↔gradient desync class.

### 1. The wall is the dense Schur *assembly*, not the Cholesky

At the accepted stationary iterate the evidence log-det path does (newton_step.rs:131-133):

- `build_dense_schur_direct`: `S = H_ββ − Σ_i H_βt^(i) (H_tt^(i))⁻¹ H_tβ^(i)`, cost **O(n·q·k²)** with `k = Σ_k M_k·p` (border dim), `q` = per-row coordinate dim;
- `factor_dense_reduced_schur`: **O(k³/3)**.

At #2230 phase-1 shapes (p=7168, K=1 circle ⇒ M=3, k≈21.5·10³, n=6·10⁴, q≈2-3):

- assembly ≈ n·q·k² ≈ **10¹³·⁵–10¹⁴ flops**,
- Cholesky ≈ k³/3 ≈ **3·10¹² flops**.

So the assembly term is ~20-30× the factorization. Any fix that still *forms* S dense (better factorization, low-rank *corrections* to a formed S, GPU Cholesky) leaves the dominant term standing. The escape must be **matrix-free in S**.

A matrix-free matvec is cheap by comparison:

`S·v = H_ββ·v − Σ_i H_βt^(i) (H_tt^(i))⁻¹ (H_tβ^(i) v)` costs O(Σ_i q_i·k) ≈ n·q·k ≈ **3·10⁹ flops** — four orders of magnitude below one assembly. The per-row `H_tt` factors are already computed for the gradient path, so the matvec has no new factorization cost.

(For the record, the exact determinant-lemma route — write the row corrections as a rank-`Σq_i` update and use `log|S| = log|H_ββ| + log|I − U^T H_ββ^{-1} U|` — is only sub-dense when `n·q ≪ k`. That holds for the tiny-N probe lanes (N≈180 repros) and could be wired there, but at n=6·10⁴, `n·q ≈ 1.2-1.8·10⁵ > k`, so it cannot serve real fits. Not the road.)

### 2. Why plain SLQ was rightly kept off the CPU criterion path

`slq_logdet.rs` exists (32 Rademacher probes, device-gated ≥4096). The reason it must not be dropped naively into `reml_criterion`: the outer solve consumes **both** the value ½log|S| and its analytic ρ-gradient. If the value is a stochastic estimate and the gradient is the exact trace channel (which is exact today — the #2087 audit confirmed the trace channel), the line search descends on a function whose gradient belongs to a *different* function. That is precisely the obj↔grad desync genus this repo has been burned by repeatedly. Fresh probes per eval are even worse: the criterion becomes noise on the scale of the stall tolerances.

### 3. The desync-safe construction: a *fixed* rational surrogate, differentiated exactly

Fix, per outer solve (not per eval):

- probe block `V = [v_1 … v_m]`, Rademacher, **common random numbers across every ρ evaluation**;
- a rational approximation of log on a spectral bracket `[a, b] ⊇ spec(S(ρ))`:
  `log x ≈ r(x) = c₀ + Σ_{ℓ=1}^{L} w_ℓ · x/(x + t_ℓ)` (any of the standard forms works; the Hale–Higham–Trefethen conformal-map quadrature gives geometric convergence, L = O(log κ · log 1/ε), so L ≈ 25-40 covers κ up to 10¹² at ε = 10⁻⁶).

Define the **surrogate criterion term**

&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;`L̃(ρ) = (k/m)·Σ_j v̂_jᵀ r(S(ρ)) v̂_j`,&nbsp;&nbsp; v̂ normalized probes,

computed with shifted-CG: one Krylov space per probe serves **all L shifts** `(S + t_ℓ I)⁻¹ v_j` simultaneously.

The point of the construction: `L̃` is a *deterministic, smooth* function of ρ (probes and quadrature fixed), and its **exact** ρ-gradient is

&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;`∂L̃/∂ρ = (k/m)·Σ_j Σ_ℓ w_ℓ t_ℓ · y_{jℓ}ᵀ (∂S/∂ρ) y_{jℓ}`,&nbsp;&nbsp;`y_{jℓ} = (S + t_ℓ I)⁻¹ v̂_j`

— computable from the **same** shifted solves as the value, plus matrix-free `(∂S/∂ρ)·y` matvecs (differentiate the per-row contributions; same row loop as the existing trace channel). Value and gradient are now the same function by construction: **the desync class is closed off structurally, not by tolerance tuning.** The outer BFGS optimizes L̃ exactly; Wolfe conditions are meaningful; the stall certificates apply verbatim.

Bias control is a *terminal* concern, not a per-eval one: E_V[L̃] = tr r(S) and the probe fluctuation is a fixed smooth O(m^{-1/2}·‖·‖) perturbation of the criterion surface, so ρ̂ is perturbed O(m^{-1/2}) — then certify once at ρ̂ with either (a) an independent probe block (bracket test), or (b) a single dense assembly+factorization at the terminal point only (one 5-minute eval per *fit* is fine; per *eval* is what kills).

### 4. Two refinements that come for free

- **Hutch++/deflation**: run a few subspace iterations (matvecs only) to peel the top-r eigenspace of S, take its log-det exactly, SLQ the deflated remainder. This (i) collapses the variance (the heavy tail of the spectrum is what Hutchinson variance lives on), (ii) shrinks κ and hence L, and (iii) *independently* neutralizes the 10⁵⁷-spread pathology that motivated e1aefbd3d — the same subspace that breaks reconstruct-then-refactor is the one you want deflated anyway.
- **Unit-deflation consistency**: the evidence convention (spectral_unit_deflated_schur) sends null/non-positive directions to `log 1 = 0`. In the matrix-free lane the identical convention is: bottom-subspace vectors discovered by the same subspace iteration are projected out of the probes and contribute 0 — same quotient pseudo-determinant, no ρ-dependent bias.

### 5. Cost model at #2230 phase-1 shapes

| term | dense path (today) | fixed-rational surrogate |
|---|---|---|
| per criterion eval | n·q·k² ≈ 10¹⁴ + k³/3 ≈ 3·10¹² | m probes × ~CG iters × (n·q·k) ≈ 32 × 60 × 3·10⁹ ≈ **6·10¹²** |
| per ρ-gradient | trace channel (existing) | reuses the same y_{jℓ}: + m·L (∂S/∂ρ)-matvecs |
| terminal certificate | — | one dense eval at ρ̂ |

≈ 15-20× per-eval reduction at these shapes before deflation/warm-starts (CRN probes make y_{jℓ}(ρ) smooth in ρ ⇒ warm-started CG converges in a fraction of the cold iters after the first eval — in practice the multiplier is much larger). It also removes the k×k dense allocation, which is what stops β_dim ≈ 10⁵ (the #1017 77 GB wall) from ever being reachable on the dense path.

### 6. Wiring sketch

1. `slq_logdet.rs`: add the fixed-probe/fixed-quadrature surrogate variant (probe block + bracket + quadrature stored per outer solve, e.g. on the ρ-search state next to ProbeConvergedHandoff).
2. Shifted-CG on the matrix-free `S`-matvec (per-row loop; H_tt factors reused from the gradient path). Multi-shift CG shares the Krylov basis across all t_ℓ.
3. `reml_criterion`: route k ≥ threshold (existing 4096 constant) through the surrogate on CPU as well as device; keep dense below.
4. Gradient: extend the existing per-row trace-channel loop to accept the y_{jℓ} bundle (it already knows ∂S/∂ρ row-locally).
5. Terminal: one dense assembly+factor at accepted ρ̂ as the certificate + the returned cache (so downstream consumers of the factor cache are untouched).

Cross-refs: #2230 (the hours-long phases are this per-eval cost), #1017 Phase-3 (the matrix-free matvec here is the same primitive the device-resident lane needs — build it once, host first, device second), #2087 (trace channel already exact; this construction keeps it consumed against a value of the same functional).

## Wide-κ log-det surrogate has a real ~5% deterministic bias (not Hutchinson variance)

Settled the variance-vs-bias question for the deflated rational log-det surrogate in the wide-κ regime with a **96-seed frozen-Q discriminator** (`deflation_wide_kappa_variance_vs_bias_multiseed`, gam-solve `arrow_schur/rational_logdet.rs`). Each of 96 plans uses a different probe seed but the **same** frozen deflation basis Q (rank 16) and **exact** solves, so only Hutchinson probe noise varies across seeds; a bias that survives the seed-average is structural.

```
wide-κ (96 seeds, fixed Q, EXACT solves):
  exact    = 57.388446
  mean     = 60.258544
  bias     = +2.870098   (5.001e-2 rel, 5.57σ of the mean)
  seed sd  = 5.0478   se_mean = 0.5152   ⟨internal std_err⟩ = 8.5816
VERDICT: genuine DETERMINISTIC bias survives probe-averaging.
```

**Why an earlier single-draw check read this as "variance-dominated":** the per-draw internal std_err is **8.58** (~15% of |logdet|), so on one 32-probe draw the +2.87 offset is only ~0.3σ — invisible under the noise. Averaging 96 seeds shrinks the noise floor to se_mean=0.515, and the offset emerges at **5.57σ**. So the RED gate `deflation_cuts_..._wide_kappa` was correct all along; this is not a mis-calibrated bar.

**Consequence for the surrogate:** the fix is genuine derivation work on the log-det **value** surrogate — either the exp-sinh DE quadrature (node count / sinh-tail truncation at wide κ) or the term1/term2 split normalizer `c` in `tr(Qᵀ log(S/c) Q)` — **not** variance reduction (more probes / higher deflation rank won't remove a deterministic offset). The θ-adjoint gradient folds are orthogonal and unaffected (exact at full-basis, unbiased for any probe count). Fix in progress.

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-09T15:54:55Z ---
## Retraction: the "+2.87 deterministic bias / 5.57σ" above was a probe-RNG aliasing artifact — it IS Hutchinson variance

The "Wide-κ log-det surrogate has a real ~5% deterministic bias" comment above (the 96-seed frozen-Q `deflation_wide_kappa_variance_vs_bias_multiseed` result) is **wrong, and I'm retracting it.** The offset was not a quadrature or split defect — it was an artifact of the probe RNG, and the original variance hypothesis is restored.

**Proof chain** (Python-replicated against the exact Rust spectrum + DE nodes, then confirmed in-tree):

1. **Pure DE quadrature is exact at κ=2.6e7**: Σ[Q(λ) − log(λ/c)] = −3e-10 over the full spectrum. No node-count / sinh-tail-truncation error.
2. **The term1/term2 split is exact**: for orthonormal Q, tr(QQᵀMP)=0; a full-rank deflation (rank = dim, projector P=0, i.e. *zero* Hutchinson) reproduces the exact log-det to 5e-12. So neither the split normalizer `c` nor the quadrature carries bias.
3. **The offset was RNG aliasing.** The old per-probe init set state = (seed+p)·γ, which makes the splitmix streams seeded at x₀ and x₀+γ the *same* stream shifted by one. Across 96 unit-spaced seeds the 3072 probe slots drew only **127 distinct probes** — each seed's estimate was a ~32-wide sliding-window mean of a shared pool, so the seeds were ~4-effective-independent, not 96. The sample-sd/√96 therefore **underestimated the true mean-standard-error by ~4.9×**, and 5.57σ ÷ 4.9 ≈ **1.1σ** — squarely within noise. There is no surviving deterministic offset.

**Verdict:** wide-κ error here is genuine **Hutchinson variance** (~16% of |logdet| on a single 32-probe draw), *not* a value-surrogate derivation bug. So the production lever is **variance reduction, not re-derivation**:

- Probe RNG fixed to a sequential `splitmix64_hash(seed)` master stream for both probes and the deflation start — restores cross-seed independence (>0.95·3072 distinct) while keeping per-seed CRN determinism.
- **Two-sided deflation** (`with_two_sided_deflation`): offdiag(log(S/c)) sits symmetrically on both spectral tails, so one-sided top deflation stalls at ~½lnκ. Peeling the bottom via inverse subspace iteration (matrix-free CG) as well drops calibrated std_err **7.23% → 1.49%** at |logdet|=57.4 (2.75× under equal-rank one-sided). Approx bottom-Q never biases (exact split for any orthonormal Q).

New discriminator gate `full_rank_deflation_is_exact_at_wide_kappa_deterministic_bias_localizer` (rank=dim, zero-noise, exact-Cholesky arm, asserts <1e-6) is the clean test the multiseed couldn't be. The θ-adjoint gradient folds are orthogonal and unaffected (exact at full-basis, unbiased for any probe count). Apologies for the earlier mis-call — the frozen-Q multiseed looked airtight but its own probe pool was aliased.

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-09T21:42:40Z ---
## Defect-4 root-fix derivation (from the SPEC-conformance audit)

The `value_consistent_outer_gradient` FD safeguard (outer_objective.rs) is the one remaining production finite-difference (SPEC rule 2). Audit + code reading sharpened the root fix:

**Key structural fact**: `solve_exact_stationarity` runs left-`B`-preconditioned GMRES on `A = B + ΔC`, and `B ⪰ A` by construction (Gershgorin entropy majorizer, `max(V'',0)` ARD majorizers, GN data curvature). Therefore the preconditioned operator `B⁻¹A` has spectrum in `(0, 1]`, and the desync direction (saturated IBP gate logit, data curvature `∝ σ'(ℓ)² ≈ 0`) is precisely the `μ → 0` tail of that spectrum. `θ̂_ρ` picks up a `(vᵀg_ρ)/μ` amplification there, corrupting the `−½Γᵀθ̂_ρ` envelope term into a sign flip.

**Scale-free fix**: deflate the small-`μ` subspace of the *preconditioned* spectrum (a cutoff on `μ = curvature retained as a fraction of its own majorizer` is dimensionless and interpretable, unlike any absolute ridge). Matrix-free: harvest approximate small-`μ` Ritz vectors from the GMRES Krylov space itself (they emerge for free as the stagnating directions), project them out of the solve, and zero their envelope contribution. Justification: along `μ ≈ 0` directions the inner optimizer's iterate position is majorizer-dynamics-dominated, so the true criterion's realized `dθ̂/dρ` there is NOT `1/λ_A`-scaled — the FD gradient the safeguard currently trusts confirms this empirically (moderate slope).

Once the deflated solve makes the analytic gradient value-consistent by construction, the 2-probe + 2·d_ρ FD machinery demotes to a debug-only diagnostic (or deletes), closing the SPEC-2 violation.

Validation fixture already named in the code: planted-circle IBP K=1 (railed at the ρ=1 GeneralizedLinear anchor, EV ≈ 0.87 vs > 0.95).

The rational-logdet split identity was hand-verified exact for any orthonormal Q (P/Q trace decomposition, per-probe ||u||^2 dimension counting, k*ln c bookkeeping), and the DE quadrature step/truncation bounds are correctly derived. The earlier '5.57 sigma deterministic bias' verdict was an artifact of splitmix probe-stream aliasing across unit-spaced seeds — the 96-seed battery drew ~128 distinct probe vectors instead of 3072, so a shared Hutchinson fluctuation was reported as deterministic bias. All fixed on HEAD: one sequential master probe stream, a probe-fingerprint independence guard that fails loudly on re-aliasing, and two-sided (top+bottom tail) deflation for the variance.
