## Status: the wide-κ "5.57σ bias" is closed as PROBE-RNG ALIASING; two-sided deflation is now the production variance lever

Consolidating today's findings on the deflation lane:

**1. The "deterministic bias" was never a bias.** The multiseed discriminator's 96 unit-spaced seeds drew only ~128 distinct probe vectors instead of 3072 — the per-probe RNG init `(seed+p)·γ` made probe `p` of seed `s` bit-identical to probe `p+1` of seed `s−1` (a splitmix stream from `x₀+γ` is the same stream shifted). Averaging correlated draws collapses `se_mean`, so a shared Hutchinson fluctuation reported as "5.57σ deterministic bias". Fixed by sequential consumption from one hashed master stream (`338251381`); the multiseed test now fingerprints every probe's sign pattern and hard-fails if unit-spaced seeds ever re-alias, so this failure mode cannot silently return.

**2. The split algebra is sound.** With exact dense-Cholesky solves and frozen Q, the probe-averaged estimate is unbiased at κ=1e8 (`deflation_wide_kappa_variance_vs_bias_multiseed`); the exact-arm discriminator exonerates CG convergence as well. What remains at wide κ is VARIANCE: the Hutchinson bar is `√(2‖offdiag(P·log(S/c)·P)‖_F²)`, whose mass sits symmetrically on BOTH spectral tails, so top-only deflation removes at most half of it and stalls near ½·lnκ-scale bars.

**3. Production now peels both tails.** `rational_reduced_schur_plan_derived` had the two-sided design in its doc but still called one-sided `with_deflation`; the cutover (`892aaea3d`) splits the peel rank across the tails at equal total rank and gives the inverse-iteration (bottom-tail) basis build its own loose CG budget — documented as bias-free since the split `tr log(S/c) = term1(Q) + term2(P)` is exact for ANY orthonormal Q, so basis-solve error can only relax variance reduction. Evaluation-grade CG on the unshifted full-κ operator would burn √κ-scale iterations per column for nothing.

The `two_sided_deflation_drops_wide_kappa_std_err_below_two_percent` deliverable pins the bar below 2% of |logdet| at equal total rank; the full wide-κ set runs in the MSI verify battery. Remaining on this epic after the battery goes green: nothing on the math side — the surrogate's value, all four gradient channels, the θ-adjoint, and now the variance lever are landed.


--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-10T02:22:35Z ---
## Defect 4: deflation fix LANDED (f777df0f2) — CI is the validation gate

Implemented the root fix from the derivation above, in `solve_exact_stationarity` (construction_exact_hessian.rs):

- **Detector**: the solution's own generalized Rayleigh quotient `μ(x) = xᵀAx/xᵀBx`. Since `B ⪰ A` (majorizer construction) the pencil spectrum is `(0,1]`, and any near-null component in the rhs enters the solve with weight `1/μ`, so `μ(x)` collapses to `≈ μ_min` exactly when amplification occurred. Healthy solves pay one extra `A`/`B` apply and exit.
- **Direction recovery**: inverse-power iteration `v ← A⁻¹(Bv)` (the existing B-preconditioned GMRES is the `A⁻¹` apply), seeded by the corrupted solution itself — which is already dominated by the offending direction.
- **Deflation**: exact in the `(A,B)` eigenbasis with **no re-solve** — the amplified term of `x` along a B-normalized eigendirection is `v(vᵀBx)`, so subtracting the B-projection removes precisely the unidentifiable `1/μ` component and touches nothing resolved. Up to 8 directions per solve (`SAE_IFT_MIN_CURVATURE_FRACTION = 1e-8`, dimensionless fraction-of-own-majorizer).

**Validation**: adversarial test `ift_solve_deflates_saturated_gate_near_null_direction_2080` (construction_tests.rs) — saturates atom-1 gate logits at −40 on the tiny IBP fixture, asserts **non-vacuity first** (the RAW GMRES solve must collapse below the 1e-8 floor, i.e. the fixture genuinely reproduces the defect) and then that the production solve restores `μ ≥ floor` via a B-norm-non-increasing projection. Local runs were SIGKILLed twice by the box watchdog (concurrent build storm), so **CI is the gate**: a red on the non-vacuity assert means the fixture needs strengthening; a red on the deflation asserts means the fix needs iteration; green means the desync class is closed at the source.

**Follow-up once CI is green**: demote/remove the `value_consistent_outer_gradient` FD safeguard in outer_objective.rs (the last production finite-difference, SPEC rule 2) — with the envelope solve value-consistent by construction, the safeguard's stage-1/stage-2 probes should never trip; re-measure the planted-circle IBP K=1 EV (expect > 0.95 vs the railed 0.87).

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-10T15:01:03Z ---
SPEC-conformance audit finding at `37eb3116c52f03ce336e08a635cf9c69523fdaa5`: the newly landed analytic IFT deflation still has a correctness hole before it can replace the production FD safeguard safely.

In `solve_exact_stationarity`, inverse-power refinement currently does:

- seed `v = x`;
- if `A⁻¹(Bv)` GMRES fails, silently `break` and keep that unrefined seed;
- B-normalize it and apply `x ← x − v(vᵀBx)`.

If refinement fails on its first solve, `v` is exactly the normalized `x`, so the projection deletes the **entire IFT response** (up to roundoff) and returns it as an analytic derivative. Invalid B-norms and zero/non-finite projections also silently break and return a still-sub-floor response. Negative `xᵀAx/xᵀBx` (an indefinite exact Hessian / non-minimum) is currently sent through the same “near-null” projection instead of being rejected.

Those are fallback semantics, not an analytic root fix: they can manufacture a finite gradient without a converged refinement and violate SPEC's no-fallback/converged-only contracts. I am replacing them with explicit convergence/invariant failures and a postcondition that no returned IFT response remains below the identifiable-curvature floor. The focused battery is submitted on MSI as job `12937006` (pinned to the SHA above): saturated-gate IFT, the full rational-logdet suite, and the #2080 outer-gradient gate.

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-11T04:04:46Z ---
## Wide-p perf scoping (deep trace, HEAD)

**The cubic-in-width border cost is resolved and engaged magic-by-default on the plain-SAE path — not just crosscoder.** All three drivers call `ensure_decoder_frames_active_for_current_decoder` (dense `fit_drivers.rs:4899`, streaming `fit_drivers.rs:6400`, crosscoder `crosscoder_fit.rs:848`). Per-atom Grassmann frames `B_k=C_k Uᵀ` activate at `p≥12` & `r≤0.75p`, so the arrow-Schur border carries `Σ_k M_k·r` (r≈8–32) instead of `Σ_k M_k·p`. Reduced Schur factorization and covariance become **p-independent**.

Measured (MSI job 12943297, commit 6d4cff82e, N=1500 p=4096): border `32768→64` (512×), covariance `8.59 GB→32 KB`, wall 4.35 s, MaxRSS 432 MB. The "O(p³) border Cholesky dies / 8.6 GB per atom" regime is gone.

**The remaining wide-p cost is iteration COUNT, not width.** On co-collapsed / near-singular geometry the inner Newton crawls a flat inter-atom gauge direction — each Armijo step lowers the objective sub-√εmach while ‖g‖ stays above tol — grinding the full ≥1024 inner `max_iter` at ~1 s/iterate, multiplied through the 6+ outer ρ probes. That is the K≥2 "hours-long hang," and it is a convergence-RATE problem, not a per-iterate p cost.

**Ranked perf levers (scoped):**
1. **Warm-start the inner joint fit across ρ probes** — today each criterion/fd probe cold-re-runs `run_joint_fit_arrow_schur` up to ≥1024 iterates; reuse the separated incumbent from ρ₀ as the seed for adjacent probes. `O(probes×1024×s)` → `O(probes×few×s)`.
2. **Fail-fast non-PD ρ probes** — a non-PD cross-row IBP Hessian at a probe should score infeasible-with-gradient and move the bracket, not retry into the inner budget (CPU-verifiable on the p=96 planted-circles fixture).
3. **Quotient the inter-atom shared-subspace gauge** at the inner level (analogous to the single-atom chart-gauge deflation at `fit_drivers.rs:1474`) so the grad/step gates clear at the true optimum instead of grinding — the deep root fix (research-grade).

Already landed and holding: K≥2 co-collapse fix (7a93b1d06), value-probe purity (cca741e3f), bounded probe budget (`wide_p_outer_reml_terminates_within_probe_budget_2080`: EV 0.9085, 6 criterion calls, 0 mutating probes), converged-gated acceptance (f98ef0cad).

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-12T14:14:28Z ---
## Wide-K outer REML: status audit + the analytic-gradient increment (matrix-free θ-adjoint via a single adjoint solve)

Audited at HEAD (paths verified live; the surrogate files have **moved** — see §6). This settles what the rational-log-det surrogate epic has actually delivered, locates the one cubic object still on the critical path, and works the math for the three ways forward the perf-scoping trace left open. Recommendation: **(A)**, and it turns out to cost ~**one extra matrix-free solve per outer eval**, not O(P_ρ).

### 0. The perf structure has three independent axes — name them precisely

| axis | cost | status |
|---|---|---|
| **ambient p** (output channels) | per-atom border `Σ_k M_k·p`, `O(p³)` reduced-Schur factor, 8.6 GB/atom | **RESOLVED** — Grassmann decoder frames `B_k=C_kUᵀ` (`p≥12 & r≤0.75p`) reduce the border to `Σ_k M_k·r` (r≈8–32), p-independent (measured 512×, comment 4942241098) |
| **dictionary K** (reduced-Schur dim) | dense `K×K` Schur Cholesky `O(K³)` for `log\|S\|` + `tr(S⁻¹M)` | **VALUE done, GRADIENT half-done** — the subject of this comment |
| **iteration count** | flat inter-atom gauge crawl, EFS linear rate ~0.997/iter | **the dominant remaining wide-K cost** (comment 4942241098) |

"Cubic in width" today means **axis K** (the ambient-p cubic is gone). And the payoff of fixing it is realized only by also attacking **iteration count** — which is exactly what the analytic gradient does.

### 1. What the surrogate epic landed (value + trace channels)

The evidence term splits exactly `log|H| = Σ_i log|H_tt^(i)| + log|S|`, `S` = reduced Schur (`K×K` border).

- **VALUE, matrix-free, active at k≥4096.** `log|S/c| = tr log(S/c)` via DE quadrature of the resolvent (deterministic; the truncation window `t∈[λ_min·rel_tol, λ_max/rel_tol]` bounds both tails by `rel_tol`, node count `O(log κ)` — the `3bb8d4f80` window fix) **+ frozen Hutch++ deflation** (`term1 = tr(Qᵀlog(S/c)Q)` exact over a frozen rank-r `Q`, `term2 = tr(P log(S/c) P)` Hutchinson over projected probes, `P=I−QQᵀ`), with **CRN** (probes frozen across ρ). Derived-rank policy grows `r` until `std_err ≤ 0.1·STALL_REL_TOL·(|log_det|+1)`. The "wide-κ 5.57σ bias" scare was retired as probe-RNG aliasing (comment 4930519163) — the surrogate is unbiased.
- **GRADIENT trace channels, matrix-free, all four LANDED + FD-gated** against dense selected-inverse: the shared bundle `(z_j, S⁻¹z_j)` (one CG solve family per eval, warm-started) feeds
  `ard_inverse_traces_from_probes`, `ard_log_precision_hessian_trace_from_probes`, `decoder_smoothness_effective_dof_per_atom_from_probes`, `assignment_log_strength_hessian_trace_from_probes`, and the θ-adjoint envelope `logdet_theta_adjoint_from_probes`. Each is `tr(S⁻¹M_l) ≈ (1/m)Σ_j (S⁻¹z_j)ᵀ(M_l z_j)` — **one bundle reused across all outer coordinates l**.

### 2. The gap — massive-K runs a value-only outer

Even though every gradient channel exists matrix-free, the **complete analytic outer gradient is not the production massive-K route**. Per `analytic_outer_rho_gradient_components_with_bundle` (`manifold/construction_exact_hessian.rs:873`, docstring): production Hybrid-EFS evaluates **only** the assignment-strength coordinate analytically (`analytic_assignment_strength_gradient_matrix_free`) and leaves smoothness/ARD on **Fellner-Schall** fixed-point updates; the `Some`-bundle assembler is retained "for exact dense/bundle parity … not as the production matrix-free route," because its IFT correction "requires **one exact-stationarity solve per active outer coordinate**" and still accepts the dense `DeflatedArrowSolver`. So at k≥4096 the outer `OuterEval` is value-only (zero gradient) and the loop is **EFS, linear rate 0.9965–0.9979/iter** (the repair-design cluster) — the "hours-long hang." The terminal exact-Newton polish (`7763e8478`) that would finish superlinearly rides `solve_exact_stationarity`, dense at massive-K.

**The four gaps, precise:** (i) complete analytic gradient dense-only by design (this §); (ii) every from_probes channel **hard-refuses deflated rows** → those fits fall to dense (the plain-S⁻¹ bundle can't carry the Daleckii–Krein correction; tested `..._refuses_deflated_rows_2080`); (iii) SLQ's CPU lane still assembles dense `S` for `S·v` (`O(K²)` memory, no device matvec); (iv) k<4096 always pays dense `O(K³)` Cholesky.

### 3. The one cubic object still on the critical path

At massive-K the value is matrix-free, so **no `O(K³)` remains in the value**. The cubic cost re-enters only through gap (i): the analytic gradient's IFT correction, as currently written, is `P_ρ` exact-stationarity solves on the dense `DeflatedArrowSolver` (which materializes the `K×K` selected inverse). That is why the gradient is dense-gated and the massive-K outer is EFS-only.

### 4. Options weighed, with the math

Let `V(ρ) = fit + ½log|H(θ*(ρ),ρ)| + pen`. Envelope theorem at the inner optimum `θ*`:
```
dV/dρ_l = ∂V/∂ρ_l|_θ  +  ½·Γᵀ (dθ*/dρ_l),     Γ = tr(H⁻¹ ∂H/∂θ) = ∂log|H|/∂θ
```
(the fit part is θ-stationary so drops; `log|H|` is **not** θ-stationary, so Γ ≠ 0 — this is the whole reason a θ-adjoint exists). `Γ` is already produced matrix-free from the bundle. With `dθ*/dρ_l = −H_θθ⁻¹ ∂²L/∂θ∂ρ_l`:
```
½·Γᵀ dθ*/dρ_l = −½ (H_θθ⁻¹ Γ)ᵀ ∂²L/∂θ∂ρ_l = −½ aᵀ ∂²L/∂θ∂ρ_l ,   a := H_θθ⁻¹ Γ   (ONE solve)
```
For every outer coordinate `∂²L/∂θ∂ρ_l = λ_l'·S_l θ` (smoothing) or the ARD analogue — a cheap structured apply. **So the IFT correction over all `P_ρ` coordinates is one adjoint solve `a = H_θθ⁻¹Γ` plus `P_ρ` inner products** — not `P_ρ` solves. `H_θθ` is the arrow `H`; `a` rides the same reduced-Schur CG as the bundle (single-RHS `reduced_schur_inverse_apply`, warm-started off the bundle solves). The current per-coordinate implementation is simply the forward (non-adjoint) form.

- **(A) Route the full matrix-free analytic gradient at massive-K, via the single-adjoint θ-IFT.** Cost per outer eval: the existing value bundle (`m` solves) **+ 1 adjoint solve** + `O(P_ρ)` cheap contractions. Payoff: the outer loop becomes **BFGS/Newton on an exact analytic gradient — superlinear** — replacing EFS's `0.997/iter` linear crawl. This is the only option that attacks axis "iteration count," the dominant remaining cost. New work is small and well-scoped: (1) reformulate the IFT as the single adjoint above (correct + `O(1)` solves); (2) route `efs_step` to consume the gradient when the surrogate lane is active, under invariant #1 (emit-request/assert-consume, all-or-nothing); (3) keep the deflated-row hard-refuse → such fits fall to dense (gap ii), a conservative, tested fallback.
- **(B) Keep EFS as the massive-K outer; close gaps (ii)/(iii).** (ii) = extend from_probes to carry the Daleckii–Krein correction for deflated rows; (iii) = a device `S·v` so SLQ stops materializing `S` (`O(K²)` → streaming) — this is **#1017's** device-residency surface, cross-linked. But both are **per-iterate** improvements (memory, robustness); neither touches **iteration count**. EFS stays linear-rate `0.9965–0.9979/iter` ⇒ `O(10³)` iters to strict KKT, and the superlinear terminal polish is dense. So (B) leaves the dominant cost in place.
- **(C) Lower the 4096 dense threshold.** Net-negative at mid-K: dense `O(K³)` Cholesky is exact and cheap for `k<4096` (`k=4096 → 6.9e10` flops, ~seconds, 128 MB), while the surrogate pays `m` CG solves at `O(K²·iters)` each — comparable cost, now approximate. Justified only under a memory wall, which 128 MB is not. Reject absent a measured crossover.

**Recommendation: (A)**, with (B)'s gap (ii) as a follow-up and gap (iii) handed to #1017.

### 5. Admissibility + composition with the certificate doctrine

The gradient is admissible iff it is the **exact** gradient of the surrogate **value** — otherwise the value↔gradient desync class (#2087 / #2266 / E1) reopens. Two properties make it exact by construction:
1. **Frozen-Q + CRN** make the surrogate value a smooth deterministic function of ρ; a frozen deflation basis makes the fixed-Q directional derivative exact, so the bundle contraction **is** `d(surrogate)/dρ`. The adjoint `a = H⁻¹Γ` must use the **same** frozen deflation + CG tolerance as the value's `S⁻¹` solves ⇒ one functional across value, ρ-grad, and θ-adjoint ⇒ desync closed.
2. **Invariant #1 (all-or-nothing).** The gradient consumes the bundle exactly when the value took the surrogate lane; extend it so the adjoint-RHS solve is requested/asserted together with the trace bundle — never a partial mix.
3. **Deflated-row hard-refuse (gap ii)** keeps the plain-S⁻¹ bundle honest: rather than silently double-adding a Daleckii–Krein term it cannot form, a deflating fit routes to dense — a desync-in-miniature avoided, already tested.

Error budget the certificate must see: deterministic quadrature `≤ rel_tol` (shared by value and derivative ⇒ cancels in FD gates), stochastic `std_err ≤ 0.1·STALL_REL_TOL·(|log_det|+1)` by the derived-rank policy. The outer KKT gate admits the surrogate gradient exactly when this band is below its stationarity tolerance — which the derived-rank policy enforces.

### 6. Stale-location flag (for the next session)

The surrogate lane files **moved** `crates/gam-sae/src/*.rs → crates/gam-sae/src/manifold/*.rs`. Any memory citing the flat paths is stale. Current, verified:
- `manifold/construction_quasi_laplace.rs` — `logdet_theta_adjoint_from_probes:4561`, `assignment_log_strength_hessian_trace_from_probes:3210`
- `manifold/construction_ard.rs` — `ard_inverse_traces_from_probes:201`, `ard_log_precision_hessian_trace_from_probes:1072`
- `manifold/construction_smoothness_dof.rs` — `decoder_smoothness_effective_dof_per_atom_from_probes:144`
- `manifold/construction_exact_hessian.rs` — `analytic_outer_rho_gradient_components_with_bundle:873` (the dense-parity assembler + the "one solve per coordinate" IFT to be replaced by the single adjoint)
- `manifold/outer_objective.rs` — `surrogate_lane:639`, `efs_step:2658`, `direct_logdet_admitted` routing at `:698/:2708`

### ISSUE #2132 [OPEN] — sae_manifold_fit dictionary co-collapses on planted circle mixtures (held-out EV low, decreasing in K, below linear PCA)
Author: SauersML   Created: 2026-07-04T22:01:58Z   Labels: 
Comments: 18
------------------------------------------------------------------------
BODY:
## Summary

On planted mixtures of clean circles, `sae_manifold_fit` (multi-atom dictionary) reaches
low held-out reconstruction EV that **decreases with K** (dictionary co-collapse), and
underperforms both a trivial linear-PCA baseline and its own linear-atom variant on the
exact curved structure it is designed to capture.

## Reproduction (gamfit 0.1.248)

Data: `N=1500` tokens, each lying on **exactly one** of `C` planted unit circles in a
random 2-plane of R^p (single-active, so top-1 routing is exact), 5% noise, 20% held out.
Fit `sae_manifold_fit(train, K, d_atom=1, atom_topology="circle"/"linear", top_k=1,
n_iter=12, _run_structure_search=False)`; score held-out EV via `reconstruct(test)`.

Measured (held-out EV; train `reconstruction_r2` in parens):

| regime | linear PCA @matched rank | curved (circle) | same-lane linear (`atom_topology="linear"`) |
|---|---|---|---|
| C=3, p=12, K=6 | ~0.73 (rank 3) | **0.23** (train 0.54) | — |
| C=6, p=24, K=6 | ~0.55 (rank 6) | **0.26** (train 0.37) | 0.25 (train 0.57) |
| C=6, p=24, K=8 | ~0.56 | **0.11** (train 0.46) | 0.25 (train 0.57) |
| C=8, p=48, K=6 | — | **0.23** (train 0.41) | — |

Two problems visible:
1. **Co-collapse**: curved held-out EV *drops* from 0.26 (K=6) to 0.11 (K=8) — more atoms
   make it worse. Inner-fit logs emit `[#1026] restoring incumbent` / `dictionary
   co-collapse ... reseeding all atoms`.
2. **Large train→held-out gap** (both lanes: train ~0.55 → held-out ~0.25), i.e. the
   out-of-sample encode/reconstruct path generalizes poorly, and curved atoms
   underperform even the linear-atom variant on curved data.

A linear PCA reconstruction at the matched rank reaches 0.55–0.73 on the identical data,
so the structure is trivially recoverable — this is a solver-quality gap, not a data
problem.

## Also (0.1.247 only)

`reconstruct(test)` on a circle fit raises
`sae_manifold_predict_oos: decoder_blocks[0] has M=2 but rebuilt basis has M=3` — the
trained decoder width and the OOS basis rebuild disagree (M=2 vs M=3). 0.1.248 is
consistent (M=3) and does not raise, but the held-out EV gap above suggests the OOS
encode path is still the weak point.

## Why it matters

This blocks a compute-matched curved-vs-linear dictionary frontier (curved cannot reach
the linear reconstruction ceiling here, let alone beat it at fewer atoms). The single-
chart `K=1` fits used in the dose-calibration work are unaffected; the failure is specific
to the multi-atom dictionary sweep. Harness + raw JSONs:
`SauersML/Manifold-SAE:experiments/frontier_bench.py`,
`results/suite_2026-07-03/frontiers/exact_p24_curved.json`.

On that consistent metric the curved dictionary sits at 0.23–0.26 (decreasing in K) vs linear-PCA 0.55–0.73.

Two of the three legs of this failure are now isolated with numbers (2026-07-08, manifold-zoo arena micro: K=6 atoms, 6 planted factors incl. circle/sphere/disk, L0=2, N=700):

Periodic (circle) ARD math corrected in 7c95a0c31 — directly relevant to circle-atom evidence/precision here, though **not a claimed fix** for the co-collapse:

- **von-Mises normalizer** was missing the period Jacobian `n_eff·ln P` (`log Z = ln P − η + log I0(η)`, `η=α/κ²`). No-op at `P=1`; corrects non-unit periodic axes in absolute (cross-K/topology) evidence.
- **ARD empirical-Bayes precision** step was the Gaussian fixed point `α = φ̂·n_eff/(Σq + trH⁻¹)` — only the `η→∞` limit of the von-Mises criterion. Periodic axes now solve the exact stationary root `A(η) = 1 − 1/(2·η_gauss)`, `A=I1/I0`, `η_gauss=α_gauss/κ²`, by safeguarded bisection.

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-10T04:42:46Z ---
## Remaining structural coupling found and fixed: the scale-gauge cure was never engaged on the public `sae_manifold_fit` path (missed-entry default) — flipped in 1f2981be8

Per the re-measure request, I traced the top-1 routing + gate/amplitude interaction on HEAD to check whether anything still couples atom supports after the landed fixes (fit-level incumbent 73dd39009, occupancy-scaled Jeffreys f46b1bccf, OOS-ρ* round-trip 71f06cce1, periodic-ARD 7c95a0c31). There was one live coupling left, and it is a plumbing gap, not new math:

**The mechanism (still live until today).** The default `ibp_map` gate is `a_k = σ(l_k/τ)·π_k` with the ordered stick-breaking mean `π_k = (α/(α+1))^{k+1}` (`assignment.rs::ibp_map_row`). Every atom's gate is capped by its column index — at α=1 that is 0.5, 0.25, 0.125, … — while the decoder smoothness penalty is scaled by λ only, so atom k's decoder is effectively over-shrunk by `1/π_k²` (4×, 16×, 64×…). On single-active planted mixtures with top-1 routing, each additional circle is served by a higher-index, harder-capped atom: exactly "held-out EV decreasing in K". Because all active atoms are over-shrunk in lockstep, the median-keyed collapse retraction never fires (no atom is small relative to its peers).

**The cure exists and is support-independent**: `pin_scale_gauge` (`fit_drivers.rs:5655-5676`) peels every atom's ‖B_k‖ into the UNPENALIZED log-amplitude `s_k` at accepted iterates (unit-B̂, scale-free smoothness) and re-homes `exp(s_k) ≈ 1/a_k` by a joint data-optimal solve with a monotone keep-best safeguard — so every active atom reaches the target regardless of its π_k cap, and healthy fits are inert. It is gated on `quotient_scale`.

**The gap**: d06c1255f flipped `quotient_scale` default→true on `sae_manifold_fit_inner`'s pyo3 signature (the precomputed-basis entry) and declared the public path engaged — but `gamfit.sae_manifold_fit` routes through `sae_manifold_fit_minimal` (`latent_basis_and_sae_ffi_tail.rs`), whose signature still said `quotient_scale = false`, and the Python facade never passes the kwarg. So every fit in this issue's repro family has run with the gauge OFF, including any post-d06c1255f re-measure. **Fixed in 1f2981be8**: the minimal entry now defaults true (the flag is forwarded verbatim into the shared inner: term switch + seed-decoder norm peel), matching the sibling entry and the term constructor (`construction.rs:211`).

**Why the landed set should now resolve this issue's headline numbers**, per leg:
- EV decreasing in K = π_k over-shrink, cured by the (now actually engaged) scale gauge; higher-index atoms keep unit-shape decoders with amplitude carrying the 1/π_k magnitude.
- Terminal-state decay across ρ probes = fit-level reconstruction incumbent (73dd39009) + objective-keyed incumbent (#2230, d10757054).
- Collapse ranked better than structure = occupancy-scaled Jeffreys barrier (f46b1bccf), extensive in co-fired N_eff.
- Train-vs-held-out gap = OOS solve now decodes under the fit's ρ* (71f06cce1).

**Confirming measurement** (one shot, wheel ≥ 1f2981be8): the issue's own planted-circle sweep — C=3/p=12 and C=6/p=24, K ∈ {C, C+2, 2C}, `top_k=1`, held-out `ev(test, reconstruct(test))`. Accept: EV non-decreasing in K and ≥ the matched-rank linear-PCA floor (0.73/0.55). A cheap in-tree discriminator already exists (`tests_collapse_2132`), but the sweep on the Python surface is the honest close-out since the defect was in the FFI default.

## Acceptance-harness audit: the landed driver currently asks an impossible question

`experiments/scale_close/driver_2132_planted_circle_ev_vs_k.py` currently computes a fresh PCA baseline at `rank=K` and requires the curved fit to beat it by +0.05 for every K in the sweep.

That conflicts with this thread's latest requested sweep `K ∈ {C, C+2, 2C}`. The planted signal lives in exactly `2C` orthogonal linear directions, so at `K=2C` a rank-K PCA spans the entire noiseless signal. No curved model can beat that EV-optimal full-signal linear reconstruction by +0.05. The existing harness therefore cannot pass even for an oracle curved dictionary.

The thread's stated acceptance numbers — PCA floors 0.73 for C=3/p=12 and 0.55 for C=6/p=24 — are the fixed rank-C linear baselines from the original reproduction, not a rank-K baseline that grows through 2C.

I am correcting the close driver to the actual issue contract:

1. run C=3/p=12 and C=6/p=24 with K={C,C+2,2C}, top_k=1;
2. compute one fixed rank-C PCA floor on the identical held-out split;
3. require curved held-out EV at every K to clear that floor;
4. require curved EV to be non-decreasing in K (within the explicitly reported numerical tolerance).

This is a harness correction, not a relaxation: it restores the exact comparator and sweep named in the issue and removes a mathematically impossible +0.05-over-rank-2C condition.

```
dictionary did not escape total co-collapse after 3 reseed multi-starts
(reconstruction EV=0.5187 at or below the signal-free null floor 0.5208);
every atom's decoder co-vanished and no residual structure could anchor
K=4 distinct charts for this input
[mu_hat_max=below-null-bar, decoder_norms=[23.13, 33.49, 32.11, 26.67]]
```

**Notes that sharpen the diagnosis here:**
- The decoder **norms are large and unequal** (23–33), yet the guard reports "every atom's decoder co-vanished" — i.e. co-collapse is **directional redundancy** (atoms spanning the same residual subspace), not literal norm decay. ## Co-collapse mechanism ranking + registered predictions (before study 13032206 lands)

Static analysis of the K≥2 planted-circle fit path. Predictions registered **before** the running study so its output can be read against them immediately. Framing: co-collapse is a family of **degeneracy directions — flat (or nearly flat) in data-fit, but not flat in the penalty/evidence/seed** — that the objective slides down. The seven mechanisms differ in *which* degeneracy and *when* it bites.

The single sharpest discriminator already on this issue: **same `ibp_map` assignment, LINEAR topology → 0.74, CIRCLE topology → 0.13.** That rules out routing as the primary and forces a curved-basis-specific driver into the ranking (M3 below).

### Ranked mechanisms — what each predicts the study will show

| # | Mechanism (code site) | Predicted signature in the study output | EV-vs-K shape | Hang? |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| **1** | **Ordered geometric prior shrinkage.** Gate `a_k = σ(l_k/τ)·π_k`, `π_k=(α/(α+1))^{k+1}`; decoder smoothness scaled by λ only ⇒ atom k over-shrunk by `1/π_k²`. Under top-1 routing each additional circle is served by a higher-index, harder-capped atom. | Terminal per-atom amplitude / ‖B_k‖ **decays monotonically in atom index**, ratio ≈ `α/(α+1)` per step (≈0.5 at α=1). Reconstruction of the k-th circle scales ≈ `π_k²`. | **Monotone decreasing** (the headline signature) | No — completes, low EV |
| **2** | **Cure is blinded (median-keyed guard + Softmax-only gauge).** `pin_scale_gauge`/collapse guards key off the **median** atom scale; when atoms co-shrink *together* the median moves with them, so nothing looks anomalous. Gauge only corrects the Softmax gate, not OrderedBetaBernoulli. | With `quotient_scale` nominally ON: ‖B_k‖ **still** decays in index (amplitude not re-homed) **and** `collapse_events == []` despite low EV. | reinforces #1 | No |
| **3** | **Curved-basis roughness scale degeneracy** (my degeneracy-pressure lens; the topology discriminator). Harmonic columns carry `λ‖B″‖²`; the map (curved `B→γB`, amplitude `→/γ`) is flat in data-fit but strictly downhill in roughness as `γ→0`, so the inner-Newton drives **curved B→0**. Linear (first-harmonic core, no curvature penalty) has no such direction. | **CIRCLE arm collapses; a LINEAR control on the same data recovers ≈ PCA floor.** Terminal curved-column ‖B‖→0 with constant/first-harmonic columns surviving. Gap is **topology-keyed, present even at K=C** (not purely a K effect). | topology gap at all K | **Possibly** — B→0 ⇒ near-singular H_tt |
| **4** | **Seed collision / redundant seating** (`pca_seed.rs:592-613`, `pair=(k+off)%(p/2)`; #1893 reroutes surplus). Only `C` of the seeded PC-pairs align with planted-circle 2-planes; atoms `C..K` seed onto noise planes (or, if #1893 rerouting is ineffective, exact duplicates at `(k, k+p/2)`). | If #1893 inert: **pairwise decoder cosine ≈1 at index pairs `(k, k+p/2)`**. If effective: surplus atoms distinct-but-noise (low individual EV, redundant). Primary driver of the **stagewise flat-below-floor** regime. | flat-below-floor (stagewise); mild decreasing (joint) | Only if raw duplicates ⇒ rank-deficient block |
| **5** | **Barrier abstention** (`penalties.rs:926-1004`: `ε_C=∞` when `min N_eff→0` ⇒ `continue`). On disjoint-support planted circles each atom fires on its own rows ⇒ cross-atom co-fire ≈0 ⇒ the anti-collapse barrier **switches off by construction**. | Barrier ledger shows `ε=inf` / components with `s<2` for the planted-circle fit ⇒ separation barrier contributes ≈0. Explains why the leg-2 barrier fix does **not** prevent *this* collapse (scope mismatch: barrier targets *collinear co-firing*, not amplitude/topology collapse). | permissive (no shape of its own) | No |
| **6** | **Ville birth gate blocks escape.** After collapse the residual looks like noise ⇒ held-out e-value birth gate rejects ⇒ stuck in the low-effective-K basin. | `births_rejected>0`, early stall; **effective active-atom count < K**. Birth/stagewise lane. | stalls at low K | No |
| **7** | **Evidence `K=2C < K=C`.** Downstream scoreboard: the penalized criterion scores fewer atoms better because extra atoms can't overcome `½·d_eff·log n + 1/π_k` (the `1/π_k` term **is** #1). | Criterion-vs-K and EV-vs-K both **peak near K=C** then decline. | non-monotone, peak at ≈C | No |

### What EV-decreasing-in-K specifically discriminates

- **Monotone decreasing in K (each added atom HURTS)** ⇒ destructive over-shrink / support-stealing: **#1 (+#2 cure-blinded, +#3 as the collapse direction)**. This is the **cold-joint** signature.
- **Flat-below-floor (added atoms neither help nor hurt)** ⇒ redundant seating: **#4** (extra atoms are noise/duplicate copies). This is the **stagewise** signature (matches the reported 0.594-flat-across-8-births).
- So the cold-joint-decreasing vs stagewise-flat split is **two different mechanisms**, not one: joint = #1/#3, stagewise = #4. A fix that cures one will not move the other.

### Hang vs slow convergence (the test times out at 3h)

Decisive top-level fork the study resolves:

- **If it HANGS (no K-row, outer cascade idles):** the driver is in the **rank-deficiency family — #3 (curved B→0 ⇒ near-singular per-row H_tt ⇒ non-PD reduced Schur ⇒ reseed-crawl) or #4-raw (duplicate seeds ⇒ rank-deficient joint block).** Prior history (project_1026/1388) shows exactly this: inner Newton crawls with ‖g‖ huge, Schur Cholesky hits a non-PD pivot, reseed loop, outer goes idle. **A 3h timeout with zero result rows is my prediction for the #3/#4 regime, not #1.**
- **If it COMPLETES with low/decreasing EV:** the driver is the **shrinkage/selection family — #1, #7, #5, #2** — which degrade EV but never singularize the inner solve, so the fit returns within budget.

### My ranking for the planted-circle regime (K up to ≈2C)

1. **#1 geometric-prior shrinkage** — the most direct monotone-decreasing driver; needs no ill-conditioning.
2. **#3 curved-roughness B→0** — required to explain the LINEAR-vs-CIRCLE topology gap; likely the source of any **hang**.
3. **#2 cure-blindness** — the reason #1/#3 aren't already cured (median-keyed + Softmax-only).
4. **#4 seed collision/redundancy** — dominant for the **stagewise flat-below-floor** sub-result; secondary for cold-joint.
5. **#5 Ville gate**, **#7 evidence**, **#2 barrier-abstention** — permissive/scoreboard, not drivers.

**One cheap experiment per top mechanism** (each ≈1 fit + terminal-state read, no 9.4h needed): #1 → terminal ‖B_k‖ vs index with `quotient_scale` on/off (geometric decay vs uniform); #3 → CIRCLE vs LINEAR on identical data, and CIRCLE at `smoothness λ→0` (collapse should vanish if roughness is the degeneracy); #4 → pairwise decoder cosine at `(k,k+p/2)` + per-atom coord→planted-circle assignment; #5 → `births_rejected`/`stopped_reason`; #2 → dump barrier `ε_C` per component (expect `inf`).

The prediction I'd stake the most on: **the CIRCLE arm's EV-vs-K is monotone-decreasing with per-atom ‖B_k‖ decaying ≈geometrically in index (#1), a LINEAR control on the same data does NOT decrease (#3), and if the run times out it does so as a non-PD-Schur reseed-crawl with no K-row (#3/#4), not as slow-but-progressing convergence.**


--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-12T14:41:24Z ---
### Update — mechanism #3 analytically confirmed (still before the study lands)

A term-by-term derivation (#2228 issuecomment-4951568325) proves **mechanism #3** (the curved-basis over-smoothing degeneracy) analytically, and exhibits it at K=1 on real GPT-2: the quasi-Laplace criterion is **unbounded below** as any atom over-smooths to collapse — `½·log|β-Schur| → −∞`, *extensive* in the data, as `a²‖B‖² → 0`, while the reconstruction loss stays finite and the Occam/complexity term is subdominant. So the collapse is not a basin the optimizer wanders into; it is the criterion's actual infimum. That is exactly the #3 degeneracy above (curved `B→0`: flat in data-fit, strictly downhill in the penalized criterion), now with a closed form and a real-data instance.

Directly relevant to what **this** study decides: the occupancy-scaled Jeffreys anti-collapse barrier is **K≥2-gated** (`penalties.rs:124/214` early-return) and prices only **pairwise** decoder overlaps. A lone atom — or an individual atom solo-collapsing *inside* a K≥2 fit — has **no counter-term at all**. The K=1 self-Jeffreys term (diagonal analogue, same `ε_C` MP-edge calibration) is being added; the **per-atom-at-all-K extension is the open decision this study informs.**

**What this sharpens in the registry:**

- **#3 moves from candidate to confirmed driver** (at K=1). The study's remaining job is the **relative weight of #3 vs #1 (prior shrinkage) vs #4 (seed collision)** in the K≥2 planted-mixture regime.
- **New decisive question:** does the pairwise (off-diagonal) barrier suffice for K≥2, or are per-atom (diagonal) self-terms needed? My **‖B_k‖-vs-index confirmer discriminates exactly this:**
  - if individual atoms *solo*-collapse — some `‖B_k‖→0` while their pairwise decoder overlaps stay small, so the pairwise barrier never engages — **per-atom self-terms are required**;
  - if collapse appears only as pairwise decoder alignment (high `(k,k+p/2)` cosine, co-firing overlap), the off-diagonal barrier is the right locus and just needs to be un-gated / un-blinded (#2, the median-keyed + Softmax-only blindness).
- **Hang prediction, refined:** because the criterion is genuinely *unbounded below* along the collapse direction (not merely a competitive basin), the inner solve has **no finite stationary point** to converge to along it — which reinforces the earlier call that a 3h timeout in the #3-dominated regime is a **non-PD-Schur reseed-crawl with no K-row**, not slow-but-progressing convergence.

Net: the top of the ranking is now #3 (analytically confirmed) as the *direction* of collapse, with #1 setting *which* atoms collapse first (high-index, geometric-prior over-shrink) and #4 governing the stagewise flat-below-floor sub-result. The study's highest-value readout is the per-atom `‖B_k‖`-vs-index profile with the barrier ledger, because it decides pairwise-vs-per-atom for the counter-term design.


--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-12T15:48:12Z ---
### Update 2 — attractor vs detector-gap taxonomy (+ two more detector gaps)

Sharpening the frame so the study readout attributes every observation to one of two distinct failure classes:

**A. The collapse ATTRACTOR — the criterion's own pull toward collapse.**
- **#3** curved-`B→0`, unbounded-below (analytically confirmed): the criterion's infimum *is* collapse.
- **#1** geometric-prior over-shrink: biases *which* atoms collapse first (high index).

**B. DETECTOR / COUNTER-TERM GAPS — defenses that go blind in exactly the failure regime.**
- **#2a — barrier co-firing blindness (sharpened): functional redundancy ≠ co-activation redundancy.** Under top-1 / near-disjoint routing two atoms can decode the *same output structure* while **never co-firing**. The occupancy-scaled Jeffreys barrier prices only co-*activation* overlap (`Q∘O` on co-firing edges), so it is structurally blind to functionally-redundant-but-disjoint-support atoms — which is precisely the planted-circle regime (disjoint supports by construction).
- **#2b — the K>R detector gate (new).** `structural_coherence_collapsed_pairs` early-returns "no collapsed pairs" when `K > R` (union output-frame rank), to avoid overcomplete false-positives — but that **disables the duplicate detector exactly in the overcomplete regime where duplicates are most likely**, and the stronger second-stage contribution-cosine test is never reached past that gate.
- **#2c — median-keyed guard blindness** (already registered as #2): when atoms co-shrink *together* the median moves with them, so no atom looks anomalous and the guard never fires.

**Why the taxonomy is the load-bearing readout:**
- Collapse persists with detectors **notionally active** ⇒ the **attractor** is winning ⇒ the fix is a **counter-term / criterion** change (per-atom self-Jeffreys; or bound the `log|β-Schur|` reward so it is not unbounded-below).
- Collapse appears **only where a detector is gated off** (`K>R`, disjoint routing, median-blinded) ⇒ the **defenses failed to catch an otherwise-catchable collapse** ⇒ the fix is a **detector** change (price functional redundancy via decoder-subspace cosine, not co-activation; drop/repair the `K>R` gate; robustify the median key).

**How the cheap confirmers separate A from B** (per-atom `‖B_k‖`-vs-index + pairwise decoder-subspace cosine + barrier-`ε` ledger, read together):
- two atoms with **high decoder-subspace cosine, zero co-firing, barrier `ε` finite-but-zero-contribution** ⇒ functional-redundancy blindness (**#2a**);
- a duplicate pair present at **`K>R` with the collapsed-pairs detector returning empty** ⇒ the `K>R` gate (**#2b**);
- some `‖B_k‖→0` with **`collapse_events==[]`** and the median un-moved ⇒ median-blindness (**#2c**);
- `‖B_k‖→0` with **no** redundant partner at all (a solo atom decoding into an unpenalized-amplitude sink) ⇒ pure attractor **#3**, no detector could have caught it — needs the counter-term.

**Fix-direction (for whichever the study convicts):** the audit endorses **residual-row / residual-subspace births over PC reseeding** for entangled factors. Sequential PCA peeling assumes orthogonally-peelable components, but **entangled product manifolds need not peel**, so PC-pair seeds land off the true factor planes (mechanism **#4**). Residual-row/subspace births target the actual unexplained structure regardless of orthogonal peelability — that is the seed/birth fix if **#4** is convicted. If **#3/#2** are convicted instead, the fix is the per-atom self-Jeffreys counter-term (attractor) and/or functional-redundancy pricing + un-gated detector (defenses) — the two are independent and the study's per-atom profile says which is needed.


--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-12T16:04:36Z ---
### Defenses half of the fix — #2b landed; #2a is not a detector (analysis)

The detector/counter-term gaps are study-independent (they fail regardless of which attractor drives collapse), so they get fixed now rather than after the readout.

**#2b — the `K > R` detector gate: FIXED (landed 384ee2c8f, `fit_drivers.rs::structural_coherence_collapsed_pairs`).** The gate returned *no collapsed pairs* whenever `K > R` (union output-frame rank), to avoid the `ordered_beta_bernoulli` frame-only false positive — but that disabled the whole detector in the overcomplete regime, where duplicates are most likely, so the second-stage contribution-cosine verdict was never reached. The gate now drops **only** the PASS-1 frame-coherence prune (which is pigeonhole-forced and thus uninformative overcomplete), never the verdict: when `K > R` every pair is admitted as a candidate and **PASS-2 contribution-cosine adjudicates it**. That is exactly the functional-redundancy measure that stays valid overcomplete — a true duplicate has collinear gated contributions (cos→1, flagged); benign pigeonhole sharing sits at the independence null (not flagged), so the `ordered_beta_bernoulli` case is handled by the verdict stage rather than by blinding the detector. Pinning tests (in the same commit): `overcomplete_duplicate_is_detected_past_the_k_gt_r_gate_2132` (K=3 atoms in a 2-D output plane, R=2<K=3: the true duplicate `(0,1)` is now flagged where the old gate returned empty) and `overcomplete_distinct_phases_stay_silent_2132` (same overcomplete geometry, distinct phases: stays silent).

**#2a — functional-redundancy "independent of co-firing" is NOT implementable as an output-statistic detector without breaking a measured contract.** The governing regression `structural_coherence_detector_fires_on_duplicate_not_orthogonal_2082` **case (2)** pins the contract: two atoms with the *same decoder but different phases* (same output structure, disjoint rows) must **NOT** be flagged — the `ordered_beta_bernoulli` benign-overcomplete regression. That is exactly the shape #2a proposed to flag ("two atoms decode the same output structure while never co-firing"). The obstruction is fundamental, not incidental:

- For genuinely **disjoint-support** atoms, benign tiling (case 2) and a genuine same-chart duplicate differ **only in per-row coordinate alignment**, which is *unobservable* across disjoint rows (the two atoms never share a row to compare on).
- Every support-independent statistic collapses them to the same value: the output second-moment `Q_kC_kQ_k^T`, the decoded function `Φ(t)B`, and cross-reconstruction (`Φ_k` evaluated at atom j's coords) all give **identical** answers for case (2) and for a same-chart duplicate, because both pairs share the decoder and the coordinate *distribution*; only the row labels differ. So any such channel would false-fire on case (2).

Concretely: the reconstruction-redundancy that warrants a reseed is "one atom is removable without EV loss." For two atoms serving **different** rows with the same structure, removing one **loses those rows** → they are not redundant for reconstruction; they tile. Distinguishing over-tiling (each atom covers the *full* structure, so one is removable) from complementary tiling (each covers *part*) requires per-row coverage/alignment that disjoint supports do not expose to a post-hoc detector.

**Correct locus for the disjoint-support case: births, not a detector.** The remaining disjoint-support redundancy (two atoms seeded onto the *same* planted structure — the seed-collision / redundant-seating mechanism #4) is best prevented at **seed/birth time**, which matches the audit's endorsed direction: **residual-row / residual-subspace births over PC reseeding.** Sequential PCA peeling assumes orthogonally-peelable components; entangled product manifolds need not peel, so PC-pair seeds land off the true factor planes and duplicate coverage. A residual-row birth targets the actual unexplained structure, so a second atom is seeded onto an *uncovered* factor rather than a duplicate of a covered one — removing the duplicate before it exists, where "duplicate vs benign tiling" is still decidable (from the residual), instead of after, where it is not. This is the seed-side counterpart to #2b's decoder-side fix.

**Net (defenses):** #2b closes the overcomplete detector gap for co-firing duplicates (landed + pinned). #2a's disjoint-support case is a birth/seed problem (residual-row births), not a post-hoc output-cosine detector — a detector there cannot separate duplication from benign tiling without the per-row info disjoint supports hide. The attractor counter-term (per-atom self-Jeffreys at all K) remains the criterion-side fix and is sequenced behind e1's K=1 landing.

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-13T02:22:23Z ---
## Root cause of the `birth_reseed_sequential_deflation_separates_curved_atoms_2132` red (two bugs)

The green-oracle red at `b63a91522` was `reseeded == []` (the sequential-deflation reseed planted NOTHING). Two distinct bugs stacked here.

### Bug 1 (production): the noise-floor gate used the median, whose 50% breakdown point fails when signal fills half the (few) output directions

`leading_direction_above_noise_floor` estimated the residual noise scale as `median · log2(#dirs)`. The median only reads the noise level while fewer than half the directions carry signal. The full two-circle target's 4×4 output-Gram spectrum is `≈ [7.7, 7.7, 48, 48]` — both circles fill **all four** directions — so the median (27.8) is pulled onto circle A's own energy and `median·log2(4) = 55.7` buries the peak (48). The gate read genuine two-circle signal as pure noise, so the reseed terminated before atom 0 → `reseeded == []`.

Fix (`cd4518e9b`): estimate the noise subspace from the **lower quartile** instead of the median. It tolerates real structure spanning up to ~3/4 of the directions, yet — unlike the raw minimum — stays robust to a lone rank-deficient near-zero eigenvalue. Pure-noise spectra still sit below the `log2(#dirs)` Bonferroni floor, so the existing separation test (`leading_direction_above_noise_floor_separates_signal_from_noise_2132`) still passes; I added direct pins for the `[7.7,7.7,48,48]` and peeled-remainder `[~0,~0,7.7,7.7]` spectra.

### Bug 2 (test DGP): circle B was planted as circle A's exact 2nd harmonic — absorbable by the m=5 chart

With Bug 1 fixed, `reseeded` advanced to `[0]` but not `[0,1]`. The generator used `tb = 2·row + 0.37`, i.e. circle B winds **exactly twice** per revolution of circle A → circle B is the 2nd harmonic of atom 0's chart. With `m = 5` (harmonic order 2) atom 0's provisional decoder absorbs circle B through its own 2nd-harmonic columns, so the peeled residual is genuinely ~zero and the terminator **correctly** stops. That is right model behavior — one atom plus a 2nd-harmonic decoder is the parsimonious representation of an absorbable factor — so the `[0,1]` expectation, not production, was wrong; the docstring's "incommensurate" claim contradicted the commensurate 2× construction.

Fix (`f66e39350`): wind circle B **three** times per revolution (a harmonic index beyond the order-2 chart span), so neither circle lies in the other's harmonic reach. Atom 0's order-2 basis is orthogonal to circle B's 3rd harmonic over the grid, so it peels only circle A; the residual genuinely retains circle B; the second reseed lands atom 1 on it — exercising the real disjoint-structure separation the test names.

### Verification status (real runs)

- **Red reproduced** at `b63a91522`: `reseeded == []` (warm MSI, `cargo test -p gam-sae --lib`).
- **Bug 1 fix verified GREEN** on the exact #2132 spectra: the unit test `leading_direction_above_noise_floor_separates_signal_from_noise_2132`, extended with direct pins on `[7.7,7.7,48,48]` (the full two-circle Gram) and the peeled-remainder `[~0,~0,7.7,7.7]`, **passes** (warm MSI run at `016c01048`). This is the root production bug and it is confirmed fixed.
- **Bug 1 alone advances** `reseeded` from `[]` → `[0]` (real repro at `016c01048`), isolating Bug 2 as the remaining cause.
- **Bug 2 fix (winding-3)**: the end-to-end `birth_reseed_...2132` green rests on exact harmonic orthogonality (atom A's order-2 basis is orthogonal to circle B's 3rd harmonic over the uniform grid, so A peels only circle A and the residual retains circle B). A clean end-to-end run is currently blocked purely by MSI build contention — gam-sae's compile+link exceeds the citizen walltime on the oversubscribed nodes, and the fleet HEAD is torn (`gam-terms`/`row_jet_program` checkpoints), so no warm target holds a compiling SHA with these fixes. The green-oracle runs this exact test on each green SHA (it is what flagged the red), so it will confirm the end-to-end green on the next green SHA that carries both commits.

### ISSUE #2228 [OPEN] — SAC stagewise/manifold fit: RemlConvergenceError (inner solve stalls at fixed ρ) at LLM width p=4096 and on clean synthetic circles
Author: SauersML   Created: 2026-07-08T01:49:53Z   Labels: 
Comments: 37
------------------------------------------------------------------------
BODY:
## Summary

`sae_manifold_fit_stagewise` (and `sae_manifold_fit`) raise `RemlConvergenceError` — "inner solve did not converge at fixed ρ; objective stalled for 3 consecutive refine rounds" with a large residual KKT gradient (`‖g‖ ≈ 1e1–1e2`) — on LLM-width residual-stream activations (p = 4096), under **both** the Euclidean and the behavioral-Fisher metrics, and it does not terminate within 5 min at p = 4096. The same failure reproduces on **clean low-dimensional synthetic circle data**, so it is not specific to the LLM acts.

This blocks the App-B "Fisher currency" A/B (iid vs GLS reconstruction) from using the stagewise engine; that experiment fell back to a closed-form rank-r linear reconstructor. Filing so the fitter is fixed for the manifold path. Likely the same wide-`p` / structural-coherence cluster as #2080 / #1094.

## Repro

gamfit 0.1.250 (wheel `gamfit-0.1.250-cp310-abi3-manylinux_2_28`).

### A. clean synthetic circle, p = 8, K = 1

```python
import numpy as np, gamfit
rng = np.random.RandomState(0)
n, p = 120, 8
th = rng.uniform(0, 2*np.pi, n)
X = np.zeros((n, p)); X[:,0] = np.cos(th); X[:,1] = np.sin(th)
X += 0.05*rng.randn(n, p)
gamfit.sae_manifold_fit(np.ascontiguousarray(X), K=1, d_atom=1,
    atom_topology="circle", assignment="ibp_map", fisher_factors=None,
    n_iter=30, random_state=0)
# -> GamError: SaeManifoldTerm::reml_criterion: inner solve did not converge at
#    fixed ρ; neither the KKT gradient ‖g‖=1.37e2 nor the quotient KKT gradient
#    ‖Π⊥gauge g‖=1.37e2 met tolerance 3.45e-4
```

### B. real Qwen residual-stream acts, p = 4096, stagewise

```python
import numpy as np, gamfit
X = ...  # (70, 4096) last-token residual acts, mean-centered
gamfit.sae_manifold_fit_stagewise(np.ascontiguousarray(X), d_atom=1,
    atom_topology="circle", assignment="ibp_map", structured_whitening=False,
    fisher_factors=None, max_births=8, max_backfit_sweeps=2, n_iter=40,
    random_state=0)
# -> RemlConvergenceError: inner solve did not converge at fixed ρ; objective
#    stalled for 3 consecutive refine rounds (‖g‖=1.27e1, tol 2.6e-4) and the
#    undamped evidence factorization failed at each stall point
#    [RESEED-DIAG collapse_events=0 dict_reseeds=0 struct_reseeds=0]
# structured_whitening=True fails identically; hangs >5 min before erroring.
```

Both metrics (`fisher_factors=None` and a behavioral-Fisher shard) fail the same way. At p = 4096 the fit also does not return within 5 min.

## Expected

The stagewise / manifold fit should converge (or return a best-incumbent with a soft-fail flag) on a well-conditioned single circle at small p, and on mean-centered LLM-width acts. The REML inner solve stalling at a large `‖g‖` far above tol, with the undamped evidence factorization failing at the stall point, suggests the inner Newton/quotient step is not making progress under rank-deficient geometry at LLM width — a hard error here makes the manifold path unusable for reconstruction A/Bs.

## Notes

- Seen while landing App-B (behavioral-Fisher "nats currency"): the closed-form rank-r GLS-vs-PCA reconstructor was used instead and returns cleanly, so the currency measurement is unblocked — but the manifold fitter itself is the bug.
- `RESEED-DIAG collapse_events=0` on the p=4096 case (no reseeds fired), while the p=8 synthetic shows structural-coherence collapse/reseed churn — consistent with the co-collapse cluster.

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-08T16:01:29Z ---
## Diagnosis (HEAD 33a434af6, code-trace; local wheel is stale so no faithful repro): two DISTINCT failure modes under one error string, and neither is owned by the #2226 affine-invariant criterion

The `RemlConvergenceError` is raised from the `SaeManifoldTerm::reml_criterion` inner-solve refine loop (`crates/gam-sae/src/manifold/construction.rs`), which has **two** refusal branches with different predicates. The two repros in this issue hit different branches with different roots.

- **Branch 1** (`construction.rs:5734`): refine budget exhausted and neither the raw KKT gradient `‖g‖` nor the quotient `‖Π⊥gauge g‖` met `grad_tolerance = SAE_MANIFOLD_INNER_GRAD_REL_TOL(1e-5) · iterate_scale` (`:5507`). `‖g‖` is read straight off the assembled penalized system `sys.gt/gb` (`:5491`), i.e. factorization-independent.
- **Branch 2** (`construction.rs:5888`): the #1051 objective-stall fixed point where the affine-invariant Newton-decrement certificate (`:5849`, #2226) did **not** confirm stationarity AND the undamped evidence factorization failed at the stall point, for `consecutive_stall_factor_fail ≥` the min-rounds threshold.

### Case A — synthetic circle, p=8, K=1 → **Branch 1, a genuine inner non-convergence**
`‖g‖ = 1.37e2`, `tol = 3.45e-4` ⇒ `iterate_scale ≈ 34.5`, so the residual is ~4× the iterate scale and ~7 orders above the 1e-5 relative tol. This is **not** a metric / conditioning-floor plateau. Decisively, the message reports **raw `‖g‖` == quotient `‖Π⊥gauge g‖` == 1.37e2** — the gauge projection removed nothing — and the circle's rotational gauge **is** deflated (`AtomTopology::Circle → SaeAtomBasisKind::Periodic`, gauge arm at `fit_drivers.rs:1474`). So the 137 lives in the **identifiable** subspace: the damped inner Newton (`run_joint_fit_arrow_schur`, `fit_drivers.rs:4133` → `solve_with_lm_escalation_inner` + the quotient trust-region gate `:4442`) parks at a non-stationary iterate within budget on a clean, trivially-fittable circle.

This is the near-singular-reduced-Hessian / weakly-identified-direction inner-solve genus (**#1094 / #1051**), **not** the #2226 affine-tolerance axis: #2226 only shifts the acceptance point by a couple of digits at the conditioning floor (its own comment describes arm64-vs-x86 parking "a couple of digits apart"); it cannot close a 137-vs-3.4e-4 gap. It is also not the #2080 outer-criterion-cost axis.

Two candidate sub-roots I could not disambiguate without a runnable build (the installed extension is stale — missing `sae_default_ibp_concentration_for_k_atoms` — and the reported wheel 0.1.250 predates #2144):
1. **LM over-damping** — the LM ridge / trust-region shrinks the step in the identifiable descent direction so `‖g‖` cannot be closed within the refine budget; or
2. **objective↔gradient inconsistency** — the (majorized/assembled) Hessian used for the step and the measured gradient `gt/gb` disagree, so Newton does not drive `‖g‖ → 0` (the recurring objective↔gradient-desync class). Note the stall detector's value is `loss.total()` (`construction.rs:5769`), which still **excludes** the separation barrier / decoder-repulsion / analytic penalties that the measured `‖g‖` **includes** — a desync signature to check (at K=1 the barrier is inactive, but decoder-repulsion / analytic incoherence are not).

Decisive next step: a debug build logging, per refine round on this fixture, `‖g‖`, the LM ridge actually applied, the trust-region radius vs the taken step norm, and whether `loss.total()` is still decreasing while `‖g‖` is flat (the desync tell).

### Case B — Qwen residual acts, p=4096, stagewise → **Branch 2, gated by undamped-evidence-factorization failure**
Here `‖g‖ = 12.7` (much smaller) and the refusal is specifically "the undamped evidence factorization failed at each stall point." That factorization is the cross-row IBP evidence Schur, which **#2144** (`e1f621564`, "IBP PSD majorization is UNCONDITIONAL — one operator for assembly, evidence, rho-trace, and theta-adjoint") now makes PD **by construction** (clamp `cross_row_d ≥ 0` at `construction.rs:7034` + `ibp_psd_majorized_hdiag`). `e1f621564` landed **after** wheel 0.1.250, so this case is plausibly already relieved on HEAD: once the undamped factor succeeds, the affine-invariant #2226 Newton-decrement certificate (`construction.rs:5849`) can evaluate and **accept** the fixed point rather than refuse. This matches this issue's own note ("after `e1f621564` the ibp_map lane that previously died inside these stalls now *evaluates* — worth re-testing the p=4096 repro"). **This case needs a HEAD re-run, not a new fix.**

### Ownership + fix status
- **Case B**: likely already improved by #2144 (landed) + #2226 (affine criterion, in-progress). Re-test the p=4096 / synthetic repro on HEAD (≥ `e1f621564`); owned by the #2226 verify lane. No new code needed unless it still refuses.
- **Case A**: the genuine unowned residual — inner-solve globalization/consistency on the K=1 circle in the identifiable subspace. Same root family as **#1094** (near-singular inner solve emitting a spurious refusal despite a good fit). Recommend homing Case A under the #1094 / inner-solve lane with the `sae_manifold_fit(K=1, atom_topology="circle", p=8)` fixture as the minimal diagnostic.

**Not implemented.** The candidate fix sites (`construction.rs` inner-solve loop, `fit_drivers.rs` `run_joint_fit`/LM, `outer_objective.rs`) are all under concurrent edits by other agents right now, and disambiguating the Case-A sub-root (over-damping vs desync) requires a runnable build — a blind edit would collide and would be guessing between two roots. Diagnosis-only.


--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-08T16:04:52Z ---
## Single root uniting #1095 and #2228: the inner-solve acceptance certificate is gated behind an UNDAMPED (ridge-0) factorization that rank-deficient circle geometry makes fail by construction

Cross-linking **#1095** and **#2228** — same root. Minimal repro (thanks to the #1095 measurement on wheel 0.1.251): `sae_manifold_fit(standard_normal(180,32), K=1, d_atom=2, atom_topology="circle", n_iter=30)` → `RemlConvergenceError: … objective stalled for 3 consecutive refine rounds (‖g‖=2.76e1, tol 8.88e-5) and the undamped evidence factorization failed at each stall point`, EV≈0.11.

### The gating bug, line by line (`crates/gam-sae/src/manifold/construction.rs`)
The inner-solve stall handler tries to *accept* a stalled iterate via a stationarity certificate, but the whole certificate lives inside an `if let Ok(...)` on an **undamped** solve:

```
if stalled && refine_rounds >= MIN_ROUNDS {
    let stationary_sys = assemble_arrow_schur(...)?;                       // :5796
    if let Ok((dt, db, cache)) =
        solve_arrow_newton_step_with_options(&stationary_sys, 0.0, 0.0, options) {  // :5799  UNDAMPED (ridge_t=0, ridge_beta=0)
        // grad-norm acceptance ....................................... :5814  Ok(cache)
        // affine-invariant Newton-decrement ½λ² acceptance (#2226) ... :5862  Ok(cache)
        // else: fall through, keep refining (no refusal)
    }
    // reached ONLY when the undamped solve returned Err:
    consecutive_stall_factor_fail += 1;                                   // :5886
    if consecutive_stall_factor_fail >= MIN_ROUNDS {
        return Err("… the undamped evidence factorization failed at each stall point …"); // :5888
    }
}
```

The undamped solve factors the per-row `H_tt^(i)` blocks at `ridge_t = 0` (`probe_undamped_evidence_row_factors` → `factor_blocks_for_system(sys, 0.0, …)`, `crates/gam-solve/src/arrow_schur/newton_step.rs:254-280`). **For a circle those blocks are rank-deficient by construction:**
- a circle is intrinsically 1-D, so a `d_atom=2` latent (the #1095/#2228 repro) gives every per-row `H_tt^(i)` a structural rank-1 null direction (the radial mode) → the `ridge_t=0` per-row Cholesky fails; and
- a near-perfect circle sits in a rank-~3 ambient subspace, so the evidence border β-Schur is also near-singular (that one is floored at `newton_step.rs:133`, but the per-row factor is the un-rescued one).

So on exactly the geometry these tests probe, the undamped solve **can never succeed at the true optimum**, the `if let Ok` is never entered, and the code hard-refuses at `:5888` — even though the iterate is the legitimate optimum of degenerate geometry (`‖g‖=27.6` cannot fall to `8.88e-5` because that floor is set by the rank-deficient conditioning). This is why a *clean synthetic circle* — the easiest possible target — fails.

### Why prior landings did not fix it
- **#2144** (`e1f621564`, unconditional IBP PSD majorization) makes the *assembly/evidence* operator PD, but the failing factor here is the **per-row `H_tt` at ridge 0**, not the cross-row capacitance — so #2144 does not touch it. (Confirmed: repro still fails on 0.1.251, which postdates #2144.)
- **#2226**'s affine-invariant Newton-decrement certificate (`:5862`) is exactly the right acceptance test — but it is **downstream of the undamped `if let Ok`**, so it is never reached when the undamped factor fails. #2226 as currently wired cannot rescue rank-deficient geometry.
- The Rust pin `sae_manifold_small_n_circle_seed_accept.rs` stays green because it drives a **different** entry (`OuterProblem::run` with hand-tuned ridges `1e-6`, `INNER_MAX_ITER=50`) — the non-zero ridge makes the per-row factor succeed, masking the public-FFI ridge-0 failure.

### Fix direction (principled; needs a build to validate)
Decouple the acceptance certificate from the undamped-factor-success bit. Concretely: compute the stationarity certificate (grad-norm + affine Newton-decrement ½λ²) from a **spectrally-deflated / minimally-ridged** factorization that unit-deflates the structural per-row null directions — the *same* `factor_dense_reduced_schur(…, options.schur_pd_floor, unit_deflate=true)` / deflation convention the evidence log-det already uses for collapsed directions — so ½λ² is evaluated on the identifiable subspace and the degenerate-geometry optimum is **accepted** (½λ²/scale ≤ `SAE_MANIFOLD_INNER_OBJECTIVE_STALL_REL_TOL`) instead of hard-refused. Keep the undamped per-row factor as the #2080 infeasible-ρ *probe signal*, but it must not be a **precondition** for evaluating the certificate. (An over-parametrized latent `d_atom > intrinsic_dim` is a legitimate, common configuration; the fit should return the best incumbent on the deflated identifiable subspace, not refuse.)

### Ownership / status
Same certificate the **#2226** affine-invariant-criterion lane owns — recommend that lane lands the decoupling (it already added the `:5862` λ² test; this extends it to fire when the undamped factor fails). **Not implemented here:** `construction.rs` and `fit_drivers.rs` are under concurrent edit by other agents right now, and validating an inner-solve/certificate change requires a build (this box is Darwin-arm64; the manylinux wheel can't run locally). Diagnosis + surgical spec only. Treat #1095 and #2228 as one issue for the fix.


--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-08T16:25:19Z ---
## Fix landed (commit 37e4d2eae) — stall-acceptance certificates decoupled from undamped-factor success

### Root cause
`converge_inner_for_undamped_logdet` (`construction.rs`) accepts the converged inner `(t,β)` optimum at an objective-stall fixed point via two certificates — the KKT grad-norm (~:5814) and the #2226 affine Newton-decrement ½λ² (~:5862) — **both computed only inside** `if let Ok(..) = solve_arrow_newton_step_with_options(&stationary_sys, 0.0, 0.0, options)`.

An over-parametrized chart — `d_atom=2` on intrinsically 1-D circular data — plants a **rank-1 radial null in every per-row `H_tt`** (all rows sit on the unit circle in the latent plane, so scaling the radius is unpopulated). The per-row spectral deflation that rescues such a null (`factor_spectral_deflated_evidence_row`) is only enabled when `sys.row_gauge_deflation.is_some()` (`newton_step.rs:1305/1335`); the generic path uses `factor_one_row(..., allow_spectral_deflation=false)`. When the assembled stationary system's `row_gauge_deflation` is `None`, the ridge-0 factor is non-PD **by construction**, the whole `if let Ok(..)` is skipped, every certificate is bypassed, and the fit is refused to the non-convergence sentinel → public `sae_manifold_fit` K=1 circle returns `GamError` at every N.

### Fix
Before the stall-acceptance factorization, ensure the stationary evidence system opts into per-row spectral discovery — install an empty-per-row `row_gauge_deflation` (the same #974 low-rank-whiten seam). The rank-1 radial null is then unit-stiffness deflated (`log 1 = 0`, ρ-independent), so the ridge-0 factor is PD-by-deflation, the log-det is finite, and the affine ½λ² is measured on the **identifiable tangent subspace** (the deflated null contributes a bounded step, not a Schur-amplified blow-up). A full-rank block has no eigenvalue below the spectral floor and is returned bit-for-bit unchanged, so healthy fits are untouched — this only makes acceptance **reachable** on a rank-deficient chart. The undamped (non-deflated) per-row verdict remains the #2080 infeasible-ρ probe on the loop `sys`, unchanged — a probe signal, not an acceptance gate.

This builds on the #1094 fix (dbdb20d27), which ranks the finite deflated cache at the persistent-stall threshold when the certificates don't fire; together they make the over-parametrized circle return a best-incumbent fit on the deflated subspace instead of aborting.

### Test
`tests/sae/sae/sae_manifold_circle_d2_ridge0_fits.rs`: a d=2 Euclidean chart on a planted circle at `RIDGE_EXT_COORD = 0.0` (the sibling circle pins mask this path with a hand `1e-6` ridge) must return a fit with a finite criterion, driven through `OuterProblem::run` and re-checked via `reml_criterion` at the converged ρ. The green `sae_manifold_small_n_circle_seed_accept.rs` (hand ridge) is left in place beside it.

### Verification owed
Uncompiled (agent doesn't build). Needs `./build.sh` + the new ridge-0 fixture green on MSI, plus regression on the sibling circle pins and the #1094 set. Close #1095 + #2228 together once MSI passes.


--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-08T16:33:06Z ---
## Precise root cause: the rotation-gauge push is floored by decoded-derivative magnitude

Refining the earlier "undamped per-row factor is non-PD **by construction**" framing to the exact gate that lets it happen.

Per-row spectral deflation — the mechanism that unit-stiffens a rank-1 radial null so the ridge-0 evidence factor is PD — is only enabled when the assembled system carries a `row_gauge_deflation` (`newton_step.rs`: `factor_blocks_for_system` takes the deflating branch iff `sys.row_gauge_deflation.is_some()`; the generic path calls `factor_one_row(..., allow_spectral_deflation = false)`).

That deflation is installed from `row_gauge_deflation_for_layout`, which pushes an atom's rotation/phase gauge **only when the decoded tangent clears a hard floor**:

- `fit_drivers.rs:1581` (Linear/Euclidean/Duchon/Poincaré) and `:1597` (Periodic/Torus): `if tangent·tangent <= 1.0e-24 { continue; }`
- the tangent is `tangent = decoder_coefficients × basis_jacobian` (`atom.rs:1543`, `fill_decoded_derivative_row`).

So an axis whose **decoder curvature is sub-threshold** contributes no gauge — and that is exactly the structurally-flat radial axis of an over-parametrized (d_atom=2 on intrinsic 1-D) chart, or any cold/zero-decoder seed. When every row/axis is sub-threshold, `row_gauge_deflation_for_layout` returns `None`, and the only fallback — `low_rank_whiten` (`= whitens_likelihood && w_dim < p`, `construction_arrow_schur_assembly.rs:667/2363`) — is `false` for a plain circle. Net: assemble installs **no** `row_gauge_deflation` → `allow_spectral_deflation = false` → the ridge-0 per-row Cholesky refuses the radial null → every stall-acceptance certificate is skipped → `GamError`.

This is a genuine config-dependent exclusion of the public default path (`atom_topology="circle"` ⇒ `SaeAtomBasisKind::Periodic`, `latent_basis_and_sae_ffi.rs:1633`), not a numerical accident.

## Design decision (on record)

The fix (37e4d2eae) installs the empty-per-row deflation **acceptance-locally** — only on the stall-block stationary system used to compute the grad-norm and affine ½λ² certificates — rather than assembly-wide. Assembly-wide would also flip the **undamped** per-row verdict that `probe_undamped_evidence_row_factors` uses as the #2080 infeasible-ρ probe signal, changing what "this ρ is infeasible" means. Keeping it local preserves the #2080 probe semantics (undamped = probe signal) while making acceptance reachable on a rank-deficient chart. Undamped stays a probe, never an acceptance precondition.
