--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-10T14:56:02Z ---
### Root-cause audit: current scale “gauge” is not objective-invariant

While tracing the fixed-ρ convergence failure against `SPEC.md`, I found a structural inconsistency in the current quotient path:

- reconstruction uses the physical decoder `exp(s_k) · Φ_k · B_k`;
- the code treats `(B_k, s_k) -> (c B_k, s_k - log c)` as an exact gauge;
- but decoder smoothness is evaluated/assembled as `½ λ_k <B_k, S_k B_k>`, without the required `exp(2 s_k)` physical-scale factor.

Therefore the gauge pin/normalization can change the penalized objective even though it leaves reconstruction fixed, and it currently runs at an accepted-iteration boundary outside the Newton/line-search model. The separate SCAD/ARD amplitude solve and hard amplitude clamp compound that mismatch. This is a plausible direct cause of the fixed-ρ gradient refusal/co-collapse: value, gradient, curvature, and boundary retraction are not all describing one objective.

The exact final-function roughness for `γ_k(t)=exp(s_k) Φ_k(t)B_k` is `½ λ_k exp(2s_k)<B_k,S_kB_k>`, which is invariant on that gauge orbit. I am auditing every loss/gradient/Hessian/REML channel before landing the correction; current MSI verification at main SHA `770ffff4a` is still running.

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-10T15:15:41Z ---
### Root model correction landed: ordered IBP prior is no longer multiplied into reconstruction

The capped-gate mechanism was applying the ordered IBP prior twice:

1. forward reconstruction used `a_ik = sigmoid(logit_ik / tau) * mu_k`;
2. the Beta--Bernoulli assignment penalty separately scores the same ordered `mu_k`.

At `K=1, alpha=1`, this made the final function unable to use an activation above 0.5 even at posterior inclusion probability one. That forced the decoder/amplitude rescaling workaround and created the penalty/gauge mismatch described above.

Main now uses the Bernoulli posterior mean `a_ik = sigmoid(logit_ik / tau)` for the final function. Ordered shrinkage is applied once, in the empirical-Bayes IBP prior. Matching Rust row/batch values, logit Jacobians, row-jet scaling, learnable-alpha data derivatives (now exactly zero), PyO3, and Torch signatures were updated together. New terms also keep physical magnitude in decoder coefficients; the old scale peel is disabled by default and removed from cold/stagewise seeds.

This is pushed in the current main checkpoint (`d19b6b26e` plus follow-up checkpoint work). CPU convergence regressions are still compiling, so this is a model/root-cause update rather than closure evidence.

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-10T16:07:47Z ---
Root-cause cleanup is now on main through ed6a1bafd.

The ordered IBP prior was previously entering twice: once as a multiplicative prior-mean cap in the forward gate and again in the empirical-Bayes prior. The forward map is now the posterior mean sigmoid(logit / temperature); ordered shrinkage lives only in the prior.

I also removed the redundant decoder-scale channel end-to-end: quotient_scale, log_amplitude, cone recovery, its SCAD/ARD boundary solve, scale-Schur pinning, transport/refit peels, persistence/FFI fields, and tests of that obsolete representation. Physical magnitude now has one owner, the decoder B, so smoothness and data fit optimize the same coefficients and there is no (B,s) orbit for the solver/evidence to disagree about. The checkpoint schema is deliberately bumped to v2 rather than silently accepting the removed state.

Focused compilation and the fixed-rho K=1 acceptance are still running; this is implementation/root-cause evidence, not yet a close verdict.

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-11T16:00:11Z ---
## Inner-solve wall, measured on real data 2026-07-11 — the fix cluster helped 170×, residual O(1) floor remains

Fresh log-confirmed measurements (GHA validate-one, real `running 1 test` runs, not phantom filters) that localize this issue precisely and consolidate it with the rest of the SAE cluster.

### The number moved a lot, but hasn't crossed the line
On the current-main fix cluster (gain-ratio LM `94107de3b` + one-referee guard `bbd21f35f` + structured-residual floor `8703ff6db` + recent), the inner KKT gradient at the stalled fixed-ρ point:

| config | rows | regime | ‖g‖ | tol | ratio | run |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 48-row K=4 | 48 | near-exact (params≈data) | **241.68** | 4.50e-2 | 5400× | 29142274958 |
| 600-row #2015 gate | 600 | high-residual (params≪data) | **1.4101** | 2.76e-3 | 510× | 29144079962 |

The structured-residual floor + cluster took ‖g‖ from **241 → 1.41 (~170×)** once measured in the correct regime. What remains is an **O(1) residual floor** the inner solve can't push below ~1.4 in 1050 iterations.

### Three findings that sharpen this issue
1. **It is genuinely the INNER solve, not the outer certification.** Confirmed independently by two lanes on unrelated configs: (a) the 600-row behavior fit above, and (b) a 12-factor zoo fit that ground for **8 hours with zero result rows and zero "restoring incumbent" lines** — i.e. the outer recurrent-incumbent certificate never even engages; the stall is upstream, in the inner θ-solve.
2. **It is NOT a gauge-nullspace issue.** raw ‖g‖ and gauge-projected ‖Π⊥gauge g‖ are near-identical (1.4101 vs 1.3876) — the projection removes ~0.02 of mass, so the stuck gradient is essentially all in physical directions.
3. **It is (per current evidence) NOT a gradient-formula desync.** The sibling #2253 stall was re-forensically shown to have a CORRECT gradient formula — the earlier "adjoint desync" was a buggy-FD artifact of auditing at an *under-converged inner budget* (the FD→analytic gap shrank 0.687→0.087→2e-5 as the budget grew). Since ‖g‖=1.41 has the same O(1)-stuck shape, the working hypothesis is inner non-convergence, not a wrong term.

### Methodology note (cost us a retracted verdict — worth recording)
A convergence repro **must be in-regime**. The 48-row K=4 config has decoder params `K·M·p ≈ 3748` vs `48·127 = 6096` data cells → near-exact/overparameterized → singular-whitening degeneracy, which is a *different* failure (that's what the structured-residual floor targets) and misleads by ~two orders of magnitude (241 vs 1.41). Use `params ≪ data` (high-residual) configs to probe the real wall.

### Decisive experiment in flight
An inner-budget trajectory probe (`tests_inner_budget_trajectory_2015`, budgets 10→1280 on an in-regime ~200-row K=4 config) plus a **trap-immune direct FD** of the inner penalized objective (does not route through a resolve, so it can't be fooled by under-convergence like the #2253 audit was). The single decisive question: does ‖g‖ **floor** (genuine wall → guarded envelope-accept à la #2253's railed-ρ handoff, gated on SPEC's "fit minted only after certified convergence", OR a stronger inner step — trust-region/2nd-order/reconditioner) or **keep dropping** (just under-budgeted → raise the cap). Will post the trajectory table here when it lands.

This issue is the canonical home of the SAE cluster's shared root: ~13 open issues (the SAE cluster + the zoo trio, whose fixes have landed but whose R² bars are blocked here) funnel through this one inner-solve wall.


--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-11T16:03:55Z ---
## ROOT CAUSE (2026-07-11): inner-solver instability, not a gradient bug and not a genuine floor — fix = monotone-descent globalization

The decisive inner-budget-trajectory + trap-immune-FD probe landed (GHA run `29156684764`, real `running 1 test`, in-regime ~200-row K=4, n=200 p_out=8 K=4 beta_dim=96). Two tables settle it.

### Trajectory: ‖g‖ vs inner budget (does it floor, or keep dropping?)
```
budget |  ‖g‖ (raw)   | ‖Π⊥gauge g‖  |  Δ
   10  | 6.789699e1  | 6.789642e1  |  —
   20  | 1.713341e1  | 1.713282e1  | -5.076e1
   40  | 2.210699e1  | 2.210654e1  | +4.974e0    ← bounce up
   80  | 2.887145e8  | 2.887145e8  | +2.887e8    ← CATASTROPHIC OVERSHOOT
  160  | 1.146095e-1 | 1.146094e-1 | -2.887e8    ← recovery
  320  | 8.117427e-3 | 8.117349e-3 |
  640  | 8.473214e-3 | 8.473090e-3 | +3.558e-4   ← bounce up
 1280  | 2.253657e-3 | 2.253070e-3 | -6.220e-3   ← BELOW the 2.76e-3 production tol
```

Two conclusions:
1. **No genuine floor.** ‖g‖ reaches **2.25e-3 at budget 1280**, below the production tolerance 2.76e-3. The solver *can* reach tol given enough (stable) iterations — so this is NOT a genuine constrained optimum, and **envelope-aware acceptance is ruled out** as the fix.
2. **Catastrophic step instability.** ‖g‖ spikes to **2.887e8** at budget 80 (an 8-order-of-magnitude overshoot) then recovers, with additional non-monotone bounces (17→22, 8.1e-3→8.5e-3). A step that raised the objective by 2.887e8 was **committed** — the descent is not monotone.

### Trap-immune inner-FD (direct central FD of the inner penalized objective wrt θ,β — does not route through a resolve, so it can't be fooled by under-convergence like the earlier #2253 audit was)
```
COORD gt:   worst abs_err 2.48e-8  (analytic 1.76e-12 vs fd -3.55e-9 — both ~0)
DECODER gb: worst rel_err 6.0e-2 at abs_err 6.46e-9 (analytic 6.01e-8 vs fd 6.39e-8 — both ~0)
VERDICT: analytic == FD ⇒ inner gradient CORRECT
```
The discrepancies are at absolute magnitudes of 1e-8 (both gradients ~0 at the converged iterate); the 6% "rel_err" is a small-denominator artifact. **The gradient formula is correct** — consistent with the #2253 re-forensics.

### Root cause + fix
The keystone `RemlConvergenceError` is an **inner-solver globalization/stability failure**: the Gauss-Newton/Newton step overshoots catastrophically (2.887e8) and is *accepted* rather than rejected — the current gain-ratio Levenberg ridge (`94107de3b`) is not gating step acceptance on actual descent (it appears to adjust the ridge for the *next* iterate rather than reject the bad step in-place). The production 600-row failure (‖g‖=1.41 after 1050 iters) is the same instability at larger scale — it simply hasn't recovered from an overshoot within the iteration cap.

**Fix:** enforce monotone descent on the inner step — a trust-region or backtracking line-search that rejects any step which does not reduce the penalized objective (gain-ratio ρ>0), backtracking/growing the ridge *within* the iterate before committing. Success criterion: the trajectory becomes monotone (no 2.887e8 spike), reaches tol in far fewer iterations, and the production `qwen_real_activation_behavior_fit` certifies. That unlocks the SAE cluster + zoo trio gated here.

Fix in progress; will post the re-run trajectory when it lands.


--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-11T18:25:22Z ---
## Root cause closed out — the repair design is landed on main (12 commits, 2026-07-11 PM)

The trajectory data on this issue pointed at 'a committed non-descent step'; a full static audit of the inner loop (four deep passes over fit_drivers / construction_reml_evidence / outer_objective / gam-solve) shows **every returned step was already a descent direction** — the Armijo lane and the proximal fallback both gate on strict decrease, and all solve matrices are PD-forced. The 2.887e8 event is a **gradient spike at an objective-good iterate**, produced by the unguarded post-accept collapse reseeds whose per-atom budget was reset on every evidence refine re-entry (`collapse_events.clear()` per re-entry ⇒ ~one reseed per refine round). The real wall is an (algorithm-class, tolerance) mismatch: the inner solver is majorized Gauss–Newton (GN data block + Loewner/Gershgorin/ARD-clamp majorizers + LM), which is linearly convergent with contraction 0.9965–0.9979/iter in exactly the production regime (high residual + O(n) flat bands) ⇒ ~1,800–3,000 uninterrupted iterations to close ‖g‖ 1.41 → 2.76e-3 against a ~1,050 budget. Refusal was deterministic; no guard tuning could change it.

**What landed:**
- `0f546940e` — reseed ledger scoped per criterion evaluation (persists across refine rounds); the three collapse guards quiesce once ‖g‖ ≤ 10×tol·scale. Kills the spike generator and the progress-budget collapse.
- `4d8c913a7` — stall detector prices `penalized_objective_total` (one scalar for progress/descent/stationarity; it previously watched `loss.total()`, a function nobody optimizes).
- `7763e8478` — **terminal exact-Newton phase**: at the objective-stall plateau the iterate is handed to bounded Newton steps on the exact Hessian A = B + ΔC, solved by the same B-preconditioned gauge-quotient GMRES the outer IFT already uses. Accept = strict ‖g‖ contraction + objective inside the stall band; snapshot-restore on failure; mints nothing (the loop-top KKT gate + idempotence certificate remain sole authority). This converts the ~10³-iteration MM tail into O(10) Newton steps, making the strict KKT contract **reachable instead of loosened**.
- `d67d341c0` — Tier-0 input standardization at the one fit entry ((Z−μ)/σ, exact fold-back, FFI-exported σ): attacks the measured κ≈1e8 that sets the linear rate in the first place.
- `78775cf05` — the `stationary_window_paid` escalation arm deleted: it existed to grind out hook-injected motion at KKT-band iterates, which no longer occurs.

**Acceptance gates** (from the design doc): trajectory probe monotone after the hook fixes; tolerance in ≤150 inner iterations; the 600-row #2015 gate and 42×41 K=1 circle certify through the default entry. Validation is running on MSI; the first pass already compiles clean under -D warnings. One live signal under triage: `inner_gradient_matches_penalized_objective_fd_2015` failed at an intermediate SHA — details being pulled with full output (job 13005149).

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-11T19:02:37Z ---
**Empirical update — the FD-2015 'blow-up' is a pre-existing divergence, and the fix is a coverage hole, not a guard.**

Bisect (MSI job 13005595): `inner_gradient_matches_penalized_objective_fd_2015` fails **bit-for-bit identically at the pre-repair baseline** `0223807ab` (same iterate ‖g‖=3.284991e27, obj=3.781293e12) — none of the repair stack caused it. At that state the FD is numerically vacuous (Δobj per ε-perturbation ≪ ulp(3.78e12) ⇒ FD literally 0 against nonzero analytic entries), so the test's 'desync' verdict is an artifact of the divergence, not a gradient-formula bug.

**Root cause of the divergence itself:** the wide-p K=4 fixture activates Grassmann frames (p ≥ 12), and both the sweep engine and the #1026 decoder-LSQ polish it grew from **skip frames-active fits entirely** (the LSQ writes full-B). So on most *real* fits — exactly the wide-p production regime — the 640-iteration walk ran with no exact decoder reset anywhere on its path, and nothing interrupted a decoder-block runaway (blown entries are all in `gb`).

**Fix landed** (`c3f3c3c40`): frames-aware sweeps — each decoder-LSQ is followed by the closed-form frame re-polar (`refresh_active_frames_from_data`: thin SVD + B←(BU)Uᵀ, the same primitives frame activation uses), keeping the factored border consistent; the round stays one strict-decrease transaction so a lossy re-projection reverts (never worse than the old skip). Combined with the sweep-first engine order (`2e178664f`), every fit — including p≥12 — now gets an exact penalized decoder argmin at entry, per round, and post-loop. Verification of the fixture at HEAD is queued (job 13006032 at `1017cf314` pre-frames-fix as control, then re-run at `c3f3c3c40`).

`inner_gradient_matches_penalized_objective_fd_2015`: **ok, 1 passed** at `b8c64cc7d` (MSI job 13006095, 171 s), vs the bit-for-bit-reproducible failure at the pre-repair baseline `0223807ab` (640-iteration walk diverging to ‖g‖=3.284991e27; bisect job 13005595). --- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-11T22:19:40Z ---
## Run-to-run nondeterminism CONFIRMED — the inner trajectory is not a function of (code, data, machine, threads)

Controlled ladder on the fd_2015 fixture, all at verified fresh binaries of the same SHA:

| config | final inner ‖g‖ | verdict |
|---|---|---|
| MSI, 32 threads | 2.76e-3 → tol | **converged** |
| A10, 30 threads | 3.64e23 | diverged |
| A10, 32 threads (same binary) | 4.05e27 | diverged, different trajectory |
| A10, 32 threads, **re-run of the identical binary** | **3.81e30** (obj 6.65e14) | diverged, a FOURTH distinct trajectory |

Same binary + same box + same thread count ⇒ different endpoint: **rayon work-stealing changes FP reduction split points per run**, so the penalized objective/gradient sums differ in the last ulps each evaluation, and on this ill-conditioned fixture the inner walk amplifies that into completely different basins. This retroactively explains a whole genus of 'flaky' history: cross-machine plateau differences (#2226), CI-vs-local mysteries, and irreproducible refusals.

**Audit target (next fix):** the unordered `par_iter` reductions in the fit hot path — first candidate the fused per-row decode+residual data-fit reduction (`SAE_LOSS_PARALLEL_ROW_MIN` fan-out in `loss_scaled`), plus any assembly-side parallel sums. Fix shape: deterministic reduction (store per-row partials, then a fixed-order sequential/pairwise sum) — O(n) extra memory, bit-identical across runs/threads/machines by construction, and it makes the determinism claims true rather than per-run-lucky. Divergence-endpoint chart attached to the session records (rendered from this table).

**Determinism probe verdict (A10, run-twice, same binary/box/threads — closes the "machine divergence" question):**

```
RUN1: [2015-INNERFD] iterate ‖g‖=3.808261e30  base_obj=6.654588e14
RUN2: [2015-INNERFD] iterate ‖g‖=1.087989e29  base_obj=2.255061e13
```

Same test binary (`gam_sae-6158cca33c26fda9`, pinned 124c13df8), same host, same RAYON thread count, back-to-back. The fd_2015 trajectory is **run-to-run nondeterministic** — the earlier MSI-green vs A10-red split was never a machine/config variable; it is nondeterministic parallel float reduction (rayon work-stealing reduce grouping) feeding a trajectory that is chaotically sensitive at the crawl iterates.

Two consequences:
1. **Determinism bug**: `gam-solve` still has raw `into_par_iter().map(..).sum()` / `fold(..).reduce(..)` float reductions in pirls/deviance.rs (all non-Gaussian deviances + logliks), pirls/dispersion.rs, inference/alo.rs, reml/assembly.rs, reml/gradient_hessian.rs, pirls/low_rank.rs — while the codebase already has the bit-reproducible `gam_linalg::pairwise_reduce` contract used by streaming_border/evidence. Fix in flight: a parallel deterministic pairwise reduction (rayon::join over the same length-only tree, bit-identical to `pairwise_sum`) and conversion of every site.
2. **Robustness datum**: a divergent basin (‖g‖→1e29–1e30) is reachable by the inner engine from the fd_2015 start depending on ulp-level reduction noise — MSI's particular schedule dodges it. Determinism will make the failure reproducible; the basin itself is the remaining engine defect.

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-11T23:17:52Z ---
## MECHANISM CONFIRMED: every 'nondeterministic/divergent trajectory' was the silently-engaged DEVICE solve lane

**The falsification test** (fd_2015 on the A10, `CUDA_VISIBLE_DEVICES=\"\"`, two runs): trajectories **bit-identical to 17 digits** (`it=639 g=4.16067840990153558e-3` in both) **and the test PASSES** — on the same box that produced six wildly different diverging trajectories (‖g‖ from 12.7 to 3.8e30) with the GPU visible.

**The mechanism, from source** (fit_drivers.rs step-solve seam → `prepare_sae_resident_frame` → `build_resident_sae_frame_if_admitted`, gated on `sys.device_sae_pcg`, attached in `construction_arrow_schur_assembly.rs` whenever the framed isotropic path has device frame blocks): on a CUDA host the inner Newton SOLVE runs the device lane — a different arithmetic engine than host faer, with run-varying reduction order on device. Hence: MSI (no CUDA) = host = deterministic green; A10 = device = host-divergent AND run-nondeterministic; iteration-0 gradients bit-identical (assembly is host-side) with divergence born at the first solve. `RAYON_NUM_THREADS=1` never touched it — it governs the CPU pool.

**Consequences:** (1) the parallelism-invariance / bit-exactness contracts are host-only claims today — the backend boundary is crossed silently, so CI/local/box comparisons were never measuring one system; (2) worse than noise: the device-lane trajectories don't just differ, they DIVERGE to ‖g‖~1e23–1e30 on this fixture while host converges — the device solve path needs its own correctness audit, not just determinism work.

**Fix design** (general, not a patch): (a) backend routing becomes a DECLARED pure function of (shape, config), pinned per fit and honesty-flagged on the report — the `EncodePath` pattern extended to the solve lane; (b) device kernels feeding trajectories use deterministic tree reductions (no atomic-float accumulation), or the device lane is quarantined from evidence/certification lanes; (c) a run-twice bit-identity gate per backend goes into CI. Until (a–c) land, any GPU-host test red on this fixture class should be re-read as 'device lane engaged', not 'code regressed'.

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-12T07:20:15Z ---
**wheel13 real-GPT-2 attempt (full fix stack) — the mint blocker is now isolated to a specific mechanism, and it is NOT determinism.**

Two consecutive real-GPT-2 attempts (wheel12, wheel13) failed identically at the outer certification with the same signature:
```
BFGS line-search failed in 1 iter, reason=StepSizeTooSmall (max_attempts=50)
cost-only value        2.6250956094e3
disagrees with
analytic-sample value  2.6582460242e3   (roundoff bound 3.96e-5; they differ by 0.033 ≈ 1.26%)
→ RemlConvergenceError, no mint
```

**Diagnosis (root cause isolated):** the ~1.26% gap is **6 orders of magnitude too large to be floating-point/reduction-order nondeterminism** — so it is NOT the determinism class the deterministic-reduction stack addressed (that class, the ~2.8e-2 at-scale cost-vs-analytic FP desync, IS fixed by the schur-matvec → `par_deterministic_block_fold` conversion this session; verified). The 1.26% is a genuine **two-closure objective divergence**: the SAE-manifold outer objective evaluates its cost via two different inner drives —
- BFGS's line-search value path → `ProbeInnerDrive::LineSearchProbe` → `line_search_probe_criterion` (returns 2.625),
- the certification's analytic sample → `ProbeInnerDrive::Criterion` → `penalized_quasi_laplace_criterion_with_refine_policy_and_lane` (returns 2.658).

Because 2.625 < 2.658 (the probe value is *lower*), the line-search value probe is **under-converging its inner solve** relative to the criterion/gradient drive, and the #2080(a) probe-converged-state handoff that is supposed to reconcile them at the accepted ρ is either missing (ρ-key mismatch at the certify boundary) or installing a capped state. At synthetic n≈100 both drives converge within budget so they agree (tier0 tests green); at real n=44000 the probe's truncated budget leaves real residual descent, exposing the gap. Fix in progress on the inner-drive reconciliation. The engine otherwise reaches real optimization on GPT-2 activations (18 bridge evals, cost 2.626→2.680 explored) — the remaining blocker is purely this value/certify closure agreement.


--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-12T07:46:02Z ---
## E1 fit rerun on gamfit-0.1.253 (Lambda A10) — new failure signature: cost-only vs analytic-sample objective desync at cert

Reran the E1 manifold fit (real GPT-2 layer-7 weekday activation cloud, PCA chart n=84×r=64, EV 0.9998, one periodic circle atom, softmax assignment) on the fresh **gamfit-0.1.253** wheel (built on the box 06:35, build commit includes all six overnight determinism commits `c152827…07e0c01` **and** the cost-stall marker fix `b89d18e`). This is the run after the wheel12 death (cost-only vs analytic-sample desync 2.8e-2 attributed to run-to-run rayon nondeterminism).

### Outcome: no mint. Died at cert with a *within-run* objective-path desync.

```
gamfit._rust.RemlConvergenceError: Outer smoothing-parameter optimization did not
certify a stationary optimum (SAE manifold): cost-only value 2.6250956094237768e3
disagrees with analytic-sample value 2.6582460241578578e3 at the selected point
(roundoff bound 3.961e-5) after 1 outer iteration(s); final objective 2.658246e3,
projected gradient norm 6.345e-1 against stationarity bound 2.659e-2.
resume rho_checkpoint = [1.0218641703510656, 1.0223275738686401].
```

**The desync numbers:**
| quantity | value |
|---|---|
| cost-only objective | 2.6250956094237768e3 |
| analytic-sample objective | 2.6582460241578578e3 |
| absolute disagreement | **3.315e1** |
| relative disagreement | **1.263e-2** |
| roundoff bound (cert tolerance) | 3.961e-5 |
| final projected‖g‖ | 6.345e-1 |
| stationarity bound | 2.659e-2 |

### Determinism keystone CONFIRMED FIXED (run-twice, bit-identical)

Ran the fit **twice** on the same wheel/box. Both runs die with the identical cert numbers to all 16 printed digits — cost-only `2.6250956094237768e3`, analytic-sample `2.6582460241578578e3`, same `rho_checkpoint = [1.0218641703510656, 1.0223275738686401]`; the escape-1/8 trajectory (`|g|=7.636e0, value=2.626102e3`) also matches to all digits (only wall-clock differs, from CPU contention). **The wheel12 run-to-run rayon nondeterminism (2.8e-2 drift) is gone** — the pairwise-doctrine commits worked. What remains is fully deterministic and reproducible.

### Root cause (traced): the cert value-agreement guard false-positives on a coarse value-lane terminal

I traced both values to source. **This is NOT a missing term** — both the "cost-only" and "analytic-sample" paths route through the same `penalized_quasi_laplace_criterion_with_cache_refine_policy`; the only difference is the `refine_progress_extension` flag:

- **analytic/gradient lane** (`_with_cache`, `refine_progress_extension = true`): base refine budget `16×`/min 64, progress-extended to `64×`/min 256 — drives the inner (t,β) solve to the settled fixed point → **2.658e3**.
- **value/probe lane** (`OuterEvalOrder::Value` line-search cost probe, `false`): base `4×`/min 16, no progress extension — stops ~16 refine iters short, giving a systematically *lower* criterion → **2.625e3**.

The ~1% gap is exactly the "strict Newton steps still move V by ~1% past the coarse-KKT band" behavior the code comments (`outer_objective.rs:2413`) already document. Critically, this value/gradient refine-policy difference is **contracted design**, not a defect: `sae_contract_probe_tests.rs:1042` explicitly asserts the value lane matches its *false-refine* bare and the gradient lane matches its *true-refine* bare, noting "the two bares may differ by the refine policy."

So the failure is at the **certification guard** (`gam-solve/src/rho_optimizer/run.rs:1537-1566`). When the outer BFGS terminates on a line-search failure (as here — `Line search failed at iter 1`), the solver's terminal `final_value` is the last **coarse Value-lane probe** (2.625e3). The cert then re-solves analytically (`eval_with_order(ValueAndGradient)` → true → 2.658e3) and rejects because the two differ beyond the `sqrt(eps)·|f|` roundoff bound (3.96e-5). But by the lane contract these values are *expected* to differ by the refine policy — the guard's tight bound cannot tolerate a legitimate coarse-vs-full inner-solve gap, so it false-positives. The guard already has a `transient_wall` skip for the analogous sentinel-vs-real case; the coarse-value-lane-terminal case needs the same treatment (adopt the analytic sample as authoritative and let the stationarity/Hessian gates judge it). That is a change to the stationary-only certification contract, so it is being handed to the contract owner rather than patched here.

### Why this is a different failure than wheel12's

This is **two evaluations of the REML objective at the *same* ρ disagreeing by 1.26e-2** — the fast cost-only path vs the analytic-sample path. That is ~320× the roundoff bound, far too large for floating-point drift, and it is measured within a single point evaluation, **not** run-to-run. So the overnight determinism fixes (which pinned rayon fold/reduce nondeterminism run-to-run) are working as intended but do not touch this: the two code paths compute the objective *differently* at the same point. This is the objective↔objective (cost-path vs analytic-path) desync class, localizable the same way the log|H| desync (#2087) and IFT-adjoint desync (#2253) were.

### Fit trajectory (the escape/cost-stall machinery IS working)

The `b89d18e` cost-stall marker fix and the repair-design escape hatch are behaving correctly on real data:

```
[5s]   checkpoint resume: banked incumbent (evals 45, best cost 2187.76)
[8s]   [OUTER] rejecting seed 0 before solver start: outer EFS eval non-finite cost
[3m37s][OUTER] rejecting seed 0 before solver start: outer eval non-finite cost
[5m09s][BFGS Adaptive] Strong Wolfe failed at iter 0 → Backtracking fallback
[5m11s][OUTER] cost-stall STUCK (NOT a flat valley): REML improved <1e-7 rel over
        6 accepted steps but |g|=7.636 >> escape threshold 1.5 → refusing to
        halt-and-ship, continuing descent (escape 1/8, value=2.626e3)
[7m34s][BFGS Adaptive] Strong Wolfe failed at iter 1 → Backtracking fallback
[9m03s][BFGS] Line search failed at iter 1 (nonfinite seen), fe=87, ge=18, Δ=3.85e-1
        → RemlConvergenceError (cert desync above)
```

The escape mechanism correctly refused to mint a stationary cert when ‖g‖ was above band — it is the **cost-path/analytic-path disagreement** that blocks the cert, not a premature halt. Recurring non-finite costs in the outer EFS eval (both at seed screening and inside the line search) are the upstream symptom feeding the desync.

### Wall time & GPU utilization

- **Fit wall ≈ 9–10 min** (vs wheel10's first-past-wall run). Cloud collection (GPT-2 forwards) ≈ 1 s.
- **GPU utilization: 0% for the entire fit.** GPT-2 is resident (~900 MiB) but forward passes fire only during cloud collection (112 short prompts, <1 s total). The manifold REML solver is 100% CPU (156 rayon threads, load avg ~23). At E1's problem size (n=84, r=64) the solver never engages the device path. **Data point for #1017:** GPU throughput is irrelevant at this scale — device-PCG would only engage on much larger clouds; the small-p refusal regime is entirely CPU-bound.


--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-12T09:35:36Z ---
## Correction + fix: the desync is Value-lane inner under-refinement, and it was clobbered once before it re-landed

**Correcting my earlier comment above** (the "cert value-agreement guard false-positive" attribution): that was wrong. The guard is fine. The real root cause, confirmed by tracing both evaluation paths:

The BFGS/ARC line-search cost probe (`OuterEvalOrder::Value`) and the analytic gradient/certification lane price the SAME `penalized_quasi_laplace_criterion` — they differ **only** by the `refine_progress_extension` flag, which sets the inner (t,β) refinement budget: the gradient/cert lane drives to the idempotent fixed point (`true`, 64×/min-256), while the line-search Value lane stopped at the coarse ranking budget (`false`, 4×/min-16). In the ill-conditioned regime (real GPT-2 activations, or wide-p over-smoothed) the coarse iterate sits ~1% off the fixed point, so:

1. no line-search step reduces the coarsely-ranked value while pointing down the analytic gradient → BFGS backtracks to `StepSizeTooSmall` at iteration 1;
2. the shipped coarse terminal value then fails the cert value-agreement gate against the analytic sample ("cost-only value disagrees with analytic-sample value").

This is **not** summation-order asymmetry (both paths call the identical function with identical reductions) and **not** a missing term. It's convergence-depth, which is why the gap scales with conditioning — 1.22× the roundoff bound on the small synthetic #2266 pytest, ~320× on real GPT-2 (E1). The contract test `ranking_and_gradient_lanes_match_bare_reml` pins the *ranking* lane (`eval_cost`) to the coarse budget (#1029/#2138) — but it does **not** cover the line-search Value lane, so that lane must price the fixed point.

**Fix** (landed 65e08b571): the Value line-search lane prices at `refine_progress_extension = true` — the same fixed point the gradient differentiates and the cert samples — so value, gradient, and certification are one coherent objective. The coarse eval_cost ranking budget is untouched (contract preserved). The polish only runs when the iterate is already near the fixed point, so it's cheap; a no-op at small n (tier0 unchanged).

**Durability / process note (the lead asked this be on the record):** the equivalent one-line fix landed once as `ec243d300`, then a concurrent fleet session's rewrite of `outer_objective.rs` (which deleted `line_search_probe_criterion` in favor of the basin-lower-envelope `eval_cost` and this `Value`-order drive) **silently clobbered it** on a branch that forked pre-fix — last-writer-wins. This is the **second** cross-session clobber of this fix. So the re-land (65e08b571) ships **with a pinning regression test** (`value_lane_prices_at_shared_fixed_point_2228`): it builds a wide-p over-smoothed fixture, sanity-asserts the coarse-vs-full budgets actually diverge there (so it can't pass vacuously), then asserts the Value lane agrees with the analytic lane within the certification roundoff bound — the exact invariant the cert enforces at fit end, checked at probe time. Any future rewrite that reintroduces the coarse budget on the Value lane now goes red instead of silently landing. **Lesson: single-line fixes in fleet-hot files must land with a pinning test, or a concurrent rewrite erases them.**

Empirical end-to-end validation (E1 mint + #2266 pytest green on a wheel built from 65e08b571) is in progress; the determinism keystone remains confirmed fixed (run-twice bit-identical).

This is exactly the "outer search cannot certify … loops in EV churn" behavior tracked in #2253 — not the Value/gradient desync this issue was about.

Being chased now: the principled fix is a **typed recoverable refusal** (non-PD / did-not-converge class) at the NaN-producing sub-term so the outer bridge folds it as an infeasible trial and the line search backtracks cleanly, rather than an `Ok(NaN)` propagating.

The "REML objective improved <1e-7 over 6 steps yet projected |g|≈80 persists" cost-stall is downstream of (A): the line search can accept no step because trial points return non-finite cost, so the objective looks flat while the true gradient stays ~80. The `railed=[]`-at-a-boundary observation compounds it (the rail cert has a lower-bound λ→0 counter but no upper-bound twin, so an upper rail at rho=30 isn't projected out) — under investigation as part of the same degeneracy.

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-12T14:39:05Z ---
## E1 wall: derivation of the quasi-Laplace criterion limit as an atom collapses (verdict: W2, cross-confirms #2132 at K=1)

Deriving the limit of the fitting criterion `v(ρ)` as an atom's realised DOF `d_eff → 0` — driven here by over-smoothing (`λ_smooth, λ_ard → ∞`, which shrinks the latent coords onto the penalty null space and collapses the weighted basis Gram `Φᵀdiag(a²)Φ` in rank). This decides whether the `construction.rs:437` `Ok(+∞)` veto is wrong-for-fitting (W1) or load-bearing (W2).

### The assembled criterion
`v = loss.total() + extra_penalty_energy + quasi_laplace_complexity − occam`, with
`quasi_laplace_complexity = ½(log|H| − log|H_tt|) + rank_charge`, `rank_charge = Σ_k ½·d_eff,k·ln(max(N_eff,k, 1))`.

### Term-by-term limit as d_eff → 0
1. **`loss.total()`** (penalized reconstruction deviance at the inner optimum) → **FINITE**. The atom flattens onto its penalty null-space submodel; the reconstruction tends to the null-submodel fit and the penalty energy `λ‖P^½ t‖²` stays finite (`t` → the null space where `P t = 0`). This is the ordinary REML "the term is as simple as the data warrants" limit.

2. **`occam`** = `−½ Σ_k r_k·rank(S_k)·log λ_smooth,k (+ #972 frame correction)` → diverges only **O(log λ)**. This is the REML smoothing-penalty `½log|λS|₊` evidence piece; logarithmic in the smoothing strength, hence **subdominant** to term 3.

3. **`quasi_laplace_complexity`** → **−∞, EXTENSIVE in the data**.
   - `rank_charge = Σ ½·d_eff·ln N_eff → 0` (since d_eff → 0).
   - `log|H| − log|H_tt| = log|β-Schur complement|` (arrow factorization `|H| = |H_tt|·|S_ββ|`; `coordinate_block_log_det` sums `2·ln(diag)` of the t-block Cholesky, construction.rs:395-411). As the decoder collapses (`a²‖B‖² → 0`) the β-Schur complement → singular and `log|S_ββ| → −∞`, and this divergence is **extensive** — it grows with the co-fired data / `N_eff` (construction.rs:337-339: "VANISHED decoder (a²‖B‖²→0): the β-mode is degenerate, the β-Schur log-det → −∞ is the Laplace approximation BREAKING DOWN"; #2132 measured this as basins "hundreds of nats lower within Δρ≈1e-2").

### Net
`v → finite + extra_penalty + (−∞, extensive) − O(log λ) = −∞`. **The criterion is unbounded below as the atom collapses.** This is exactly #2132's owner finding — *"the evidence criterion RANKED COLLAPSE BETTER than structure… the Laplace collapse reward is extensive in the data."*

### VERDICT: W2 (genuine collapse attractor). The veto is load-bearing.
The `+∞` at construction.rs:437 is the guard that prevents the optimizer diving to `−∞` by degenerating the atom. It is a hard cliff, not a smooth cost, which is why the outer search pins against it (the observed `|g|≈80`, objective flat, cert-fails signature) rather than settling.

### Why #2132's fix does not save E1: the barrier is K≥2-gated
#2132 landed the occupancy-scaled Jeffreys anti-collapse barrier `−½·Σ_C N_eff,C·log det(F_C + ε_C·I)` (penalties.rs) that makes collapse cost grow with `N_eff` and flips the ordering. But it is **pairwise and K≥2-gated**: `if k_atoms < 2 { return … }` at penalties.rs:124 and :214. It prices OFF-diagonal decoder overlaps `o_jk` between *distinct* atoms (co-collapse of merging atoms). For E1's **single atom (K=1)** it abstains entirely — so a lone atom over-smoothing onto its own null (SELF-collapse, the diagonal Jeffreys term) has NO counter-term, and the `−∞` attractor is un-opposed. **E1 is the #2132 collapse pathology at K=1 on real data — the cross-confirmation the wall predicted.**

### Fix plan
The principled fix is the **SELF (diagonal) analogue** of the #2132 barrier: a single-atom anti-collapse counter-term in the same `N_eff` currency (penalize `det(F_self)→0` for one atom, active at K=1), so a lone over-smoothing atom's collapse cost grows with its co-fired data and the criterion regains a finite minimum. Then the outer search settles at the warranted curvature — or the atom honestly dies via the warrant/retraction path (#2261) if a curved atom is unwarranted for GPT-2 refusal directions — instead of pinning against the veto cliff. This is a modeling-level fix (extend the anti-collapse barrier's diagonal term to K=1), NOT a numerical β-Schur floor and NOT the #2253 adjoint. The `construction.rs:437` typed-refusal is confirmed a behavioral no-op (the bridge already maps `Ok(+∞)`, typed `Err`, and non-finite gradient uniformly to `recoverable`), but the "cost must be finite-or-refused, never Ok(inf)" hygiene invariant will be pinned regardless.

### Two corrections to my earlier comments on this issue
1. **`cost=inf` conflated two distinct refusals**, both laundered to `Ok(+∞)` by `eval_cost` (outer_objective.rs:3596/3608): the rank-collapse veto (construction.rs:437, `Ok(inf)`) AND inner-solve recoverable refusals (typed `Err`: non-PD / "did not converge"). If so the true limit is **finite (W1-leaning)** and the veto is a **discrete MP-rank cliff** slamming `+∞` on a point whose criterion is a perfectly good finite value.

### Consequence for the fix
If W1 holds, the fix is **not** a cancellation-matched Jeffreys for a −∞ divergence (there is none to cancel) — it is to price the `d_eff→0` limit at its true finite value (the null-space submodel) so the search settles at/just-below the cliff, and/or soften the discrete MP-rank classification so `rank_eff` doesn't round to 0 discontinuously. Confirming with an approach sweep (ard → veto at E1-like smooth) to read the last-finite-before-cliff trajectory; final W1/W2 + the correct fix to follow.

Progress: root cause confirmed and first fix pushed to main (`c01a224e6`).

**Root cause (empirically confirmed):** the inner SAE Newton step's dense Direct/SqrtBA reduced β-Schur solve never deflates the closed-form chart-gauge orbit (circle rotation / torus phase / patch translation+scale). That orbit's β-component is an exact null direction of the reduced β-Schur `S_β` (Schur identity: `H·(δt,δβ)=0 ⇒ S_β δβ=0`), so the step's orbit component is arbitrary — it drifts `t` off the chart across the outer ρ-walk and starves the identifiable descent. Instrumented the K=1 circle inner solve and observed the signature crawl directly: ε-sized quotient steps (~1e-6) while ‖g‖ plateaus near tolerance, thousands of iterations.

Notably, the `ArrowBetaGaugeQuotient` Faddeev–Popov machinery (`P S_β P + Q Qᵀ`) already existed and was unit-tested but reachable only from tests — `solve_arrow_newton_step_artifacts` hardcoded `beta_gauge_active = false`.

**Fix:** `SaeManifoldTerm::closed_form_beta_gauge_directions` (β-part of the closed-form gauge, structurally 1 per circle/torus phase → no ρ-walk count flicker, addressing the #2253 concern) installed as the reduced-β gauge quotient on the fit-step system for the dense modes; the dense step now solves the pinned quotient with the RHS projected onto the identifiable complement. The loss/criterion are gauge-invariant, so only the convergence path changes — the fit converges to a gauge-fixed representative on the chart. Every non-fit-step caller leaves the quotient `None` and is byte-identical; the wide-p InexactPCG lane is left byte-exact for a follow-up.

### ISSUE #2233 [OPEN] — MDL crossover theorem: curved atoms win Eq-4 bits via SUPPORT+residual (not code) for s=d+1 kinds; closed-form birth pre-screen
Author: SauersML   Created: 2026-07-09T14:03:02Z   Labels: 
Comments: 17
------------------------------------------------------------------------
BODY:
# The MDL crossover theorem: when a curved atom beats flat latents in Eq-4 bits — and a closed-form birth pre-screen

## Setup

Zoo Eq-4 (bench/bsf_manifold_zoo.py:658-699) prices a featurizer at distortion δ per token:

    bits = support + code + resid + dict
    support = log2 C(G, L0)                              (global, L0 = mean active atoms)
    code    = Σ_g p_g · Σ_i ½ log2(1 + λ_i^g / δ)        (per-atom active-contribution spectrum, water-filled, truncated to code_dims_g)
    resid   = Σ_j ½ log2(1 + μ_j / δ)                    (residual covariance spectrum)
    dict    = params · ½ log2(N) / N                     (BIC-style ½ log N per parameter, amortized)

Consider ONE planted factor: intrinsic dimension d, ambient span s (the dimension of the smallest linear subspace containing its manifold image: circle s=2, sphere s=3, torus s=4, Möbius s=3, swiss s=3, helix s=3), activation rate ρ, per-direction signal energy λ.

- FLAT (BSF-generous matching): s latents active per firing token; code_dims = 1 each; dictionary s·P.
- CURVED: one atom, code_dims = d+1 (coords + amplitude); dictionary m·P, m = basis size (circle with H harmonics: m = 2H+1; torus: (2H+1)²).

## The per-term crossover

**Code bits.** Flat transmits s scalars, curved transmits d+1. Savings per firing token ≈ ρ·(s−d−1)·½log2(1+λ/δ).

The surprise: **for most curved zoo kinds this term is ZERO.** Circle (s=2, d+1=2), sphere (s=3, d+1=3), Möbius (s=3, d+1=3), swiss (s=3, d+1=3) — the curved atom transmits exactly as many scalars as the flat span. Strictly positive only when d+1 < s: **torus (3 < 4), helix (2 < 3)**, and generally high-codimension curves (a d=1 curve winding through s ambient directions saves s−2 scalars/token — grows with winding complexity).

**Support bits.** Flat activates s atoms where curved activates 1. At dictionary size G and budget L0, the marginal support cost of one extra active slot is ≈ log2(G/L0). Savings ≈ ρ·(s−1)·log2(G/L0). At G = 32768, L0 = 32: **10 bits per extra slot per firing token.** This is the term that scales with overcompleteness — the 32K regime is where curved atoms win support bits hardest.

**Residual bits.** At matched rank, the flat s-dim projection leaves the CURVATURE energy in the residual: for a circle of radius r embedded with noise σ², flat rank-2 capture is exact in-plane but any rank-BUDGETED fit (fewer than s slots granted) leaves O(r²) energy; more generally the curved atom's nonlinear image captures energy a rank-(d+1) LINEAR code cannot (Eckart-Young gap between the manifold's nonlinear width and its linear span). This is second-order vs support/code but always ≥ 0 for a correctly-fit curved atom.

**Dictionary bits.** The curved SURCHARGE: (m−s)·P·½log2(N)/N per token. Circle H=3: m=7 vs s=2 → 5P·½log2(N)/N.

## The theorem (crossover condition)

A curved birth strictly lowers Eq-4 bits iff

    ρ·N·[ (s−d−1)·½log2(1+λ/δ) + (s−1)·log2(G/L0) + Δresid ] > (m−s)·P·½log2(N)

Numbers at the creditscope shape (N=96k, P=2048, G=32K, L0=32, SNR ~ 20dB → ½log2(1+λ/δ) ≈ 3.3):
- circle (s=2,d=1,H=3): LHS/token ≈ ρ·(0 + 10 + Δr); RHS total ≈ 5·2048·8.3 ≈ 85k bits → a circle pays for itself when ρ·N·10 > 85k, i.e. **ρ > 0.09%** activation rate. Essentially every real feature clears this.
- torus (s=4,d=2,H=3 product, m=49): code+support LHS ≈ ρ·(3.3 + 30); RHS ≈ 45·2048·8.3 ≈ 765k bits → needs ρ > 2.3%. Rich atoms need to fire often.

**Corollary (the #1026 margin explanation).** The Adam-lane hybrid's thin EV margin at matched actives is EXPECTED: for circles the per-token CODE cost equals flat's — the win is support + residual, which EV-at-matched-actives only partially credits. The MDL scoreboard (bits at fixed R²) credits all three. We have been fighting on the weakest scoreboard.

## The engineering payoff: closed-form birth pre-screen

`run_structure_search_rounds` refits EVERY proposal (`candidate_fit` per proposal per round) — the expensive gate. All crossover quantities are available at PROPOSAL time, before any refit:
- ρ̂: residual-factor activation mass (rows where the birth decoder projects above noise),
- ŝ: participation ratio of the factor's residual covariance spectrum, (Σλ)²/Σλ²,
- d, m: from the candidate topology,
- λ/δ: factor energy over the current residual floor.

Pre-screen: compute predicted ΔMDL for every proposal, refit only the positive-predicted ones (or the top few). The e-process gate stays the arbiter (the pre-screen can only DEFER a proposal, never accept one), so honesty is unchanged while the per-round refit count drops from #proposals to #plausible.

**Correspondence check (why this is principled, not a second criterion):** the ledger's REML evidence delta IS the Laplace estimate of the description-length change (evidence = −DL in nats); the ½(m−s)·log N dictionary surcharge is exactly the Laplace/BIC rank charge. The pre-screen is the ledger's own currency computed in closed form from spectra instead of by refit — the unified SaeMigrationLedger (#2232 Inc 3, landed 1ea7f699f) carries `reml_delta + rank_charge + dl_bits`, so the pre-screen writes its prediction into the SAME record the post-refit verdict fills in; prediction-vs-verdict becomes a logged calibration curve for free.

## Tasks
1. `structure_harvest`: compute (ρ̂, ŝ, λ̂) per birth proposal from the residual factor spectra already harvested; closed-form ΔMDL; sort + gate proposals (defer non-positive). Log predicted-vs-realized on every refit.
2. Zoo: assert the per-kind crossover table empirically (torus/helix show code savings; circle/sphere show support-only wins) — per-atom Eq-4 breakdown already exists.
3. #1026 close: report bits-at-R² (Eq-4) alongside EV for hybrid-vs-flat at 32K — the scoreboard the theorem says we win by a wide margin, not a thin one.

**Task 1 — pre-screen (`predicted_birth_dl_bits`, structure_harvest.rs:731–823).** Implements exactly
```
ΔMDL = ρ̂·N·[ (ŝ−d−1)·½log₂(1+λ̂/δ) + (ŝ−1)·log₂(G/L0) ] − (m−ŝ)·P·½log₂(N)
```
from spectra already harvested at proposal time (no candidate refit): ŝ = `participation_ratio` of the factor-energy spectrum, ρ̂ = fraction of tokens whose residual projects above the per-direction noise floor δ_j = u_jᵀD u_j (fitted, not hand-set), (d,m) from `curved_topology_for_span(ŝ)`, G=`k_atoms()`, L0=`mean_active_atoms`. Three correctness details worth flagging:
- The **code term is signed** `(ŝ−d−1)` — a topology needing MORE code dims than its span is honestly charged, not floored to zero. Matches the theorem's "zero for circle/sphere, positive for torus/helix."
- The **Eckart–Young Δresid ≥ 0 is deliberately OMITTED** → the pre-screen strictly *under*-credits every birth → it can only DEFER (proposal returns next round as the residual evolves), never accept. The e-process gate stays the sole arbiter, so honesty is unchanged — exactly the property the issue requires.
- `(m−ŝ).max(0)` and the N≥2 log floor keep it finite on degenerate inputs; deferred proposals are logged with their predicted bits (`birth_predictions`, `deferred_predicted_bits` on `HarvestReport`), so predicted-vs-realized is a free calibration curve.

**Task 2 — crossover accounting (`crossover_firings`) + tests.** The break-even firing rate `f* = Φ_extra·L_param / Δcode` (Φ_extra = curved dictionary surcharge params, L_param = distortion-matched per-scalar rate). Reference test `crossover_matches_mdl_reference` (block b2 [1.10,0.34] vs circle [1.49] at δ²=chart.residual): I hand-verified every number — dcode = ½log₂(1+1.10/1.061)+½log₂(1+0.34/1.061) − ½log₂(1+1.49/1.061) = 0.713−0.633 = **0.080** ✓; L_param = 0.713/2 = **0.357** ✓; f* = 32·0.357/0.080 = **141.2** ✓. `crossover_says_no_on_the_control_case` confirms the accounting reports f*=∞ when the chart codes more per firing (dcode<0) — it can say NO. Beyond spec: a support-entropy H(S) (Chow–Liu tree) selection currency is charged by default with the combinatorial log₂C(G,k) worst-case reported alongside, so a tiling dictionary's predictable co-firing isn't overpaid.

**external_topk (Gao TopK flat bar), K=32768:**
- held-out EV = **0.9174**
- Eq-4 **bits at R²=0.99**: total ≈ **1,049,290** bits/token-block, decomposed:
  - **dictionary** ≈ **1,048,938** (the floor: 32768 flat atoms × 2048 params × ½log₂N/N)
  - **support** = 362.3
  - **code** = 11.2
  - **residual** = 340.8
- at R²=0.95: total 1,049,012 (code 5.2, resid 68.8); at R²=0.90: total 1,048,938 (code/resid → 0).

The flat bar's description length is **completely dominated by the dictionary term** — 32768 flat atoms each cost a full P=2048-dim decoder column. This is exactly the term the crossover theorem says a curved/hybrid dictionary undercuts: a hybrid replaces most of those 32768 flat atoms with a handful of curved atoms (m·P params for m≪K basis functions), so its dictionary bits are a tiny fraction of the flat 1.049M. The support/code/residual split above confirms the theorem's within-token accounting (support ≫ code for the circle-class regime).

**Method note (recorded for reuse):** the Eq-4 scorer is O(#firing atoms) with a per-atom SVD; at K=32768 it was ~13 min/arm at `--bits-max-rows 8192` (untenable interactively). Dropping to `--bits-max-rows 256` (far fewer of the 32768 atoms fire on a small row sample, so the per-atom loop shrinks) brought each arm to ~90 s while keeping K=32768 — the actual contest. Numbers above use `bits_rows=256`, an unbiased per-token estimate. A flat-atom fast path in the scorer (code_dims=1 ⇒ rank-1, skip the full SVD) would make the 8192-row frontier tractable.

**In flight:** the `hybrid` (flat + curved tier) and `gam_flat` (Rust flat lane) arms on the same split/scorer — the curved-tier torch fit is CPU-bound (the known ManifoldSAE E-step FFI wall), so those rows follow. ## Authoritative re-score at bits_max_rows=8192 (uncontended H100) — and a load-bearing correction about the bits metric

Re-ran the finalist arm at the authoritative `--bits-max-rows 8192` (K=32768, top_k=32, seed 0, creditscope L30) on a free H100. This surfaced a **methodological fact that changes how these numbers must be read**, and it validates the request to re-score at fixed N.

**external_topk (flat Gao-TopK bar), K=32768:**

| bits_max_rows | EV | bits@R²=0.99 (total) | support | code | resid | dict-floor (bits@R²=0.8) |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **256** | 0.9174 | **1,049,290** | 362.3 | 11.2 | 340.8 | 1,048,938 |
| **8192** | 0.9174 | **56,322** | 362.3 | 111.0 | 2601.0 | 53,610 |

The totals differ **~18×** between 256 and 8192 rows. Reason: the Eq-4 **dictionary term is `params · ½·log₂(N) / N`** where **N = the bits-scoring sample size** (`bits_max_rows`), not the training N. For 32768×2048 = 67.1M flat params, dict = 67.1M·½·log₂(N)/N → 1.049M bits at N=256 vs 53.6k at N=8192 (ratio ≈ 19.7×, matching the observed 18×). So:
- **Absolute Eq-4 bits are not comparable across different `bits_max_rows`.** The 256-row screening I posted earlier is fine for a fast within-N read but its absolute magnitude is inflated by the small-N dictionary amortization. Re-scoring finalists at one fixed authoritative N (8192) was necessary — thanks for insisting.
- The dictionary term **dominates** the description length (~95%: 53,610 of 56,322 at R²=0.99). Support/code/resid are second-order.

**Consequence for the hybrid-vs-flat verdict (important, honest):** the `hybrid` arm in `driver_1026_arms.py` stacks 256 curved atoms *on top of the full K=32768 flat dictionary* (it reduces the flat **active budget** k_lin, not the flat **atom count**). Its parameter count is therefore **larger** than external_topk's, so on this dict-dominated scoreboard the hybrid arm as configured carries a dictionary *surcharge*, not a saving — the per-factor crossover theorem (replace s flat atoms with 1 curved atom ⇒ fewer atoms) is only realized by a dictionary that **reduces the flat atom count**, which this hybrid arm does not. The real hybrid@8192 row is needed to quantify whether its support/code/residual savings overcome that surcharge; **it is currently blocked on the torch ManifoldSAE curved-tier E-step wall** (3000 curved steps did not finish in 24 min; even 500 steps exceeded 11 min — a CPU-bound FFI per-step cost, tracked separately, not the scorer). I'll append it if the reduced-step run lands.

**Scorer perf datum (for future Eq-4 runs):** `gamfit._description_length` is O(#firing atoms) with a per-atom SVD; at K=32768 it was ~13 min/arm at `bits_max_rows=8192` when the box was contended, ~1.5 min uncontended. A flat-atom fast path (`code_dims=1 ⇒ rank-1`, skip the SVD) would remove this cost.

Provenance: native `gamfit-0.1.253` (manylinux_2_35, current `main` HEAD 48bfe5865, `has_eq4` verified). Data: creditscope L30 residual_post, 96k train / 24k test, seed 0. GPU pegged at 100% during TopK training.


--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-10T21:33:30Z ---
### The theorem-faithful hybrid config the next run must use (and the scorer fast path is landed)

Two follow-ups on the finalist re-score.

**1. Scorer fast path landed** (`b21f389cd`, on `main`). `atom_code_spectrum` SVD'd every atom's column-centered contribution. A `code_dim==1` (flat) atom is rank-one (one scalar code × one decoder row) and stays rank-one under column-centering, so its single singular value is exactly the Frobenius norm: `σ₁² = ‖centered‖_F² / (rows−1)` — no SVD. That replaces an O(rows·d·min(rows,d)) SVD with an O(rows·d) sum of squares for every flat atom, which is the entire dictionary in a K=32768 TopK bar (the ~13 min/arm cost). Parity-gated: `flat_atom_fast_path_matches_svd_to_tolerance` asserts fast == SVD-top-singular-value on a rank-one contribution to fp tolerance; `curved_atom_still_uses_full_svd_spectrum` confirms `code_dim≥2` keeps the full SVD. It does NOT touch the curved-atom SVD cost (that stays O(rows·d·(d+1))), so the curved-tier E-step training wall remains the hybrid blocker.

**2. The decisive hybrid row must use a parameter-non-inflating config.** The crossover theorem's claim is that **curvature buys FEWER ATOMS** — one curved atom replaces the `s` flat latents of a factor. On the Eq-4 scoreboard, which is ~95% dictionary bits (`params·½log₂(N)/N`), a fair test therefore requires `dict_params(hybrid) ≤ dict_params(external)`: curved atoms **replacing** flat atoms, i.e. the flat tier's ATOM COUNT `K_flat` reduced (not just its active budget `k_lin`), so the added `256·(2H+1)·P` curved params are more than offset by the `(32768 − K_flat)·P` flat params removed.

The `driver_1026_arms.py` `hybrid` arm as written does **not** do this — it keeps all `K=32768` flat atoms and stacks 256 curved atoms on top (it only cuts the active budget `k_lin`). That config has MORE parameters than `external_topk`, so it carries a dictionary surcharge and cannot win the MDL scoreboard regardless of its support/code/residual savings. Any future hybrid@8192 row must be run with `K_flat` reduced so `K_flat·P + 256·(2H+1)·P ≤ 32768·P` — otherwise it measures the wrong contest. This is the required next row, alongside the curved-tier E-step-wall blocker; the flat bar (`external_topk@8192`: total 56,322 bits @R²=0.99) stands as posted.


--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-11T02:09:32Z ---
## The MDL crossover theorem, formalized against the actual Eq-4 scorer + the theorem-faithful config (landed `acf40010c`)

This states the crossover cleanly, ties every term to the Rust scorer, gives the exact dictionary-parameter inequality, and lands the driver config that makes the hybrid contest fair. Preliminary numbers are closed-form at the real scale; the held-out support/code/residual split is the one remaining GPU row.

### 0. The scorer's bit accounting (the ground truth every term ties to)

`eq4_fixed_distortion_description_length` (`crates/gam-sae/src/eq4_description_length.rs`) prices one fitted featurizer at a fixed R² as
```
bits(R²) = support_bits + code_bits(R²) + resid_bits(R²) + dictionary_bits
```
with, verbatim from the code:

- **support** `= log₂ C(G, ⌊L0⌉)` — `selection_bits(n_atoms, round(L0))`, `L0` = mean active atoms/token, **R²-independent** (`description_length.rs:selection_bits`).
- **code** `= Σ_g p_g · rate(spectrum_g)` — a JOINT firing-probability-weighted reverse-water-filling of each atom's per-firing coordinate spectrum against one shared water level (`weighted_reverse_water_filling`); atom `g` contributes `d_g = code_dims[g]` coordinates (1 for a flat atom, `d+1` for a `d`-chart).
- **residual** `= rate(residual covariance spectrum)` at that same shared water level (weight-1 component).
- **dictionary** `= 0.5 · dictionary_params / N · log₂(max(N,2))` (`eq4_description_length.rs:297`) — the BIC charge for the decoder, where **N = the bits-scoring sample size** (`bits_max_rows`) and `dictionary_params` is the decoder scalar count the featurizer reports.

At K=32768 the measured flat bar is **56,322 bits @R²=0.99, of which 53,610 (95%) is the dictionary term** — so the dictionary inequality below is what decides the contest, and support/code/residual are the second-order margin.

### 1. The dictionary-parameter inequality

A flat atom is one decoder column: `P` params, `code_dim = 1` (`arm_featurizers._flat_block_from_sparse`, `dictionary_params = decoder.size = K·P`). A curved atom is a decoder BLOCK of `b` basis functions mapping into the `P`-dim ambient space: `b·P` params, `code_dim = d+1` (`_curved_block_torch`, `dict = dec.size`). For an H-harmonic Fourier circle `b = 2H+1`.

So for a hybrid of `K_flat` flat atoms + `K_curved` curved atoms:
```
dict_params(hybrid) = K_flat·P + K_curved·b·P ,   dict_params(external) = K_ext·P
```
Because dictionary bits are monotone in params and dominate the score, an MDL win is **only possible** when
```
  K_flat + K_curved·b  ≤  K_ext          (★ the faithful-config inequality)
```
i.e. the flat **atom count** `K_flat` (not merely the per-token active budget `k_lin`) is reduced enough that the added `K_curved·b·P` curved params are offset by `(K_ext − K_flat)·P` removed flat params. Setting `K_flat = K_ext − K_curved·b` makes (★) an **equality** — identical dictionaries — so any support/code/residual saving becomes a pure net win.

The committed `hybrid` arm keeps all `K_ext` flat atoms and stacks `K_curved` curved atoms on top (it cut `k_lin`, a per-token quantity, not `K_flat`). That violates (★): `dict_params(hybrid) = K_ext·P + K_curved·b·P > K_ext·P`, a fixed surcharge that no within-token saving can overcome. This is the "impossible as configured" gap.

### 2. The per-factor crossover (theorem proper)

For one planted curved kind of intrinsic dim `d` spanning `s` ambient directions (a circle: `d=1, s=2`), replacing its `s` flat atoms with **1** curved atom of code-dim `d+1` and basis width `b`, over the `ρ·N` tokens on which the factor is active — this is exactly `predicted_birth_dl_bits` (`description_length.rs`):
```
ΔMDL = ρ·N·[ (s − d − 1)·½log₂(1+λ/δ)   +   (s − 1)·log₂(G/L0) ]  −  (b − s)·P·½log₂ N
        └──────── code ────────┘   └──────── support ────────┘      └──── dictionary ────┘
```
term by term:

- **support** `(s−1)·log₂(G/L0)` per active token: flat lights `s` slots, curved lights 1, freeing `s−1` slots each worth `log₂(G/L0)` — the term that **scales with overcompleteness** (the 32K regime). Matches `support_bits`' `log₂ C(G, L0)` delta.
- **code** `(s − d − 1)·½log₂(1+λ/δ)` per active token. **For a circle `s = d+1 = 2` ⇒ code delta = 0**: the surprise that circles win ZERO code bits. Positive only for kinds living in more ambient dims than `d+1` (a curved sheet).
- **dictionary** `−(b − s)·P·½log₂ N`, absolute BIC charge (the same charge the scorer amortizes as `½·params/N·log₂N` per token). **Sign is `b` vs `s`**:
  - circle `s=2, b=2H+1≥3` ⇒ `b>s` ⇒ dictionary is a **surcharge** (a circle atom's decoder is *wider* than the 2 flat columns it replaces). A circle wins on support, never on dict.
  - a **high-span** kind with `s ≥ b` (e.g. a shell/torus spanning many ambient dims, coded by few basis functions) ⇒ `b≤s` ⇒ dictionary is a **saving** — curvature genuinely buys fewer decoder params.

The residual (Eckart–Young) `Δresid ≥ 0` is deliberately omitted from the pre-screen (it can only defer, never falsely accept; the e-process gate stays sole arbiter).

**Crossover firing count** (`crossover_firings`): `f* = Φ·L_param / ΔL_per_firing`, `Φ = ` extra decoder scalars, `ΔL_per_firing = Δcode + Δsupport` per firing, `L_param = ` distortion-matched per-scalar rate. `ΔL_per_firing ≤ 0` ⇒ `f* = ∞` (the accounting says NO). Above `f*` the richer decoder's amortized surcharge is repaid by per-firing savings.

**Corollary (why EV-at-matched-actives is thin but Eq-4 is wide).** EV at a matched active budget prices only the *code* term. For a circle that term is 0, so the EV margin is ~noise — while the Eq-4 score also credits the `(s−1)·log₂(G/L0)` support term, which at G=32768/L0=32 is ≈10.4 bits per freed slot. The margin the EV scoreboard cannot see is exactly the support column.

### 3. Preliminary numbers — closed form at the real scale (no GPU, no wheel)

`experiments/1026_close/crossover_theorem_check.py` evaluates the two closed-form terms (support = `log₂C(G,k)`, dict = `½·params/N·log₂N`) that reproduce the scorer verbatim, at K=32768, P=2048, N=8192, L0=32, circle b=2H+1=7, K_curved=256, 8 active circle slots:

| config | dict_params | dict_bits | Δsupport | Δdict | **net bits (flat − hybrid)** | faithful? |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| external (bar) | 67,108,864 | 53,248 | — | — | — | — |
| **STACKED** hybrid (k_flat=K) | 70,778,880 | 56,160 | +83.0 | +2912.0 | **−2829 → hybrid LOSES** | ✗ |
| **FAITHFUL** hybrid (k_flat=30976) | 67,108,864 | 53,248 | +83.0 | +0.0 | **+83 → hybrid WINS** | ✓ |

`k_flat = 32768 − 256·7 = 30976` makes the dictionaries carry identical params; the circle's zero code delta plus equal residual leave the +83-bit support win as the whole (net-positive) margin. This is the crossover DIRECTION at exact scale — the stacked arm loses by the dict surcharge, the faithful arm wins on support. The dict-*negative* regime (§2, `s≥b`) is a strictly larger win reserved for high-span kinds.

### 4. The theorem-faithful config (landed)

`acf40010c`, `experiments/1026_close/`:
- **`--k-flat`** on `driver_1026_arms.py`: the flat-tier ATOM COUNT (default `None` = `K`, preserving the legacy stacked arm). `fit_hybrid`/`fit_hybrid_rust` build the flat tier at `k_flat` atoms; the curved tier is unchanged. Set `--k-flat 30976` for the faithful contest.
- **Self-certification**: every `--bits` row now records `bits_dict_params`, `bits_dict_params_external_ref = K·P`, and `bits_dict_params_faithful` (must be `true`), plus `k_flat` at top level — so the fairness of each row is visible, not asserted.
- **`run_faithful_hybrid.sbatch`**: one job runs `external_topk` then the `--k-flat`-reduced `hybrid` on the same split at `bits_max_rows=8192`, computing `k_flat = K − curved_atoms·B` and asserting `K_FLAT ≥ top_k`.

### 5. What the full GPU run still needs

The closed-form §3 settles support + dict (the ~95% of the score). The remaining GPU row measures the *water-filled* code + residual split on fitted spectra — needed to confirm the circle's `Δcode ≈ 0` empirically and to catch any residual asymmetry. It is `run_faithful_hybrid.sbatch` on one A100 window; the sole blocker is the torch ManifoldSAE curved-tier E-step wall (per prior comments: 500 curved steps > 11 min, CPU-bound FFI), tracked separately from the scorer. On landing, the row must show `bits_dict_params_faithful=true` and `bits_at_r2_0.99(hybrid) < 56,322`.

No local run: the checked-in wheel's `_rust.abi3.so` is stale for the current source (missing `DictionaryConvergenceError`), so the scorer-in-the-loop path needs the fresh MSI/GPU wheel; the closed-form checker above is dependency-free and was run locally.

- **`predicted_birth_dl_bits`** (`crates/gam-sae/src/description_length.rs:252`) implements Eq-4's crossover inequality verbatim: code term `(span − intrinsic_dim − 1)·scalar_rate_bits(signal_var, noise_floor)` (signed — zero for circle/sphere/Möbius/swiss where d+1==s, positive only for torus/helix), support term `(span−1)·log2(G/L0)`, BIC dictionary surcharge `(basis_size−span)₊·p_out·½log2(N)`. The Eckart-Young residual term is deliberately omitted so the pre-screen strictly under-credits (can only defer, never wrongly accept — the e-process gate stays sole arbiter).
- **Wired into the birth loop** (`structure_harvest.rs:722-839`): per residual-factor direction, computes span (participation ratio), (intrinsic_dim, basis_size) via `curved_topology_for_span`, and firing rate ρ from residual projections vs the fitted per-direction noise floor, then calls the pre-screen. Only positive-predicted-ΔMDL survivors are refit; the rest are counted in `births_deferred` and never reach a K=1 fit — exactly the "refit only the plausible, drop refit count from #proposals to #survivors" payoff. This also composes with tonight's birth-race parallelism/cost fixes.
- **`crossover_firings`** (`description_length.rs:445`), Eq-4 scorer + flat-atom fast path (`eq4_description_length.rs`), and the theorem-faithful driver config (`driver_1026_arms.py --k-flat`, dictionary-parameter fairness inequality) all present, with tests (`crossover_matches_mdl_reference`, `crossover_says_no_on_the_control_case`, etc.).

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-12T18:32:11Z ---
## Close-out: MDL crossover theorem + closed-form birth pre-screen — verified GREEN

The theorem, its accounting, and the closed-form pre-screen are landed and test-verified. Summary of the evidence.

### The crossover holds — SUPPORT-driven for the s = d+1 kinds

The pre-screen `predicted_birth_dl_bits` (`crates/gam-sae/src/description_length.rs`) computes the exact per-term Eq-4 delta:

```
ΔMDL = ρ·N·[ (s−d−1)·½log₂(1+λ/δ)   +   (s−1)·log₂(G/L0) ]   −   (m−s)·P·½log₂(N)
             \___ code (0 for s=d+1) ___/   \___ support ___/       \___ dict surcharge ___/
```

**Circle (s=2, d=1, m=3) — the canonical s=d+1 kind.** At N=1000, P=8, G=1024, L0=32, ρ=0.1 (`birth_prescreen_matches_hand_computed_crossover`, hand-checked to 1e-9):

| term | value |
|---|---|
| code `(s−d−1)·rate` | **0 bits** (curved atom transmits exactly the flat span's scalars — the theorem's signature) |
| support `ρN·(s−1)·log₂(G/L0)` | 0.1·1000·1·5 = **+500 bits** |
| dict surcharge `(m−s)·P·½log₂N` | (3−2)·8·0.5·9.9658 = **−39.86 bits** |
| **net predicted ΔMDL** | **+460.14 bits** → curved birth PAYS |

The win is entirely the **support** term — the extra active slots the flat span spends that the single curved atom does not — and it scales with overcompleteness `log₂(G/L0)` (5 bits/slot at G=1024/L0=32; ~10 bits/slot at the 32K creditscope regime).

**Torus at tiny ρ (s=4, d=2, m=25):** net ΔMDL < 0 → correctly DEFERRED (rich basis, negligible firing). **Control chart** that codes *more* per firing (`crossover_says_no_on_the_control_case`): f* = ∞ → never pays. The accounting can say NO.

The pre-screen is **conservative by construction**: it omits the Eckart–Young Δresid ≥ 0 term, so predicted ΔMDL ≤ true ΔMDL — it can only DEFER a proposal, never falsely admit one; the e-process gate stays the sole arbiter of acceptance.

**Empirical flat baseline (measured, H100 creditscope L30 residual_post, K=32768, top_k=32, bits_max_rows=8192):** `external_topk` = **56,322 bits @ R²=0.99** = dict 53,610 + support 362 + code 111 + resid 2601 — i.e. ~95% dictionary bits, the term a compact curved basis undercuts.

### Verified GREEN (warm MSI, gam-target-2233ps, green base b63a91522 + fix 82e476cb7)

```
birth_prescreen_matches_hand_computed_crossover ......................... ok
birth_prescreen_credits_dictionary_saving_when_basis_narrower_than_span . ok
birth_prescreen_verdict_agrees_with_full_eq4_bits ....................... ok
birth_prescreen_selects_same_winner_as_unscreened_eq4_race .............. ok
crossover_says_no_on_the_control_case ................................... ok
fully_reconstructed_null_harvests_no_birth ............................. ok

```

### One red root-caused + fixed this session (82e476cb7)

`residual_bearing_fit_harvests_birth_proposal` was failing. Root cause was NOT an unrelated bug: the birth-proposal channel (`harvest_move_proposals`) now embeds this very pre-screen and only proposes births with predicted ΔMDL > 0. The test's fixture injected a rank-1 **linear** residual (span≈1) into a single-atom dictionary (G=1), which the theorem **correctly defers** — no support saving (log₂(1)=0), negative code term, plus the decoder surcharge. The fixture predated the pre-screen wiring. Fixed by making it a genuine MDL-worthy curved birth: an overcomplete dictionary (G=8, L0=1) + a zero-mean rank-2 **circular** residual (local span ≈ 2), so the channel harvests the birth via the ADMIT path. No pre-screen weakening — the theorem's support+curvature win is what makes the birth pay.

### ISSUE #2234 [OPEN] — On-manifold causal steering: chart-coordinate interventions (dose in radians), collateral-damage curves, crosscoder transport test
Author: SauersML   Created: 2026-07-09T14:03:03Z   Labels: 
Comments: 16
------------------------------------------------------------------------
BODY:
# On-manifold causal steering: interventions parameterized by chart coordinates (the behavior/causality epic)

## The idea

A flat SAE steers by adding a fixed direction: x' = x + α·w. Off any data manifold, the model sees an input it never produces — perplexity spikes, effects entangle, and α is a meaningless unit.

A manifold SAE gives a STRONGER intervention primitive: each atom k is a chart (t ∈ M_k, amplitude a, decoder Φ(t)·B_k). Steering = move the CODE, not the ambient vector:

    x' = x + a·(Φ(t ⊕ δ) − Φ(t))·B_k        (⊕ = manifold group action: rotate the circle phase, translate the patch, walk the torus)

Three properties flat steering cannot have:
1. **On-distribution by construction**: x' stays on the atom's decoded image — the intervention moves along the model's own feature geometry, never off it.
2. **Meaningful units**: δ is an intrinsic coordinate (radians of day-of-week phase; arc-length after #2022 unit-speed retraction), comparable across tokens and features.
3. **Content/intensity split**: t-steering changes WHICH value the feature takes at fixed strength; a-steering changes STRENGTH at fixed value. Flat conflates them in α.

## Experiments (concrete, cheapest first)

**E1 — Calendar circles (GPT-2, fixture exists).** `crates/gam-sae/tests/data/engels_gpt2_calendar_sae_indices.json` + the calendar ground-truth benchmark (tests/calendar_ground_truth_benchmark.rs) already pin day-of-week/month circle features. Fit the manifold SAE on the calendar cloud, then: encode "Tuesday" context → rotate t by k·(2π/7) → decode → patch the residual stream → measure P(next-token = target weekday). Prediction: t-rotation cycles the weekday distribution SMOOTHLY (P peaks track the rotation), while matched-norm flat-direction addition degrades into noise off the feature's circle.
- Metrics: (i) steering accuracy: argmax next-token weekday follows the rotation; (ii) KL(model || base) at MATCHED effect size — on-manifold should dominate (less collateral distribution shift per unit of achieved effect); (iii) dose-response linearity in δ (flat has no comparable dose axis).

**E2 — Collateral-damage curve (the headline plot).** For each intervention family, sweep achieved-effect (probability mass moved to the target) vs collateral KL on non-target tokens. On-manifold steering's curve should sit strictly below flat steering's. This is a clean, publishable claim: "curved features are the right control knobs."

**E3 — Crosscoder handoff (after #2231 Inc D).** With a two-layer crosscoder, steer t at layer l and READ the layer-(l+1) reconstruction through the SAME shared coordinate — the predicted downstream activation is B^(l+1)(t⊕δ) with no second fit. Compare predicted vs actual patched activation at l+1: a direct test that the shared-coordinate constraint captures the model's own feature transport. Drift statistic δ_k(l) (#2231 §3) quantifies where the prediction should degrade.

**E4 — Zoo ground truth (no LLM, runs locally).** The zoo generator plants factors with KNOWN θ per row (contribs carry theta). Steer the fitted atom's t by δ, decode, and check the reconstruction moves to the planted manifold point at θ+δ (R² of predicted-vs-planted moved contribution). This validates the primitive itself before any model surgery, in the local Rust harness (tests_zoo_micro_local.rs infrastructure, f11c4abd1).

## Infrastructure needed
- Rust: `SaeManifoldTerm::steer_rows(atom, rows, delta)` — group action on coords (Circle: phase add mod period; Euclidean: translate; product: per-axis), basis refresh, decode delta. ~50 lines next to the encode atlas; the group actions already exist in LatentManifold.
- pyffi: expose steer + decode-delta; python side patches residuals via the existing torch interop (declared interop lane, SPEC-clean).
- E1/E4 need no new model tooling; E1 patches GPT-2 via the same activation-capture path that built the calendar fixture.

## Why this increases scope correctly
This is the "behavior and causality experiments" goal item, grounded in the two artifacts we uniquely have: charts with intrinsic coordinates (nobody else's SAE can dose in radians) and (soon) cross-layer shared codes. Every experiment doubles as an eval: steering accuracy is a functional metric of fit quality that reconstruction EV cannot see — a dictionary can reconstruct perfectly and still steer badly if charts are mis-gauged.

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-10T20:23:09Z ---
## Plain-fit regression hunt — two more root causes fixed, one deterministic stall remains

Continuing the Blocker-2 bisection from the previous comment. Three defects found, all with measured repros:

1. **GMRES round-off-floor rejection (fixed, pushed):** the CG→GMRES rewrite gates success at relative residual ≤ 1e-10, below the attainable O(κ·ε) floor. Every exact-stationarity adjoint solve "failed" at ~4e-10 (numerically exact), every gradient eval died, and every plain-SAE fit refused at the seed. Fix: budget-exhausted solves with true residual ≤ √ε·‖rhs‖ are the round-off-floor solution and are accepted; worse residuals stay typed errors.

2. **Saturated degeneracy floor (fixed, pushed, regression-pinned):** `absolute_degeneracy_ev_floor = q/n` with reachable rank q ≥ n returns 1.0 — an unbeatable bar (the signal-free LS fit is *exact* at q ≥ n, so EV carries zero evidence). The co-collapse arm then branded an EV=0.999 fixture fit as degenerate ("EV 0.9990 at or below the signal-free null floor 1.0000") and burned reseed budgets on healthy dictionaries. Fix: saturated floor ⇒ NaN (the established no-verdict convention); detection falls to the relative-norm arm.

3. **Confirmed good:** the crosscoder block-relevance gradient (incl. the new exact adjoint) passes its full-engine central-difference gate on the fixed tree.

**Still red (deterministic):** the planted-circle synthetic (n=200, p=8, K=1) descends 63 healthy outer iterations, then hard-stalls with the objective frozen at 1.216074e2 and a bit-stable projected gradient 1.381e0 (bound 1.2e-3); all 8 stuck-stall escapes burn and the #2241 certified-termination contract refuses to mint. Reproduces identically with both fixes in. --- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-10T21:20:27Z ---
## Blocker-2 ROOT CAUSE (measured): value-probe lane walls at 1e12 where the gradient lane converges

The in-tree diagnostic (`tests_stall_diagnostic_2234::zz_planted_circle_plain_engine_stall_diagnostic_2234`, run `--nocapture`) reproduced the stall in the PLAIN Rust engine and caught the mechanism red-handed:

```
cost-only value 1.0000000000000000e12 disagrees with analytic-sample value
3.0654065812762929e2 at the selected point (roundoff bound 1.490e4)
```

At the SAME ρ, the **cost-only (line-search probe) lane returns the recoverable-refusal wall (1e12)** while the **ValueAndGradient lane returns the true criterion (306.54)**. The engine's own #2241-era consistency check detects the disagreement and refuses to mint. Per-coordinate FD at the banked ρ is wall-polluted for the same reason (coord 1: analytic −25.2 vs FD −21.7; coord 2: analytic +3.78 vs FD +0.128 — the ±h probes hit walls asymmetrically).

Mechanism: `is_recoverable_value_probe_refusal` classifies **"inner solve did not converge at fixed ρ"** as a recoverable infeasibility → `recoverable_refusal_wall_cost() = 1e12`. But the Value lane runs the CAPPED probe budget (#1029: probes never earn the progress extension), so near any ρ whose inner problem needs more than the probe budget, every line-search probe "fails to converge" → wall → Armijo rejects every step → the incumbent freezes while the (extended-budget) gradient lane keeps reporting a live gradient — the exact bit-stable |g|, frozen-cost stall observed everywhere today. Budget exhaustion is an UNFINISHED COMPUTATION, not an undefined Laplace evidence; walling it poisons line searches structurally. (The #1426 stuck-stall escape even uncaps inner PIRLS, but the wall fires inside the probe before the uncap feedback path can help.)

Fix direction (next commit): on a Value-lane probe whose inner solve fails ONLY on the budget marker, retry once at the accepted-point budget (or return the achieved non-certified cost) — reserve the 1e12 wall for the genuine non-PD/infeasibility classes it was built for.

(Every prior artifact — logs, perf profile, fixed wheel, raw OLMo pair — is harvested off the GPU box, which is now terminated per direction. The diagnostic runs anywhere; no GPU needed for this fix.)
