--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-11T04:56:00Z ---
## Intrinsic collateral-damage curve (E2) — Rust-owned, convergence-free, landed + CI-green

Inventory first: since the earlier close-audit comments the steering machinery has substantially landed on main and is wired — the chart-coordinate group action (`SaeManifoldTerm::steer_rows`/`steer_decode` + crosscoder-aware `steer_layer_delta`/`steer_layer_decode`, `decode_at_coords`), the single-move dosimetry (`inference::steering::steer_delta`: predicted-nats, validity radius, off-manifold guard), **E3** (`tests_steering_crosscoder_2234`, the two-layer shared-coordinate transport handoff) and **E4** (`tests_steering_e4`, zoo ground-truth θ-steer), plus FFI. The remaining gap versus the SPEC-is-Rust rule was the **collateral-damage curve**: it existed only as a Python read-off of model probabilities (`analyze_collateral.py`, E2), which is inherently model-in-the-loop and blocked on outer-fit convergence.

I added the Rust-owned intrinsic counterpart so the #2234 thesis can be decided structurally, with no LLM and no outer-loop convergence:

**`gam::inference::steering::collateral_curve(term, atom_k, axis, others, doses)`** — for each chart-coordinate dose it decomposes the steering move against every atom's local decode-tangent frame at its fitted operating point:
- **on-target effect** = `‖proj_{T_k} Δ‖` (energy on the steered atom's own frame),
- **collateral** = `‖Δ − proj_{T_k} Δ‖` (energy outside the target frame — the direct generalization of the single-move `off_manifold_norm` guard to a swept intervention),
- **cross-feature** = `sqrt(Σ_{j≠k} ‖proj_{T_j} Δ‖²)` (the interpretable "moved another named feature" leakage).

The flat control replays the **same per-row move norm** along the atom's dominant tangent direction (top singular vector of its tangent field — the manifold analog of a flat SAE's single decoder column; the mean tangent is unusable, it averages to ~0 over a circle). Each arm reports collateral-per-unit-effect efficiency and the dominance verdict. Exposed on `SaeCrosscoderFitReport::collateral_curve` and a thin `ManifoldCrosscoderCore.collateral_curve` FFI (wire dict).

### Measured (CI, `validate-one` run 29140124168, all green)

Local convergence-free E2 fixture (`tests_collateral_e2_2234`): two geometrically independent hand-built period-1 circle atoms (disjoint ambient planes), steering one:

```
[E2] collateral efficiency (per unit effect): manifold=0.5835  flat=1.0000  (lower is a cleaner knob)
```

- **cross-feature leakage onto the independent atom ≈ 0 in BOTH arms** (< 1e-9) — steering a feature does not spuriously activate a geometrically orthogonal one.
- **on-manifold collateral < flat at every dose**, and manifold efficiency 0.5835 < flat 1.0000 — the on-manifold chord tracks the rotating target tangent; the fixed flat direction is off it at most rows. This matches the closed form exactly (flat off-target RMS-fraction = `√0.5`; manifold = `sin(πδ)` per dose), so the number is analytic, not fit-noise.

Also re-confirmed green in the same run: **E3** `e3_crosscoder_handoff_uses_one_shared_moved_coordinate` (one shared moved coordinate decodes both layers, √λ removed), **E4** `zz_e4_zoo_circle_contrib_theta_steer_matches_planted_moved` (native EV=1.0, steered-vs-planted R²=1.0 at +π/2).

### Status
- **Built + verified now (no convergence needed):** the steering primitives, the crosscoder transport handoff (E3), the zoo θ-steer (E4), and the intrinsic collateral-damage curve (E2, Rust-owned) — all CI-green.
- **Still convergence-blocked (measure once lane-2015's LM fix lands):** the model-in-the-loop E1/E2 next-token-KL frontier on a real model (Qwen), which needs a real SAE fit that currently walls on the outer keystone.

SHAs on main: collateral primitive + E2 test + FFI landed via the checkpoint sweep at `193b0b0f4` (structs/`collateral_curve` in `inference/steering.rs`, `tests_collateral_e2_2234.rs`, `SaeCrosscoderFitReport::collateral_curve`, `ManifoldCrosscoderCore.collateral_curve`).

## `sae_manifold_fit` outer search cannot certify on current wheels — blocks every SAE acceptance lane (#2249 #2238 #2243 #2132, #2250's zoo arm)

**Micro-repro (deterministic, 6 min, CPU-only, 42 rows):** `~/plateau_repro.py` on the shared H100 box (`gam-dose-2249`, 192.222.52.187): K=1, `d_atom=1`, `atom_topology="circle"`, `n_iter=40` on the frozen Qwen L17 weekday activations (42×41 after the driver's exact orthonormal reduction; caches also at `$R/dose_qwen36b_out/rank8/` on MSI).

```
FIT_FAIL 364.5s RemlConvergenceError: SAE manifold primary outer search stopped
without a stationarity certificate (iterations=0, final_value=1.000000e12, ...)
```

### Measured failure anatomy on HEAD (wheel from 48bfe5865, today 19:01 UTC)

1. **Seed 0 is rejected before solver start** — the exact stationarity solve inside `eval_with_order(ValueGradientHessian)` reports non-identifiable:
   `solve_b_preconditioned_gmres: failed to converge in 90 iterations; original relative residual=2.455e-7` — **bit-identical residual across 3 processes and different `random_state`s.**
   This is with a FULL (un-truncated) Krylov space after 48bfe5865 (`restart=dim.min(128)`, `max_iters=2·dim`; before that fix it stagnated at 6.4e-8 with restart=32). Full-memory GMRES on a 45-dim system stagnating at 2.5e-7 ⇒ the system itself is near-singular (κ ≳ 1e9) — i.e. a near-null mode the `DeflatedArrowSolver` gauge deflation is not catching. The 1e-10 tolerance is NOT the bug.
2. **The surviving seeds descend into a deterministic non-stationary plateau**: `value=-1.588391e1` (rdim=41) / `-1.510221e1` (rdim=16), `|g|=7.707e0` / `1.427e1` vs certified-stationary band `~2.5e-2`, relative improvement <1e-7 over 6 accepted steps, `Strong Wolfe failed at iter 1` → backtracking accepts ε-steps forever. All 8 cost-stall escapes fire, then the typed exhaustion error. Same numbers on every retry ⇒ seed-independent.
3. **A banked incumbent at best cost −39.207 exists in the checkpoint** while the search grinds at −15.88 — the resumed search neither adopts nor reaches its own banked best.
4. **Input geometry is exonerated**: singular spectrum of the demeaned 42-row matrix is smooth (head `1, 0.246, 0.225, 0.198…`, worst kept ratio 0.011 ⇒ κ≈90 in the fit subspace). Reducing to rdim=16 or 8 does not change the failure mode.

### It is not one bad commit — both current wheels fail differently

- **Yesterday's PyPI `gamfit==0.1.252`** (2026-07-09 15:37) on the same repro: infinite **#1026 EV-keyed incumbent-restore churn** — `[#1026] restoring inner-fit reconstruction incumbent after EV degraded from 0.7880 to 0.7631` repeating every ~1 s for 20+ min (the #2230/#2134 churn root, since fixed on HEAD by the objective-keyed arbitration).
- **HEAD**: the churn is gone, but the fit now dies as above.
- **Last known-good**: the ~2026-07-04 wheel that produced `$R/dose_qwen36b_out/rank{8,32,64}` (this exact fit, `reconstruction_r2≈0.98` on the 8B analogue) and the 07-08 Kimi emotion fits.

### Blast radius (all measured today)

- The **12-factor acceptance zoo** sat 65 min inside its FIRST `sae_manifold_fit` call at 8–18 cores with zero output (py-spy: `sae_manifold_fit → _fit_ours_rust → main`) — so #2238/#2243 acceptance can't run.
- The corrected #2132 EV-vs-K sweeps call the same entry — blocked.
- The #2249 exact dose replay needs the K=1 chart fit — all 3 driver attempts (n_iter 40/60/80, distinct seeds) exhaust identically — blocked.

### Suspect surface

The plateau signature (huge |g|, zero objective progress, Wolfe failing at iter 1) is the classic **objective↔gradient desync** class, and the seed rejection points at the gauge/deflation seam (`DeflatedArrowSolver` / exact stationarity system) — both under active refactor today (`OuterCriterionCertificate` rename churn, arrow_solver deflation work). --- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-11T00:11:05Z ---
**Root cause of the seed-rejection half found and fixed (44fac6ac0): the circle chart's phase-shift gauge orbit was never declared to the deflation.**

`dense_step_gauge_vectors` deflates translation/scale orbits for Linear/Euclidean/Poincaré charts and the circle-axis shift for `Cylinder` (whose comment even says it matches 'the AtomTopology::Circle identifiability choice') — but `Periodic` and `Torus` fell through to the empty match arm. So a K=1 circle fit's exact stationarity system is **singular along the global phase orbit** at phase-symmetric iterates. That is exactly what the repro measured: full-Krylov GMRES stagnating at a bit-identical 2.455e-7 relative residual across seeds and processes, and every seed rejected 'non-identifiable' before the solver starts (`iterations=0`).

Fix: each periodic axis (circle = 1, torus = 2) now declares its constant-shift field as a gauge candidate; the existing Rayleigh floor still prunes any candidate that is not genuinely flat, so evidence-pinned phases are unaffected. Combined with the escape-budget replenishment (earlier in this thread), both measured failure modes now have landed candidate fixes. Verification runs on the standing acceptance job's gate (frozen weekday-cache K=1 repro) — next green wheel at ≥44fac6ac0 tests both together.

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-11T02:01:42Z ---
## Empirical verification of both fixes (build-free, ferried wheel at cd88182fa) + a confirmed residual

**FIX 1 (phase-gauge) works exactly as designed.** On the frozen weekday-cache K=1 circle repro: seed rejection is **gone** (no more `rejecting seed ... non-identifiable`, no 2.455e-7 GMRES stagnation), and the fit is **7–10× faster** (30–35s vs 250–364s). An independent static review confirmed the mechanism: `solve_b_preconditioned_gmres` uses the `DeflatedArrowSolver` as its B⁻¹ preconditioner, so the undeclared phase orbit made B singular along phase → both the bit-identical stagnation *and* the `raw_gauges.is_empty()` seed rejection. The row-level path (`push_atom_row_gauge_deflations`) already had a Periodic|Torus phase arm since ebbd5033f9; FIX 1 closed the step/outer-gradient path that fell through to `_ => {}`. `dense_step_gauge_vector_from_field` builds the matching decoder-β compensation by least squares, so the full null (coord shift + β) is deflated, and the Rayleigh floor (1e-8·max_pivot) still prunes evidence-pinned phases.

**Residual (NOT closed by either fix):** the fit now descends cleanly but stalls **non-stationary** and never certifies:
```
value=+67.95, |g|=8.948e-1  (escape band 1.034e-1, outer tol 1e-3)
Strong Wolfe fails at iter 0 → backtracking; objective CONSTANT across all 8 escapes
→ FLAT-VALLEY STALL, NON-CONVERGED
```
FIX 2 (escape replenishment) correctly does *not* fire here — the objective makes no super-floor improvement during the escapes, so there is nothing to replenish; it's not a multi-shelf descent, it's a hard stall.

**An rdim sweep proves it is a code bug, not conditioning:** rdim ∈ {4, 8, 12, 16, 24, 41} on the same 42-row cache — **every one fails to certify**, including rdim=4 (a well-conditioned 42×4 problem, data spectrum smooth: 1, 0.246, 0.225, …). So the n≈p overparameterization hypothesis is dead.

**Signature = objective↔gradient desync (or non-descent step):** at |g|=0.89 a *correct* gradient always admits a descent direction (−g), yet Strong Wolfe fails at iter 0 and the objective won't move. The analytic outer gradient disagrees with the objective's local behavior. This is now the sole blocker for all six SAE acceptance issues (#2249/#2250/#2132/#2238/#2243/#2251). Repro (build-free, ~35s): the ferried-wheel gate in `msi_acceptance_prebuilt.sbatch` / `plateau_repro.py`.

## Cluster resolution status (2026-07-11) — both failure modes fixed, one confirming run owed

This session landed the engine fixes for both measured failure modes of the outer-search certification stall:

**Seed-rejection half** (undeflated near-null mode) — RESOLVED and empirically confirmed:
- Phase-gauge deflation (`44fac6ac0`) + GMRES round-off-floor acceptance (`93479c4c9`, `arrow_solver.rs`: accept true residual ≤ √ε·‖rhs‖ at budget exhaustion instead of refusing a numerically-exact solve). The 02:01 comment already verified seed-0 rejection is gone (7–10× faster).

**Flat-valley non-stationary plateau half** — root-caused and fixed:
- The residual was NOT a true objective↔gradient desync. It was the #2080→#2241 **1e12 budget-wall artifact**: a budget-limited inner solve mapped to the finite collapse wall, so every line-search probe direction saw a cliff and the fit froze at a live gradient. Fixes: progress-gated budget escalation (`construction_reml_evidence.rs` — a measurably-descending inner solve gets one extra window before the budget-death refusal), the cost-lane `value_probe_with_budget_rescue`, always-tight outer probes (`4ef1e4da7`), and the saturated-degeneracy-floor → NaN no-verdict (`feb6b00bb`, so healthy small-n/basis-rich fits aren't branded co-collapsed).
- **Proven on the in-tree synthetic gate** `zz_planted_circle_plain_engine_stall_diagnostic_2234` (wall-regression gate, GREEN — zero wall-cost probes, genuine descent).

Note the OLMo crosscoder gate uses `run_outer_rho_search=false`, so it does not exercise the outer certification path and cannot prove this alone — the real-data repro is required. Queued.

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-11T02:49:17Z ---
## EW line-search ruled OUT — the residual is a genuine objective↔gradient desync in the outer REML

Ran the build-free repro on a wheel with the phase-gauge fix **and** EW forcing disabled (the fleet has since removed the inexact line-search objective entirely, 3ff896439). The K=1 circle fit **stalls identically**:
```
value = 6.795128e1  (EXACTLY constant across all 8 escapes)
|g|   = 8.949e-1     (escape band 1.034e-1, outer tol 1e-3)
Strong Wolfe fails → backtracking to tiny steps STILL cannot decrease the objective
```
This is decisive: for a smooth f, steepest descent −g must decrease f for small enough α (f(x−αg) ≈ f(x) − α|g|²). It does not, even at tiny α. Therefore **the analytic outer gradient is not the gradient of the criterion being line-searched** — an objective↔gradient desync, independent of the line search and the gauge.

**It is a near-optimum desync, not a global one:** the fit descends fine from the seed to value≈68 (so the gradient is mostly right), then desyncs at the stall. That is the signature of a term that dominates only near stationarity — i.e. the **log-det evidence-derivative trace** ½·tr(H⁻¹ ∂H/∂ρ) (the #2087/#1038 desync locus), where the data-fit gradient has vanished and the criterion's ρ-dependence is carried almost entirely by the log-det term.

**Suspected interaction with the phase-gauge fix:** FIX 1 added phase-orbit deflation to the arrow solver, and the outer gradient's trace consumes the *deflated* inverse (`latent_inverse_diagonal_kept`). If the criterion **value**'s log-det is computed with a different (un-deflated) factor, grad ≠ d(value)/dρ exactly at the regime where the log-det dominates → this stall. Next step: verify the criterion log-det and the gradient trace use a consistent deflation/quotient. Build-free repro (~35–65s, ferried wheel): `plateau_repro.py` / `msi_acceptance_prebuilt.sbatch`.

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-11T02:51:27Z ---
## Refined mechanism + suggested fix

Reading `record_evidence_gauge_deflation_count` (construction_reml_evidence.rs:520): the criterion's `log_det = arrow_log_det_from_cache(&cache)` depends on the gauge-deflation COUNT, and each deflated direction re-anchors ½log|H| (a deflated direction is lifted to unit stiffness → contributes log 1 = 0, so cross-ρ values are only comparable at a **common** deflation dimension). The guard tolerates *smooth O(N)* count drift (benign for K≥2, where the count is a per-row-summed continuous quantity).

**But the phase gauge FIX 1 added is a SINGLE discrete direction (count 0 or 1).** If its eigenvalue sits near the Rayleigh floor (`evals[i] ≤ 1e-8·max_pivot`) at the stall ρ, it flickers in/out as ρ moves → a discrete ±1 re-anchor → a **step discontinuity in the reported criterion** that the fixed-ρ analytic gradient does not see. That is precisely the measured signature: value pinned at 6.795128e1, |g|=0.89, and no step (down to tiny α) can decrease across the jump.

**Suggested fix:** the circle/torus phase orbit is an *exact* gauge (global rotation + decoder compensation is an exact criterion symmetry, always flat by construction — unlike the empirical decoder-null candidates the Rayleigh floor exists to screen). It should be deflated **unconditionally** (stable count), bypassing the Rayleigh-floor threshold that lets a numerically-borderline eigenvalue flicker. That stabilizes the deflation dimension across the ρ-walk → removes the criterion discontinuity → restores gradient/criterion consistency. Needs one instrumented run (log the per-ρ deflation count on the repro) to confirm the flicker before landing. Build-free repro ~35–65s: `msi_acceptance_prebuilt.sbatch`.

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-11T03:22:19Z ---
## Next-layer diagnosis: the 1e12 wall is GONE; the residual is a curvature-floor refusal

Ran the definitive discriminator (fresh wheel at HEAD, plain K=1 circle, n=84/p=64, softmax): the fit **no longer hits the 1e12 budget wall** — my session's budget-escalation + cost-lane rescue fixed that. It now fails at a *deeper, different* point, after ~96s of genuine descent:

```
REML smoothing optimization failed to converge: non-identifiable:
solve_exact_stationarity: exact stationarity Hessian has non-positive
generalized curvature μ=-1.660836e-3; the inner state is not a stable minimum
```

**Precise location**: `construction_exact_hessian.rs:102` — the exact-stationarity IFT solve computes the generalized Rayleigh quotient `μ(x) = xᵀAx / xᵀBx` of the solution (A = exact inner Hessian incl. residual curvature ΔC; B = Gauss-Newton preconditioner, PD) and HARD-ERRORS on `μ ≤ 0`. The deflation path below it (isolate + project out the near-null direction via inverse power iteration) accepts only **positive** near-null directions (`v_mu > 0.0 && v_mu < rank_floor`, line 173).

**Assessment**: μ = -1.66e-3 is a *weakly*-negative curvature direction — a weakly-identified inner direction (the circle's amplitude/scale/residual-gauge, off the exactly-projected rotational gauge) that ΔC tipped just below zero. The Gauss-Newton inner solve converges to a point that's a minimum under B but marginally indefinite under the exact A. The `reml_criterion` evidence factor already tolerates exactly this (it spectrally deflates the indefinite inner direction, stiffening it to +1 — a ρ-independent contribution) and mints a finite evidence; the IFT solve should treat the same direction consistently (deflate it) rather than refuse the entire outer gradient. Refusing here is the residual #2253 stall — no wall, genuine descent, then a strict-minimum guard on a near-flat direction.

**Fix in progress**: extend the IFT deflation to project out near-null directions of *either* sign, with the identifiability floor made *relative* to the resolved-curvature scale (a μ of magnitude ~1e-3 is round-off-negligible only relative to the pencil's O(bulk) curvatures, so an absolute √ε floor is too tight). This matches the evidence factor's own indefinite-direction handling. Testing on the K=1 discriminator now.

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-11T04:08:48Z ---
## DEFINITIVE ROOT CAUSE (confirmed by a dedicated basin audit): value lane prices an ENVELOPE, gradient lane prices a SINGLE basin

The outer optimizer's two evaluation lanes price different functions:

- **Value lane** (line-search cost probe, `value_probe_with_budget_rescue`:2562 → `evaluate_envelope_value_probe`:2586) evaluates the **lower envelope** `V*(ρ) = min_b V_b(ρ)` over a bundle of inner basins: a discovery probe from the accepted basin (2609), re-converge every saved bundle member from its own state (2622-2626), take the argmin (2649), and install the argmin basin as a bitwise-ρ-keyed `probe_converged_handoff` (2679).
- **Gradient lane** (`eval`:3435) prices a **single basin**: consume the handoff iff one is parked at this exact bitwise ρ (3500-3507), else warm-start one trajectory from the accepted basin (3527-3532) and take cost + ∇f there (3553/3595). It **never runs the envelope**.

The intended coupling is the envelope theorem — the value lane installs the argmin basin, the gradient lane consumes it, so ∇f = ∇V_argmin = ∇V* a.e. That holds on a line-search **accept**. It **breaks at every `eval(ρ)` with no bitwise-matching handoff** — decisively at the **seed anchor** (bundle still empty): the anchor gradient is `g_0 = ∇V_accepted`, so the BFGS direction `d = −H⁻¹g_0` is a descent direction for `V_accepted` but **not** for the envelope the line search then measures (its probes discover a lower basin). Every step is rejected → Strong Wolfe fails at iter 0 → ρ frozen → the exact byte-identical stall (value=6.795128e1 constant, |g|=8.949e-1). Structurally the anchor gradient is always "one basin behind" — a lower basin is only ever discovered *during* the line search, never at the anchor.

**Fix (landing now):** extend the envelope-argmin basin selection to the gradient lane at every ρ — when no handoff is parked, run the same bundle-seed + discovery + re-converge + argmin selection and install the argmin state before `reml_criterion_with_cache`, so `∇f` is taken at the same basin the value lane prices. (Dropping the envelope instead would reopen the #2230/#2087 basin-jump pathology it was built to fix.) A secondary, independently-real desync also lands: the Value line-search order omits `add_fit_data_collapse_penalty` that the gradient lane adds (its comment claims it's 'on all lanes').

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-11T04:35:43Z ---
## Root cause NARROWED: the outer-ρ stall is an objective↔gradient desync INTERNAL to a single `eval()` — in the smoothing-coordinate gradient (log-det channel), not the gauge deflation

Two candidate fixes from this thread — the phase-gauge unconditional deflation (my `0aca0d576`, "deflate exact chart-gauge subspace unconditionally in outer-gradient solver") and the IFT indefinite-pencil deflation (`e4c0181b2`) — both landed and were verified BUILD-FREE on the frozen weekday-L17 K=1 circle repro (MSI). **Neither changed the stall.** The first wheel (`ea94ad842`) reproduced the stall byte-identically (value=6.795128e1 constant, |g|=8.949e-1). `defl=0` throughout the fit, so the phase-gauge deflation never even engages on this case — the flicker hypothesis is dead here.

### Instrumented the outer eval directly (log::warn surfaces to the MSI .out)

**Falsified: the value-lane vs gradient-lane mismatch.** I tagged `eval_cost` (`OuterEvalOrder::Value`, the line-search value lane) with `[2253-VLANE]` and `eval` (`ValueAndGradient`, the gradient lane) with `[2253-GLANE]`. The VLANE tag **never fired once** — for this K=1 circle the outer optimizer only ever calls `eval()`. So the desync is INTERNAL to a single `eval()`: the criterion value and its OWN analytic gradient disagree.

**Decisive evidence** (`[2253-GLANE]`, wheel `17db0aa50`):
```
Region A: rho=[-1.62, -0.811, -1.532]  cost=6.862559e1 (LOWEST recorded)  |g|=1.092  logdet=256.88
Region B: rho=[-1.62, -1.123, -1.566]  cost=6.863070e1 (HIGHER)           |g|=0.147  logdet=258.47
```
The analytic gradient flows to B (|g|→0.15), but B has HIGHER cost than the recorded minimum A. So `−g` is not a descent direction of the returned cost: **`grad ≠ d(cost)/dρ`**. The optimizer's best_value pins at A (|g|=1.09, never inside the 0.10 stationary band), so it never certifies.

### Localized to the log-det gradient channel

I logged the four separable terms of `SaeOuterRhoGradientComponents` per ρ coordinate (`[2253-TERMS]`): `explicit` (data-fit), `logdet_trace` = ½tr(H⁻¹∂H/∂ρ), `occam`, and `adjoint` = −½Γᵀθ̂_ρ. Findings:

- `rho[0]` (assignment log-strength) is pinned; the desync is on the smoothing coords `rho[1]`, `rho[2]`.
- `occam = [0, −3.0, 0]` is **constant** across all ρ — correct (it is the λ-independent `−½·r·rank(S)` Occam-normalizer derivative). Not the culprit.
- Reconstructing `d(cost)/dρ₁` by finite-difference from the dense ρ trajectory: near region A the TRUE slope is small (≈−0.13), but the analytic total `g₁ = explicit+logdet_trace+occam+adjoint = 3.657+0.497−3.0−0.068 = +1.086`. Wrong magnitude AND sign.
- The log-det **value** `log|H|` swings ≈+1.6 across A→B (`d(log|H|)/dρ₁ ≈ −5`), yet the analytic log-det derivative `logdet_trace + adjoint ≈ +0.43` at those points — off by roughly an order of magnitude and opposite sign.

**Conclusion:** the analytic REML criterion is correct through most of the descent (the fit reaches value≈68.6 fine) but its ρ-gradient is wrong near the optimum in the **log-det evidence-derivative channel** (`logdet_trace = ½tr(H⁻¹∂H/∂ρ)` and/or the `adjoint = −½Γᵀθ̂_ρ` implicit-state envelope). This is the #2087/#1038 log|H|-gradient desync class, exactly where the earlier review pointed — the data-fit gradient has vanished and the criterion's ρ-dependence is carried almost entirely by ½log|H|, so a small error there dominates and steepest descent cannot decrease the true criterion.

### Recommended next step (owner needed)

Isolate `logdet_trace` vs `adjoint` with an **axis-aligned per-coordinate FD of the criterion value inside a TEST harness** (FD is SPEC-legal in tests; the production FD probe is auto-stripped). The in-tree synthetic `zz_planted_circle_plain_engine_stall_diagnostic_2234` is the natural home if it reproduces this desync; otherwise a K=1 circle fixture built from the weekday-L17 cache. Compare each analytic term to its FD to pin which of ½tr(H⁻¹∂H/∂ρ) or −½Γᵀθ̂_ρ is wrong, then fix the assembly in `analytic_outer_rho_gradient_components_with_bundle` (`construction_exact_hessian.rs`).

Diagnostics were temporary log::warn probes (`[2253-VLANE]`/`[2253-GLANE]`/`[2253-TERMS]`) in `outer_objective.rs`; removing them. Raw MSI logs available on request (jobs 12972309, 12972814).

### Addendum: why the existing FD gate missed this, and the concrete fix path

The in-tree `zz_planted_circle_plain_engine_stall_diagnostic_2234` (tests_stall_diagnostic_2234.rs) already does a per-coordinate central-difference vs the analytic outer gradient — but it has two gaps that let it PASS while the real fit desyncs:

1. It finite-differences `objective.eval_cost(&x)` (the `OuterEvalOrder::Value` lane) against `objective.eval(&x).gradient` (the `ValueAndGradient` lane). The MSI probe proved the value lane is NEVER exercised in the real fit — the desync is `eval`'s gradient vs `eval`'s OWN cost. The FD in the gate should use `objective.eval(&x).cost`, not `eval_cost`, or it can pass on a lane the optimizer doesn't use.
2. The fixture is a dim-3 periodic / softmax cloud (n=200, p=8); the failing repro is dim-1 `circle`, `top_k=None`/single-atom, n=42, p=48. The desync may be dim-1-specific, so the dim-3 fixture likely doesn't reproduce it.

Concrete fix path for the owner:
- Point the gate's FD at `eval(&x).cost` and add a fixture arm matching the repro (K=1, d_atom=1, `circle`). Turn the per-coordinate `|analytic − fd|` into an assertion (it should be RED until the derivative is fixed).
- Additionally FD `arrow_log_det_from_cache(&cache)` vs `logdet_trace + third_order_correction` per coordinate to split whether the error is in the fixed-θ trace `½tr(H⁻¹∂H/∂ρ)` (`decoder_smoothness_effective_dof_*` / `ard_log_precision_hessian_trace*`, construction_exact_hessian.rs:639/680) or in the `−½Γᵀθ̂_ρ` envelope adjoint (`logdet_theta_adjoint*` + `solve_exact_stationarity`, :696-711). --- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-11T05:42:52Z ---
## Course-correction: the desync is a DIRECT gradient term, NOT the IFT/adjoint path

Verified on MSI wheel `be61f37f` (which already contains the combined #2253 IFT fixes `9d15eb231` + `8ff1031fa` + `0e86795c3` + `5406b7b6c`): the K=1 circle repro still fails with the projected gradient **`|g| = 1.092` bit-identical** to before any of them. Five lanes of `solve_exact_stationarity` / pencil-deflation / θ-adjoint / assignment-strength fixes moved the gradient by **zero bits**.

Conclusion: the objective↔gradient desync is **not** in the IFT response (`third_order`/adjoint) or the deflation screen. Because `|g|` is deterministic and bit-stable across all those changes, the wrong contribution is a **direct-computed term** that none of them touch — the `explicit` penalty-energy derivative (`½λ θ̂ᵀS_k θ̂`, from `decoder_smoothness_value_per_atom` renormalized to `loss.smoothness`) or the `logdet_trace` EDF (`½λ tr(H⁻¹ S_k)`), on the smoothing/ARD coordinates. (An earlier "adjoint collapsed ~19×" read was from a **trajectory** finite-difference across probe-vs-accepted iterates, which conflates coordinate moves with inner-state noise — disregard it; only axis-aligned FD is trustworthy here.)

Isolation method (in progress across lanes): axis-aligned central FD at the stalled ρ of the log-det VALUE `arrow_log_det = log|B|` vs the analytic log-det channel `logdet_trace + third_order`, and of `loss.smoothness` vs `explicit`. Whichever channel's ½·FD disagrees with its analytic term names the wrong `∂H/∂ρ` block. The `zz_planted_circle_plain_engine_stall_diagnostic_2234` gate (now FDing `eval()`'s own cost) is the home for this; it needs the per-piece split.

Warning restated: a "curvature-widen the stationarity certificate" change must NOT be allowed to certify this `|g|=1.092` point — that would ship a non-stationary fit and hide the bug. The gradient term must be corrected.


--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-11T06:05:25Z ---
## Certification cluster resolved — root cause was the raw-gradient ladder pre-empting the projected-gradient certificate

The final layers of this were two coupled defects where a **genuinely stationary** outer-REML fit never reached its certificate:

**1. Railed-boundary / 0-iteration handoff.** `run_outer_uncertified` errored ("all declared solver plans exhausted... after 0 outer iterations") whenever no plan's *own raw-gradient* convergence test accepted. But that test cannot see a railed or already-stationary optimum: at a smoothing parameter railed to the ρ box floor (λ→0 — an exact linear fit, or a separated smooth), the **raw** gradient stays large along the railed axis (it "wants" to push past the boundary), so the solver reports non-convergence and takes zero steps — even though the KKT-**projected** gradient (which zeroes outward-railed axes) is stationary. Only `certify_outer_optimality` computes that projected gradient. Fix: `run_outer_uncertified` hands its best finite checkpoint to the mandatory certificate, which is the sole authority on stationarity (and still rejects genuinely divergent fits). *Proof: `shared_tangent_*` pyffi tests — `ρ=[-30,-4.65,-30,-30]`, 3 axes railed, |Pg|=2.2e-4 below its 9.0e-3 bound — green ×4.*

**2. Curvature widening was over-gated.** The Newton-decrement certificate (½·gᵀH⁻¹g ≤ objective_tol ⇒ "no further descent possible") was gated to a `CostStallFlatValley` exit reason. But a 2-parameter Gaussian-linear REML that lands λ→0 is already stationary at iteration 0 (`operator_stop_reason = None`), with |Pg|=1.1e-7 sitting just above an absolute `score·1e-9 = 8e-8` floor tighter than the REML gradient's own factorization round-off. The decrement test **is** the certificate; the exit reason is irrelevant. Ungated it — safety is unchanged (self-limiting; requires PSD-along-gradient curvature; `certifies()` still rejects a globally-indefinite Hessian). *Proof: new `gam-solve` unit tests `curvature_widening_certifies_stationary_point_on_any_exit_reason` (certifies) and `curvature_widening_still_rejects_genuine_nonstationarity` (rejects |Pg|=1.0) — both green.*

Commits: `095e4a9ee` (both fixes), `4f4d47ce5` (regression guards). Combined with the earlier layers (progress-gated budget escalation, μ≤0 IFT deflation, GMRES-exhaustion isolate, transient-wall→analytic adoption, and the curvature-scaled flat-valley bound `450915f55`), the fit now optimizes and certifies interior, railed, and flat-valley optima alike.

## Production-fixture measurement + a reconciliation: option C and the #2228 globalization fix are not competing

Two data points and one synthesis, to keep the fix search from looping.

### Measured: the outer stall is budget-independent (production 42×41 weekday-cache dose fixture, K=1, `atom_topology="circle"`)
| run | n_iter (outer) | result | outer \|g\| | wall |
|---|---:|---|---:|---:|
| A_PROD40 | 40 | FAIL — "did not certify a stationary optimum" | **1.470e-1** | 487s |
| B_PROD200 | 200 | FAIL — "did not certify a stationary optimum" | **1.470e-1** | 450s |

The outer certificate `|g|` is **identical to 4 sig figs** at n_iter 40 and 200. A 5× outer-budget increase moves the plateau by zero — consistent with the inner solve flooring at a fixed residual in this range rather than slowly approaching KKT (see #2228's inner-‖g‖ trajectory, which localizes this to inner-solver instability, not a budget shortfall).

### Reconciliation: the "gradient correction" and "inner globalization" fixes do not conflict
Two lanes have been treating these as competing directions; they are not.

- The **#2228 diagnosis is the root**: the inner solve is unstable (no monotone-descent globalization gating step acceptance); once it genuinely reaches KKT, the envelope holds and the outer gradient — which inner-FD confirms is correct — is right as-is. Fix = trust-region/line-search that rejects non-descent steps. This needs no gradient change.
- **Option C** (the non-envelope term `rᵀθ̂_ρ`; note it has been applied and reverted repeatedly and is **not on current main** — main `ff5fdf4a0` is the baseline stationary-only contract) is **gated on `‖r‖ > tol`** by design, so when the inner reaches KKT `r → 0` and the term **vanishes**. Whether or not C is present, it is a no-op exactly where the globalization fix takes effect — so it is at worst a harmless safety net for a residual off-KKT accept, not a rival to the globalization fix. The two need not be reverted against each other.

### What does NOT fix it
"Require-stationary" alone (a pure revert to the baseline gradient) leaves the production fit stalling at `|g|=0.147`. #2253 should not be considered closed on that state.

### Close gate
The inner-globalization fix landing AND the production fit certifying with a real fitted circle (a genuine stationary optimum), verified in isolation — not option C alone, and not a generic projected-gradient certificate guard. --- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-11T17:33:29Z ---
ARD fixed-state channel audit (FD +0.208 vs analytic +1.066), static pass over the explicit+trace pair:

**Ruled out — the majorizer-clamp hypothesis.** Both `ard_log_precision_hessian_trace` and `coordinate_block_ard_log_precision_hessian_trace` contract `w·prior.hess.max(0.0)` (construction_ard.rs), and since V'' is linear in α (Euclidean V''=α; von-Mises V''=α·cos κt), ∂max(V'',0)/∂logα = max(V'',0): the clamped kernel is exactly the derivative of the majorized log-det the value factors. The explicit channel (energy + normalizer derivative, incl. the #1113-safe I1/I0 ratio) also matches `ard_value` term-for-term.

**Remaining suspect — the dispersion→rank-charge coupling.** `hard_rank_charge_derivative` fills `direct_rho` ONLY at the λ_smooth indices; its within-branch ∂/∂logα is zero by the integer-MP-branch assumption. But `reconstruction_dispersion` depends *continuously* on α through the ARD-shrunk coordinate edf (n_active − α·tr(H⁻¹), plus the #2133 SURE deflation), and φ̂ feeds `recon_spectrum`'s noise edge — so an FD probe in logα can move the MP hard count across a branch (an O(½·edf·log N_eff) value jump per unit rank) that the analytic channel holds constant by contract. A 5× fixed-state mismatch is the size of exactly one such branch event divided by the FD step. Suggested unit test: recompute `rank_hard` at logα ± h on the frozen #2253 state and check whether the count moves; if it does, the FD is differencing across a rank-charge kink and the analytic gradient is correct on its branch — the fix is FD-step branch pinning in the probe, not a formula change.

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-12T12:07:21Z ---
## The plateau is an outer-step overshoot, not a certifier-strictness gap — and the outer problem is dim=2 (exact Hessian ~free)

Follow-up to the real-GPT-2 repro above, now with the **gradient-lane** trajectory (order=ValueAndGradient), which changes the diagnosis. It is NOT a near-stationary point the certifier wrongly rejects — ‖g‖ is *large and non-decreasing*, and the cost oscillates:

| outer iter | cost | ‖g‖ |
|---:|---:|---:|
| 0 | 2657.08 | **1.176** |
| 1 | 2542.51 | **43.97** |
| 2 | 2500.56 | 42.67 |
| 3 | 2295.06 | 41.50 |
| 4 | 2637.07 | **36.11** |

Two things stand out:

1. **The first step overshoots catastrophically.** Iter 0 is *near-stationary* (‖g‖ = 1.18) — the resumed search sits close to a critical point. Yet the very first step drives ‖g‖ to **44** (a ~37× jump) while the cost barely improves (2657 → 2542). A step that large from a gradient that small means the **step scaling is wrong**, not the gradient. Thereafter the iterate oscillates (cost 2295 ↔ 2637, ‖g‖ pinned ~40) and **never returns to the banked incumbent (best cost 2187.76)** — it diverges away from the good basin it resumed near. So the earlier Value-lane "plateau" (rho_distance frozen ~2.0, ~5e-4 cost change at iter 5) is the **line search failing to find descent along an overshooting Newton/BFGS direction**, downstream of this.

2. **The outer problem is `dim=2`, and the solver runs `hessian=Unavailable → BfgsApprox`.** A 2-parameter BFGS curvature estimate from a handful of evals is a poor Hessian, and a poor `H⁻¹g` is exactly what turns ‖g‖ = 1.18 into a step that lands at ‖g‖ = 44. But at **dim = 2 the exact Hessian costs O(dim) extra gradient evals** (or a 2×2 analytic block) — nearly free relative to a 7s eval.

**Suggested direction (does not re-tread the reverted option-C IFT adjoint — this is about the outer *step*, not `dV/dρ`):** for the low-dimensional outer REML problem, form the exact/FD Hessian and take a **trust-region-damped Newton step** instead of the `BfgsApprox` first-order bridge. From a near-stationary iterate (‖g‖ = 1.18) a proper Newton/trust-region step is tiny and the certifier closes; the current BFGS-approx step overshoots into the ‖g‖ ≈ 40 oscillation and can never certify. The dim=2 case makes the exact Hessian essentially free, so the usual "no Hessian at high width" objection doesn't apply to the E1/steering regime.

Fixture + seed (GPT-2 L7 weekday, K=1, seed 20260709) available if a real-data outer-step regression is useful.


--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-12T12:11:32Z ---
## The robust route already exists in the planner — E1 just misses it by declaring no Hessian

Traced the outer-step overshoot to the exact policy site: `gam-solve/src/rho_optimizer/capability.rs::plan()`.

- **The good path is already there** (`capability.rs:376`):
  ```
  (D::Analytic, D::Analytic) => OuterPlan { solver: S::Arc, hessian_source: H::Analytic }
  ```
  `Solver::Arc` is Adaptive Regularization with Cubics — a **trust-region Newton**, precisely the step that would kill the ‖g‖ 1.18→44 overshoot (from a near-stationary iterate ARC takes a properly-regularized tiny step; it can't blow up like the BFGS-approx `H⁻¹g` did).

- **E1 misses it** (`capability.rs:391`):
  ```
  (D::Analytic, D::Unavailable) if efs_plan_eligible() => { solver: S::Efs, hessian_source: H::EfsFixedPoint }
  ```
  The SAE manifold outer objective supplies an **analytic gradient but declares `Hessian::Unavailable`**, so the planner routes to EFS (and, on the non-finite-cost seed bail, to BFGS-approx) — the first-order bridge that overshoots.

**Minimal fix:** at low outer dimension (E1/steering is `dim = 2`), FD the *already-analytic* gradient into the exact 2×2 Hessian (~2–4 extra gradient evals — trivially cheap next to a 7 s eval) and have `declared_hessian_for_planning()` return `Analytic`. The planner then selects the existing `Solver::Arc + HessianSource::Analytic` route with no new solver code. This is orthogonal to the certification gate (option C / stationary-only contract) — it changes only how the outer *step* is taken, so a near-stationary start converges instead of oscillating at ‖g‖ ≈ 40.

The "no Hessian at high width" rationale behind the `Unavailable` declaration is real for k=10–50 smoothing params, but the E1/steering outer problem is `dim = 2`, where the exact Hessian is essentially free — so a dimension-gated declaration would keep the wide-p fast path untouched while fixing the low-dim overshoot.


--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-13T00:18:20Z ---
Three false-state paths are now removed on `main`: production finite-difference SAE curvature was deleted in `65aa93220`; schema-2 persistent iterates are invalid and cached Hessians are accepted only when the current objective declares analytic curvature (`84c8a625b` + `12f40caeb`); and EFS/MacKay proposal zeros can no longer certify the profiled objective—the final proof is the full analytic-gradient/KKT root, while matrix-free SAE without that proof surface disables fixed-point certification (`1da0c6d87`). `548eeb043` also upgrades checkpoint coverage from decoder-byte restoration to bit-identical authoritative objective and gradient replay.

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-13T16:58:25Z ---
## Path C (exact analytic outer Hessian) progress — 3 channels green, and a zero-row bug caught before the flip

**Context.** #2253 forbids finite differences in production certification, so the outer optimizer cannot use an FD Hessian to cross the E1 indefinite saddle. Path C builds the **exact analytic fixed-stratum outer Hessian** so the planner can declare `DeclaredHessianForm::Dense` and route ARC. Assembler: `SaeManifoldTerm::exact_fixed_stratum_outer_hessian` (construction_exact_hessian.rs).

### Landed + FD-gated
| Channel | Status | Gate |
|---|---|---|
| Occam | zero (ρ-independent) | n/a |
| Explicit smoothness + ARD | ✅ green | `outer_explicit_smoothness_ard_hessian` |
| Rank-charge `direct_rho` | ✅ green | `rank_charge_direct_rho_hessian` |
| **logdet Daleckii–Krein** | ✅ **green (job 13114288)** | `logdet_daleckii_krein_hessian_matches_finite_difference_2253` |
| Third-order forward-sensitivity | pending | — |
| **Sparse / softmax log-strength** | **MISSING — see below** | — |

The assembler still returns `Err(incomplete)` and `capability()` stays `Unavailable`, so **nothing steers on partial curvature**.

### The logdet channel needs TWO inverses, not one
The `logdet_trace` gradient channel is `½log|H| − ½Σ_i log|H_tt^(i)|` differentiated once — it carries a **coordinate-block subtraction**. So the D-K second derivative runs through two inverses: the full joint `G = H⁻¹`, and the **block-diagonal row-local** `H_bd⁻¹`. Uniform, no branching:

```
block[i,j] = ½·δ_ij·( tr(G Cᵢ) − tr(H_bd⁻¹ Cᵢ) )
           − ½·( tr(G Cᵢ G C_j) − tr(H_bd⁻¹ Cᵢ H_bd⁻¹ C_j) ),   Cᵢ = ∂H/∂ρ_i
```

It self-specializes: a smooth `Cᵢ` is β-only while `H_bd⁻¹` is t-only, so `H_bd⁻¹·C_smooth = 0` identically and the K-leg vanishes for smoothing with no special case. Sanity identity: the δ diagonal term equals that coordinate's own `logdet_trace` value exactly.

### ⚠️ Zero-row bug found before flipping (the important one)
The assembled Hessian has an **identically-zero row/column at the sparse (softmax log-strength) coordinate**, while the gradient there is nonzero. `sparse_flat_index` appears exactly **once** in the entire Hessian surface — inside the *gradient* assembler (construction_exact_hessian.rs:752) — and in **no** Hessian channel.

Had we flipped `capability()` → `Dense` with that, **ARC would have solved a singular system** and taken an arbitrary/unbounded step in ρ_sparse. That is **strictly worse than `Unavailable`**, where BFGS at least builds a curvature approximation. The E1 mint fixture `small_two_atom_periodic_term` is softmax(0.8), so `sparse_flat_index()` is `Some` and the mint route hits it directly.

The crosscoder `log_lambda_block` coordinates (#2231 block relevances) appear to have the **same** zero-row bug — and they are empty on the circle fixture, so no fixture would catch it.

**Root-cause fix, not a patch:** a **coordinate-coverage invariant** in the assembler — the set of flat coords the Hessian channels write must equal the set the gradient writes (smooth ∪ ard ∪ sparse ∪ log_lambda_block); any coord with a live gradient but a zero Hessian row must **refuse**, never return a singular block.

### Two false-green traps this work had to dodge (worth recording)
1. **Frozen-cache FD.** An FD gate that holds the factor cache fixed validates only the `δ` self-term and lets the *entire* D-K cross term (which exists only because `∂G/∂ρ = −G C_j G`) through unchecked. The FD **must** rebuild the fixed-θ̂ cache at each ρ±h.
2. **Penalty-floor vacuity.** At the fixture's default ρ=−6 floor, λ=α≈2.5e-3, so the D-K cross terms scale O(λ²)≈6e-6 — *under* the 1e-5 FD tolerance. The gate would have passed on the self-term alone. Fixed by lifting ρ and adding an **off-diagonal** non-vacuity assert (an off-diagonal has no δ term, so it is pure cross-term).

Tolerances were **not** loosened anywhere.

### Remaining to close #2253
CH4b (sparse logdet leg) → CH6 (sparse explicit ∂²) → CH5 (third-order, over **all** coords) → coverage invariant → **full-gradient** HVP·v vs FD gate on the softmax fixture → flip `Err`→`Ok` and `capability()`→`Dense`.

Note the general lesson: **every channel can be green while the channel *set* is incomplete.** Only the full-gradient gate checks the set as a whole. Per-channel greens are not sufficient to flip.

### ISSUE #2263 [OPEN] — Steering dosimetry calibration + structure_certificate unusable on real activations
Author: SauersML   Created: 2026-07-11T15:28:30Z   Labels: 
Comments: 6
------------------------------------------------------------------------
BODY:
**TL;DR:** On real Qwen3-8B activations (layer 20, weekday/month circles), the steering path works — but its **dose calibration is far off at defaults**, and the **e-value `structure_certificate` cannot run at all** because it requires a minted closed-form fit (see the solver issue #2258). Items 1–3 are calibration/UX improvements with measured numbers; item 4 is a dependency of the solver fix.

*AI-filed (Silico agent, run by Scott); numbers from recorded overnight-experiment artifacts.*

**Roadmap:** L11 in the five-experiment synthesis ledger (experiment #6); item 4 is the user-facing face of L6 (filed separately).

## 1. Default amplitude/dose scaling is far too small on real activations

`fit.steer` amplitude-1 plans produce ~0.02-nat realized doses that move nothing behaviorally. An alpha sweep to **16** was needed to reach behavioral effect: **85–89% calendar-move rate at the concept token** (weekday 89%, month 85%) vs **58–61% for the matched-norm in-chart control** (and ~16% for a matched-norm random ambient direction). A user following the documented recipe at default amplitude will conclude steering doesn't work.

## 2. Predicted-vs-realized KL goes nonlinear across layers

The endpoint output-Fisher dose meter tracks well at small doses in-layer (median realized/predicted ratio 1.16–1.35 at the final-token site) but is off by **22× at alpha = 1 down to 0.27× at alpha = 16** when the dose is set 16 layers before the readout. This blocked precise dose targeting: there was no reliable way to request "N nats at the output" from a mid-stack intervention. Closed-loop dosing (search alpha against realized KL) was the workaround; it could ship as the recommended cross-layer recipe.

## 3. Month steers overshoot the requested target

Month rotations move in the right direction but overshoot: requested advances of +1..+6 months realized a mode of **+8**. Same calibration root as (1)–(2), listed separately because it changes the sign of the UX problem (not "nothing happens" but "too much happens").

## 4. `structure_certificate` unusable on real activations (dependency)

The e-value structure certificate and `validity_radius` require a minted closed-form fit, and the closed-form engine never returns one on this data (#2258) — so no run in the study could produce a certificate. Not a separate bug: fixing #2258 (or letting the certificate machinery accept torch-lane fits) resolves this. Filed here so the linkage is on record: the steering path currently ships with its certification layer unreachable in exactly the setting people want to steer in.

## Evidence (recorded artifacts, cluster paths)

- Per-steer records (arm, k, alpha, outcome, realized KL): `/mnt/data/artifacts/silico/experiments/_flat/exp_01kx7r4wtte1b8w64efhcs99de/cyclic_qwen3_8b_l20/steer_*_records.jsonl`
- Output-Fisher factors used for the dose predictions: same dir, `steer_*_fisher.npz`
- Move-rate / coherence / KL summaries per arm and site: experiment #3's `results/steering_stats.json` (worktree)

------------------------------------------------------------------------

## Audit note: the Tier-0 frame confound also contaminated this issue's dosimetry; the 0/39 cert is a separate (convergence-wall) failure — both must clear before re-measure

Cross-linking the end-to-end calibration audit posted on #2249. Two independent defects sat under this issue's real-activation numbers, and they invalidate different halves:

1. **Dosimetry (shared with #2249).** The steering dose path (`steer_delta` → `0.5·δᵀMδ`) priced `δ` in the Tier-0 **standardized** decoder frame while the metric `M=UUᵀ` is in **raw** activation units — a per-column `1/σ_c` mis-scale (`D⁻¹MD⁻¹`), fixed in `ace3b9af3` and guarded by `predicted_nats_survive_tier0_frame_rescale_2249`. Any dose/collateral numbers this issue produced on real Tier-0-standardized fits before that commit are invalid and must be re-run. (Full mechanism, including the moderate-R²/off-slope signature and the validity-radius contamination, is on #2249.)

2. **structure_certificate 0/39 (the other half).** This is not a dosimetry bug — it is the #2228 convergence wall: on real activations (high residual, κ≈1e8 conditioning, flat frame bands) the K=1 chart fit could not reach a certifiable KKT-stationary optimum, so `structure_certificate` had nothing valid to certify. ### Re-measurement (both gated on #2253 resolving + a green wheel with `ace3b9af3` + #2228):

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-12T15:49:11Z ---
## Protocol v2 addendum: the fix is a target-dose API, not a magic amplitude (validate it in the re-measurement)

Item 1 of this issue ("dose scale", the `alpha≈16` / `amplitude=1.0` default in `examples/dictionary_cli.py`) has no principled resolution as a constant, because **`amplitude = 1` has no universal meaning** — the nats a unit amplitude buys depend on the atom, the operating point, the layer, and the metric scale. The right user surface, and what the re-measurement should validate, is a **target-dose** call `steer_to_target_nats(q*)`:

- **Closed-form first-order seed.** With `predicted_nats = ½·a²·dgᵀF dg` (`dg = g(t_to) − g(t_from)` the unit-amplitude chord), inverting for a target `q*` gives
  ```
  a0 = sqrt( 2 q* / (dgᵀ F dg) ).
  ```
  This is exact in the in-radius quadratic regime — and note it is **exact only because of `ace3b9af3`**: `dgᵀF dg` must be evaluated with `dg` and `F` in the same (raw) frame, which the Tier-0 un-scaling now guarantees. Pre-fix, `a0` would have inherited the per-column `σ_c` mis-scale.
- **Closed-loop patched-forward correction.** Cross-layer propagation and softmax saturation (mechanism C in the calibration audit) bend the true `a ↦ KL(a)` curve away from the quadratic past the readout/KL radius. So apply `a0`, measure `KL(a0)` by a patched forward, and secant/Newton-correct `a` on the measured curve until `KL ≈ q*` within tolerance. In-radius this converges in 1–2 forward passes (the seed is already right); it only spends extra passes exactly where the quadratic model breaks.

This is what converts the slope-mechanism decomposition into the **actual product fix**: the frame fix makes the closed-form seed correctly scaled, and the closed loop absorbs the residual saturation. No `alpha_search`/`target_nats` API exists today (grepped) — this is the design to build and then validate.

**Re-measurement acceptance for the API:** across features × layers × doses, `steer_to_target_nats(q*)` lands measured patched-forward `KL` within X% of `q*`, and report the number of forward passes to converge (should be ~1–2 in-radius, more only past the readout radius). Runs on the same frozen L17 environment as the calibration replay, post-#2253.

Cost anatomy for the 900-s example, from the full static audit: the wall time is multiplicative through the default pipeline — topology race (≤6 candidate REML fits/atom) × 2 structured-whitening passes (each installs a NEW likelihood and re-runs the entire outer ρ search) × outer iterations × line-search probes (each a full inner re-convergence to the same KKT gate) × refine rounds (16–64×) × up to ~1e3 inner iterations at contraction ~0.998. The landed stack shrinks the two innermost factors — the terminal Newton phase ends the ~1e3-iteration crawl in O(10) steps (#2228, `7763e8478`) and EFS routing (`072c01c57`) removes the per-probe full re-convergence lane for small fits (EFS has no line search) — and Tier-0 standardization (`d67d341c0`) cuts the κ that sets the crawl rate. ### ISSUE #2280 [OPEN] — Atlas-first manifold discovery: local charts + transition holonomy replace global-linear seeds and the fixed topology menu
Author: SauersML   Created: 2026-07-12T15:58:45Z   Labels: 
Comments: 4
------------------------------------------------------------------------
BODY:
## Principle

One model expression generalizing the zoo: **fit local charts, read topology from their transition graph, hand the recognized topology to the specialized chart families**. Swiss-roll unfolding, Möbius twist detection, seed-collision elimination, and a structural anti-collapse force all fall out as side effects of one mechanism — no shape-specific methods.

## The reframe

The K-atom SAE is already an atlas: atoms = charts, softmax gates = partition of unity, birth/death = atlas refinement, `chart_transfer.rs` = the transition-map algebra (`A_kj(x) = (J_k^T J_k)^{-1} J_k^T J_F(x) J_j(x)`, transfer certificates, `so2_polar_angle`). What's missing is (a) local seeding, (b) gluing consistency, (c) the discrete topology readout.

## Mechanism

1. **Local patch seeding**: deterministic farthest-point landmarks (the #2023 Tier-1 coordinate seeder pattern) → Voronoi neighborhoods → per-patch local PCA charts (d-dim). Local charts are always injective — small neighborhoods cannot fold — so the fold-failure class (swiss roll, spirals, entangled products) vanishes at the seed level. Patch radius selected by the spectral-noise-floor bandwidth doctrine (#2243), no user knobs.
2. **Gluing consistency**: on rows where two charts co-fire, their coordinates must relate by one smooth transition map — a penalty expressible with the existing pulled-back operators. This is also a principled anti-collapse force (#2132's functional-redundancy blind spot): two atoms decoding the same region either agree on a transition (one manifold → merge) or provably do not (genuinely distinct structure).
3. **Topology readout (holonomy + nerve)**: compose transition operators around cycles of the patch graph:
   - cycle, composed transition ≈ identity → **circle**;
   - cycle with **det < 0** composed Jacobian → orientation-reversing holonomy → **Möbius** (the half-twist as a discrete sign, replacing the fragile PC1/PC2/PC3 seed assumptions);
   - two independent cycles → **torus**; closed nerve with Euler characteristic V−E+F = 2 → **sphere**; trivial holonomy + planar nerve → **sheet** (gluing IS the unrolling — swiss roll needs no special method);
   - anything else → an honest new shape, reported as such.
4. **Promotion by MDL**: recognized topology → refit with the existing specialized zoo chart family (compressed, evidence-optimal); the patch-atlas → global-chart promotion is a #2233 description-length crossover event, priced by the existing birth-gate machinery. The zoo becomes the CLOSER; the atlas is the topology-agnostic OPENER.

## Relation to in-flight work

- Stage 0 (running, #2240): intrinsic-metric seed raced against PCA + topology-agnostic fold diagnostic — the tactical general fixes.
- This issue is the end-state: subsumes the swiss-roll/#2240 remainder, the Möbius seed fragility, the #2132 seed-collision mechanism (#4) and functional-redundancy gap (#2a), and extends the discoverable topology set beyond the planted menu.
- Reuses: chart_transfer operators + certificates, farthest-point landmarks, partition-of-unity gates, merge_tiers/terminal_joint_assembly, the Ville/MDL birth gates, spectral-noise-floor bandwidth selection.

## Acceptance

- Planted swiss roll (1.5+ turns): recognized as sheet, unrolled coordinates, held-out EV matching an oracle unrolled fit — with zero roll-specific code.
- Planted Möbius band: holonomy sign detected; handoff reproduces the existing deck-invariant fit.
- Planted circle/torus/sphere: recognition agrees with the current zoo race winners.
- Structureless noise: no topology recognized (nerve fragmentless), no false promotion.
- Determinism: bit-identical run-twice; all selection deterministic.

🤖 Generated with [Claude Code](https://claude.com/claude-code)
------------------------------------------------------------------------
COMMENTS:

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-12T16:10:42Z ---
## Geometry review of the topology readout (mechanism 3) — with numerics

I'm the geometry owner for this; the reframe is sound and the chart_transfer operator algebra + partition-of-unity gates are the right substrate. But I stress-tested the **holonomy + nerve** readout numerically (farthest-point landmarks → membership patches → nerve on point clouds of a sphere, torus, and disk), and there are three corrections that change the implementation, one of which you flagged and the numbers confirm.

### 1. The patch GRAPH does not give surface topology
The 1-skeleton (patches = vertices, pairwise overlaps = edges) gives only `V − E`. On my clouds that is `−64` (sphere), `−45` (torus), `−48` (disk) — it's `1 − b₁(graph)`, a property of the overlap graph, not the manifold. **Do not read χ or the handle count off the graph.** It over-counts cycles badly: a sphere's overlap graph is full of cycles, but they all bound higher simplices.

### 2. `V − E + F` (truncating the nerve at triples) is WRONG when 4+ patches co-overlap
This is the Euler-characteristic claim to fix. Truncated `V−E+F` gave **sphere = 7, torus = 12, disk = 5** — nowhere near `2 / 0 / 1`. The nerve is a simplicial complex of *every* order of common intersection; with a data cover, 4-, 5-, 6-way overlaps are non-empty, so you must take the **full alternating sum** `χ = Σ_k (−1)^k · N_{k+1}` where `N_j` = number of `j`-wise co-firing patch sets (rows where `j` charts' gates are jointly active). Truncation is only valid for a cover with no thick multi-overlaps, which a data-driven cover does not have.

### 3. Full-nerve χ recognizes sphere and sheet robustly, but the TORUS is fragile
With the full alternating sum:
- **sphere χ = 2** — rock-solid across landmark counts m∈{40,60} and membership k∈{4,6}.
- **disk/sheet χ = 1** — solid.
- **torus χ = {16, 6, 3, −13}** — garbage, unstable in m and k.

The sphere and disk work because they're simply-connected / contractible and a crude cover is already "good enough". The torus fails because the naive membership cover is **not a good cover** (Nerve theorem needs every nonempty finite intersection contractible); on a multiply-connected manifold the higher-overlap combinatorics are noise-dominated and χ does not converge. So **raw nerve χ is not a reliable torus detector** from a data cover.

### Consequence for the readout: holonomy is primary, χ is a sphere/sheet tie-breaker
Recognition should be layered by robustness, not treat χ and holonomy as co-equal:
1. **Orientation holonomy** (det-sign of the composed `chart_transfer` Jacobian around a nerve 1-cycle) — local, robust, and the RIGHT signal for Möbius vs cylinder and Klein vs torus. This is your strongest primitive.
2. **b₁ = cycle count** read from **H₁(nerve)** (graph cycles quotiented by the 2-cells), NOT raw graph cycles — else the sphere shows spurious 1-cycles. Circle b₁=1, torus b₁=2, sphere/sheet b₁=0. But note b₁ inherits the same good-cover fragility as χ for the torus, so cross-check it against the number of nerve 1-cycles carrying non-trivial transition holonomy (a handle carries monodromy; a spurious cover-cycle bounding a 2-cell does not).
3. **χ (full nerve)** as the **sphere-vs-sheet discriminator only** (both have b₁=0; χ=2 vs 1 separates them) — where it is robust.

Net: holonomy + orientation is the reliable core (and it's exactly what nails the two shapes we care most about — Möbius and cylinder); χ closes the simply-connected gap (sphere) where holonomy is blind (S² has π₁=0, every loop contractible, so **all** holonomy is trivial — you correctly noted the sphere needs the nerve); and the **torus needs a certified good cover** (contractible overlaps, e.g. radius from the spectral-noise-floor doctrine with an overlap-contractibility check) before χ or b₁ is trustworthy. I'd gate the torus verdict on that certificate rather than a raw count.

### Stage-0 validation (the tactical fix under #2240) is confirmed
The intrinsic-metric seeder is worth adding to the race exactly as framed. Isomap (kNN graph → geodesic distances → classical MDS to d dims) held-out reconstruction vs PCA seed on a thin-plate decoder:
- rolled 1.5 turns: PCA 0.985, **Isomap 0.999**, oracle-intrinsic 1.000
- rolled 3.0 turns (all three singular values comparable): PCA 0.937, **Isomap 0.996**, oracle-intrinsic 0.998

Isomap matches the oracle unrolled fit and beats PCA on folds; on non-folds it ties PCA. So racing intrinsic-vs-PCA under the same REML evidence (PCA wins when injective, cheaper) is the right shape-agnostic mechanism, and the swiss roll falls out with no roll-specific code — as the reframe intends.

I'll implement the readout with holonomy primary + full-nerve χ for the sphere gate + the good-cover certificate as the torus precondition, running as a diagnostic alongside the race first (recognition-only), and validate against the planted zoo before wiring promotion.

### ISSUE #2304 [OPEN] — GPU SAE row-jet missing latent-coordinate and logit-x-coordinate channels — cannot serve as production row jet
Author: SauersML   Created: 2026-07-13T05:13:02Z   Labels: 
Comments: 6
------------------------------------------------------------------------
BODY:
## Summary
The GPU SAE row-jet kernel covers only the gate-logit subspace of the derivative tower; latent-coordinate and logit×coordinate channels are missing, and the module doc explicitly forbids wiring it as the production row jet until they exist.

`crates/gam-sae/src/gpu_kernels/sae_rowjet.rs:17-21`:
```rust
//! This module currently accelerates the **gate-logit subspace** of that tower:
//! decoded values are device inputs and therefore constants with respect to the
//! `K` seeded logit primaries. It does not yet emit latent-coordinate or
//! logit×coordinate channels from the basis Jacobian/Hessian tensors. It must
//! not be described or wired as the complete production row jet until those
```

## Impact
The device-resident SAE fit (#1017 core, now closed) still round-trips to the CPU for the coordinate-bearing derivative channels; the GPU row-jet cannot take over the full inner solve until these channels are emitted. This is the concrete remaining kernel gap on the GPU cutover path — related to the #932 jet unification but not tracked by any open issue.

## Fix sketch
The basis Jacobian/Hessian tensors are already device-resident inputs; the missing channels are contractions of those tensors with the logit-seeded jet coefficients (latent-coordinate: J^T seeded-grad; logit×coordinate: mixed second-order contraction). Emit them in the same kernel launch to keep the tower single-pass, and gate parity vs the CPU RowProgram tower at 1e-12 as with the existing channels.

|---|---:|---:|---:|
| `sae_rowjet_second` | 9 | 7.106 ms | 789.6 us |

The same trace also exposed the remaining root cause, so I am **not closing this issue yet**. At 100 ms sampling, SM utilization peaked at only 12% (1.63% whole-run mean; 5.5% mean over nonzero samples), with 519 MiB peak VRAM and 55.64 W peak power. Nsight attributes 542.688 ms / 83.7% of GPU memory-operation time to 36 device-to-host copies and another 103.432 ms / 15.9% to 108 host-to-device copies; the 36 kernel launches total only 9.947 ms.

This is structural, not a batch-size artifact: `device_tile` rebuilds every tensor into host `Vec`s on every call, performs twelve H2D uploads, allocates four output buffers, then performs four D2H downloads. The sole production caller immediately converts those downloaded arrays into host scheduled rows. Thus the newly completed derivative tower is exactly correct on CUDA, but it still cannot serve as a device-resident production row jet and the requested single-pass cutover is not complete.

The principled next boundary is a device-resident tile/channel handle: persist and reuse shape-stable buffers, upload row-varying inputs once, keep the complete first/second/beta/mixed tower resident through its downstream contraction/reduction, and transfer only the final reduced result. Shared primary/beta layouts should be uploaded once per shape. Kernel fusion should then be judged from the resident trace rather than used to hide PCIe traffic.

### ISSUE #2310 [OPEN] — Quotient-chart census: spectral-mask theorem closes the zoo (RP², Klein bottle); flat-vs-embedded torus is a closed-form penalty, not a topology
Author: SauersML   Created: 2026-07-13T05:17:12Z   Labels: 
Comments: 5
------------------------------------------------------------------------
BODY:
# Quotient-chart census: the spectral-mask theorem closes the low-dim zoo (RP², Klein bottle) and the flat-vs-embedded torus is a penalty, not a topology

## Motivation

`SaeAtomBasisKind` grew shape-by-shape: circle, sphere, torus, cylinder, Möbius, Duchon sheet. The Möbius evaluator (`crates/gam-sae/src/basis.rs:2577`, `MobiusHarmonicEvaluator`) quietly landed the *general* mechanism — a deck-invariant subspace of a covering space's harmonics — as a one-off. This issue states the theorem that makes that mechanism the census-closing principle, derives the two missing closed 2-manifolds (RP², Klein bottle) as pure column masks over evaluators we already have, and resolves the flat-vs-embedded torus question by deriving the exact closed-form Laplace–Beltrami penalty of the donut torus (it is banded with geometrically decaying closed-form entries). No new latent-manifold variants, no new gauge machinery, no new solver paths.

## 1. The spectral-mask theorem

**Setup.** Let `X` be a model geometry with a computable harmonic basis and isometry-invariant spectral penalty: for us `X = S²` (spherical harmonics `Y_lm`, penalty eigenvalues `l(l+1)`) or `X = T² = R²/2πZ²` (Fourier modes `e^{i(kθ+lφ)}`, penalty eigenvalues `k², l²` per channel). Let `Γ` be a finite group of isometries of `X` acting freely, and `M = X/Γ`.

**Theorem.** Functions on `M` are exactly the `Γ`-invariant functions on `X`. Since every `γ ∈ Γ` is an isometry, the pullback `γ*` commutes with the Laplace–Beltrami operator `Δ_X`, hence the averaging projector

    P_Γ = (1/|Γ|) Σ_{γ∈Γ} γ*

commutes with `Δ_X` and preserves each eigenspace. Therefore:

1. **Basis**: an orthogonal harmonic basis for `M` is the `Γ`-invariant subspace of `X`'s basis — computable as a *selection rule* (column mask) whenever `Γ` permutes basis elements up to sign.
2. **Penalty**: the isometry-invariant penalty on `M` (any spectral function of `Δ_M`, e.g. `∫(Δf)²` or `∫|∇²f|²`) is the restriction of `X`'s penalty to the masked columns — *same eigenvalues, same diagonal structure, zero new code*.
3. **Null space**: `ker` of the penalty on `M` = `Γ`-invariant part of `ker` on `X`. For every closed case below this is exactly the constants.
4. **Latent chart**: rows keep coordinates on the *cover* `X` (existing `LatentManifold::Sphere`/`Product(Circle,Circle)` — `crates/gam-terms/src/latent.rs:189`). Because every basis column satisfies `φ(γ·t) = φ(t)`, the per-row NLL is exactly deck-invariant: the trust-region row solve is well-posed on the quotient with no modification. This is precisely the contract the Möbius evaluator already enforces (`basis.rs:3349` test `mobius_basis_is_invariant_under_deck_transform`).

**Census (why exactly two kinds are missing).** Closed surfaces admitting a geometry with closed-form harmonics: curvature +1 → `S²` (landed) and `RP² = S²/{±1}` (missing); curvature 0 → `T²` (landed) and the Klein bottle `K = T²/ι` (missing). Flat-with-boundary: cylinder (landed), Möbius (landed). Genus ≥ 2 is hyperbolic; its harmonics (Maass forms) have no closed form — that stratum is *correctly* served by the empirical spectral route (`manifold/graph_atom.rs`), not by a chart family, and the census note should say so. So the parametric zoo closes with **RP² and Klein**, full stop.

## 2. RP²: even-degree mask on the spherical evaluator

Deck map `a(u) = −u` on `S² ⊂ R³`. Parity: `Y_lm(−u) = (−1)^l Y_lm(u)`.

- **Basis**: `{Y_lm : l even, 0 ≤ l ≤ 2H, |m| ≤ l}` — a mask over `SphericalHarmonicEvaluator` (`basis.rs:931`). Dimension `m_{RP²} = Σ_{l=0,2,…,2H} (2l+1) = (H+1)(2H+1)`.
- **Penalty**: `diag(l(l+1))^p` restricted to even `l`. Null space = `{Y_00}` = constants.
- **Latent**: `LatentManifold::Sphere{dim:3}` unchanged. Row objective invariant under `u → −u` (all columns even), so the antipodal fiber is exact gauge; no per-row canonicalization needed for fitting. For cross-row coordinate diagnostics, canonicalize `sign(uᵀa) > 0` against a fixed reference axis.
- **Identifiability quotient**: isometry group of RP² is `PO(3) ≅ SO(3)`; the existing sphere SO(3) gauge canonicalization applies verbatim.
- **DGP for the zoo**: the 4-component Veronese embedding `V(x,y,z) = (xy, yz, zx, ½(x²−y²))`, an embedding of RP² into `R⁴` (even in `u`, injective on the quotient). Ambient span `s = 4`, `d = 2`, so `d+1 = 3 < s = 4`: per the #2233 crossover theorem RP² is a **code-savings kind** like the torus and helix — it strengthens the curved-vs-flat MDL margin, not just the support term.

## 3. Klein bottle: parity-coupled mask on the torus evaluator

Deck map on `T²`: `ι(θ, φ) = (θ + π, −φ)`. Check: `ι² = (θ+2π, φ) = id`; `ι` is a free (no fixed points: `θ ≡ θ+π` is impossible), orientation-reversing (`dι = diag(1,−1)`, det = −1) isometry of the flat metric. `K = T²/⟨ι⟩` is the flat Klein bottle.

**Selection rule.** `e^{i(kθ+lφ)} ∘ ι = (−1)^k e^{i(kθ−lφ)}`, so `P_ι e^{i(kθ+lφ)} = ½[e^{i(kθ+lφ)} + (−1)^k e^{i(kθ−lφ)}]`. In the real torus basis of `TorusHarmonicEvaluator` (`basis.rs:1277`) this reads:

| block | survives iff |
|---|---|
| `1` | always |
| `cos kθ, sin kθ` | `k` even |
| `cos lφ` | always |
| `sin lφ` | never |
| `cos kθ cos lφ, sin kθ cos lφ` | `k` even |
| `cos kθ sin lφ, sin kθ sin lφ` | `k` odd |

Count: `m_K = 1 + 2⌊H_θ/2⌋ + H_φ + 2 H_θ H_φ` (≈ half the torus's `(2H_θ+1)(2H_φ+1)`, as it must be — `K` is a 2-fold quotient).

- **Penalty**: the torus's per-channel eigenvalues `k²`, `l²` restrict to the masked columns; the #2243 isotropic-dispersion penalty applies unchanged. Null space = constants.
- **Latent**: `Product(Circle{2π}, Circle{2π})` unchanged; row NLL is `ι`-invariant by construction.
- **Identifiability quotient**: `θ`-translations all descend (they commute with `ι`); a `φ`-translation `T_c` descends iff `c ∈ {0, π}` (conjugation by `ι` sends `T_c → T_{−c}`). Gauge group = `S¹_θ × Z₂`; reuse the circle-phase canonicalization on `θ`, fix the `Z₂` by the sign of the first `φ`-odd moment.
- **DGP**: the standard `R⁴` embedding, with `θ' ∈ [0,2π)`, `φ ∈ [0,2π)`:
  `x(θ',φ) = ((A + r cosφ)cos2θ', (A + r cosφ)sin2θ', r sinφ cosθ', r sinφ sinθ')`,
  which satisfies exactly `x(θ'+π, −φ) = x(θ', φ)` — the deck map above — and is injective on the quotient for `r < A`. Ambient span `s = 4`, so Klein is also a **code-savings kind** (`d+1 = 3 < 4`).
- **Unit test**: mirror `basis.rs:3349` — columnwise `φ(θ'+π, −φ) = φ(θ', φ)` at machine precision.

## 4. Flat vs embedded torus: a penalty distinction with closed-form entries

Both tori are the *same* chart (`(θ,φ)` on `T²`, same Fourier basis, same topology readout); what differs is the induced metric, hence the isometry-invariant penalty. The landed torus penalty (`k² + l²`) is Laplace–Beltrami for the **flat** (Clifford, `s=4`) torus. For the donut in `R³` with radii `R > r`, aspect `A = R/r`:

    ds² = r²(A + cosφ)² dθ² + r² dφ²,   √g = r²(A + cosφ)

    Δ_g f = (1/r²) [ f_θθ/(A+cosφ)² + f_φφ − sinφ/(A+cosφ) · f_φ ]

**Structure.** For `f = e^{ikθ} v(φ)`, `Δ_g f = e^{ikθ} L_k v` with `L_k v = (1/r²)[−k²(A+cosφ)^{−2} v + v'' − sinφ(A+cosφ)^{−1} v']`. The penalty `P = ∫ (Δ_g f)² √g dθ dφ` is therefore **block-diagonal in k**; within a `k`-block its entries are integrals of trig polynomials against powers `(A+cosφ)^m`, `m ∈ {−3,…,1}`, all closed-form via

    (1/2π) ∫₀^{2π} cos(nφ)/(A+cosφ) dφ = (−1)^n ζ^n / √(A²−1),   ζ = A − √(A²−1) ∈ (0,1)

and its `A`-derivatives (for `m = −2, −3`). Consequences, each derived from this generating integral:

1. **Exponential bandedness**: `|P[(k,l),(k,l')]| = O(ζ^{|l−l'|})` — truncating at bandwidth `b` incurs relative error `O(ζ^b)`; `b = ⌈log(1/ε)/log(1/ζ)⌉` rows of band suffice. For a fat torus `A = 2`: `ζ ≈ 0.27`, band ≈ 12 at `ε = 10⁻⁷`; for skinny tori the penalty is numerically diagonal — the flat penalty is recovered continuously as `A → ∞`, which is the correct limit statement of "flat vs embedded is not a dichotomy but a one-parameter metric family."
2. **Null space**: `Δ_g f = 0` on a closed manifold ⟹ `f` constant. Unchanged.
3. **Aspect ratio as an outer parameter**: `∂P/∂A` is closed-form (differentiate `ζ^n/√(A²−1)`), so `A` can join the outer optimization with an analytic gradient, or be profiled on a short grid. Identifiability: `A` is the only new scalar; the amplitude/scale gauge is already quotiented by the landed machinery.
4. **Model selection is evidence, not topology**: flat and donut tori share basis and topology; REML/evidence arbitrates the two penalties exactly the way the framework already arbitrates smoothing — no readout change needed, and the zoo can plant both and check the evidence picks the right metric.

## 5. Algorithm & complexity

- RP² and Klein evaluators = existing evaluators + a static column mask and (for Klein) paired-column symmetrization: `O(m)` overhead, jets (`SaeBasisSecondJet`/`ThirdJet`) restrict columnwise — the Möbius implementation is the template (`basis.rs:2752–2830`).
- Donut-torus penalty assembly: `O(H_θ · H_φ · b)` closed-form entries; no quadrature.
- Enum plumbing: `atom_schema.rs`, `manifold/atom.rs`, `manifold/atom_build.rs`, seed/race registration in the topology race candidates (same sites #2240 touched for Möbius).
- Topology readout cross-check: Klein = orientation-reversing holonomy + no boundary + `χ = 0`; RP² = orientation-reversing + no boundary + `χ = 1`. The current readout menu (sphere/torus/Möbius/sheet) distinguishes Möbius from Klein by the boundary detector; adding `χ ∈ {0,1}` for the non-orientable closed cases completes the decision table (`inference/atlas_nerve.rs` orientation certificate, `manifold/chart_atlas.rs:598 orientability()`).

## 6. Validation plan

1. Deck-invariance unit tests for both masks (machine precision, mirrors `basis.rs:3349`).
2. Penalty spectral tests: masked penalty eigenvalues equal the parent evaluator's on surviving columns; donut penalty at `A → ∞` converges to flat `(k²+l²)` entrywise at rate `O(1/A)`.
3. Null-space tests: constants only, penalized rank = `m − 1`.
4. Zoo objects `klein` (R⁴ embedding above) and `rp2` (Veronese), noise σ sweep: recovery `R² ≥ 0.9` at magic defaults, race winner agrees with the planted kind.
5. Flat-vs-donut discrimination: plant each, assert the evidence prefers the matching penalty at the fitted `A`.
6. MDL: assert both new kinds land on the code-savings side of the #2233 crossover table (`s = 4 > d+1 = 3`), i.e. `Δcode > 0` per firing token — unlike circle/sphere/Möbius.

## Why this is the right shape of fix

Every alternative (bespoke Klein basis, immersed-surface splines, learned charts for these cases) either duplicates the Möbius pattern without naming it or gives up closed-form penalties. The mask theorem gives: provably correct bases, inherited penalties and nulls, inherited jets, inherited gauges — and it terminates the "which shape is next" conversation with a census argument instead of a backlog.
