### ISSUE #2311 [OPEN] — Finite-sample error rates for the atlas holonomy readout: gauge-cancellation, per-cycle CLT, orientation-flip tail bound, χ confidence (#2280 readout → test)
Author: SauersML   Created: 2026-07-13T05:17:20Z   Labels: 
Comments: 3
------------------------------------------------------------------------
BODY:
# Finite-sample error rates for the atlas holonomy readout: gauge-cancellation, per-cycle CLT, orientation-flip tail bound, and a χ confidence — turning #2280's heuristic into tests

## Motivation

The atlas topology readout (#2280: `inference/atlas_nerve.rs` — `AtlasOrientationHolonomyCertificate` at :287, `ConvexIntersectionProof`; `manifold/chart_atlas.rs:598 orientability()`, `SphereChartTransition::sign()` at :251) currently reports orientability, cycle holonomy, and interior Gauss–Bonnet χ as point readouts with hand-tuned thresholds. This issue derives the finite-sample distribution of the Procrustes frame-transport holonomy under the actual noise model, yielding (i) a per-cycle z-test with a plug-in variance, (ii) an orientation-flip probability bound with explicit constants, (iii) an integer-rounding confidence for χ, and (iv) a sample-size prescription `n_patch(P, σ, λ, margin, α)` that tells the seeder how many rows per patch the readout *needs* — replacing "it seems robust" with a stated error rate. A corollary explains *why* the readout is empirically robust (holonomy noise is first-order proportional to inter-patch tilt, not to raw noise), and a cheap projection trick removes the ambient-`P` penalty from the variance.

## Noise model and estimator

Rows in patch `j`: `x_i = μ_j + U_j t_i + ε_i`, `t_i` in-plane with covariance `Λ_j` (d×d, smallest in-plane eigenvalue `λ_j`), `ε_i ~ N(0, σ²I_P)`, `n_j` rows. Local PCA gives `Û_j ∈ R^{P×d}`. Edge transition: `R̂_ab = polar(Û_aᵀÛ_b) ∈ O(d)` (Procrustes). Cycle `C = (j_0, j_1, …, j_L = j_0)`: holonomy `Ĥ_C = Π_e R̂_e`; readouts are `det Ĥ_C ∈ {±1}` (orientability) and, for `d = 2`, the angle `α̂_C` of the rotation part.

## 1. Gauge-cancellation lemma

Per-patch PCA bases are arbitrary up to `Q_j ∈ O(d)`; under regauging, `R̂_ab → Q_aᵀ R̂_ab Q_b` and `Ĥ_C → Q_{j_0}ᵀ Ĥ_C Q_{j_0}`. Hence `det Ĥ_C` is exactly gauge-invariant, and for `d = 2` the conjugation preserves `|α̂_C|` (a reflection gauge flips its sign — report `|α̂_C|`). **The cycle holonomy is a function of the estimated projectors `P̂_j = Û_jÛ_jᵀ` alone**; all randomness enters through subspace (out-of-plane) error, never through in-plane basis choice. This is the exact statement of "the readout only trusts local primitives."

## 2. Subspace fluctuation input

Write `δ_j = (I − U_jU_jᵀ) Û_j` (out-of-plane error, the only gauge-free error). Two standard inputs, both stated with constants in the issue implementation notes:

- **First-order distribution** (Anderson-type asymptotics for the spiked model, in-plane spike `λ + σ²` vs noise floor `σ²`): each column `δ_{j,a}` is asymptotically Gaussian in the normal space with per-direction variance `γ_j / n_j`, where

      γ_j = σ²(λ_j + σ²) / λ_j²

- **Non-asymptotic tail** (Davis–Kahan + Koltchinskii–Lounici): with probability ≥ 1 − e^{−t},

      ‖sinΘ(Û_j, U_j)‖ ≤ C √(γ_j (d + t)/n_j) · (1 + √(P/n_j))

  The `√(P/n_j)` factor is the high-dimensional price; §5 removes it.

## 3. Per-edge and per-cycle distribution (d = 2)

Gauge patches so true frames are Procrustes-aligned along the cycle. Let `θ_e` be the principal angle between the true tangent planes of edge `e = (a,b)` (small for a good cover). Perturbing `M̂_e = Û_aᵀÛ_b` to first order:

    δM_e = δ_aᵀ U_b + U_aᵀ δ_b

and the polar angle picks up `δα_e = ½(δM_{e,21} − δM_{e,12})` (from `polar(R(1 + N)) ≈ R·exp(skew(N))`).

**Key structural fact**: `δ_a ⊥ U_a`, so `δ_aᵀU_b` is `O(sin θ_e)` — if the two planes coincide, the *first-order* angle noise vanishes identically and only the second-order term `δ_aᵀδ_b` survives. Carrying both orders:

    Var(α̂_C) ≈ Σ_{e=(a,b)∈C} sin²θ_e (γ_a/n_a + γ_b/n_b) · κ_e   +   Σ_e (P − d) γ_aγ_b /(2 n_a n_b)

with `κ_e ≤ 1` a computable in-plane geometry factor (exact expression from the tilt direction's decomposition in the two frames; adjacent edges share a patch, and the shared-patch contributions enter the cycle sum with signed weights whose covariance is included in the plug-in formula — everything is a quadratic form in the per-patch Gaussians, so the exact cycle variance is computable, not just bounded). First term: noise ∝ **tilt × subspace error** — this is the theorem behind the observed robustness. Second term: the ambient-dimension floor, dominant when `P` is large (P = 2048!) and tilts are small; §5 kills it.

**Bias**: the true composed transport around `C` differs from the continuum holonomy `∫∫_D K dA` (disk `D` spanned by `C`) by the discretization `O(Σ_e θ_e³)`; this is a deterministic geometric term, not noise, and is inherited by any transport scheme — state it, don't test against it.

**Test (i) — trivial holonomy / winding**: reject `H_0: α_C = 0` when `|α̂_C| > z_{1−α/2} · τ̂_C`, `τ̂_C²` the plug-in of the display above (θ̂_e from principal angles of `Û_aᵀÛ_b`, γ̂_j from the patch spectrum, n_j known). This upgrades the circle-vs-disk and cone-point readouts to stated type-I error. Multiple cycles: the nerve has `E − V + 1` independent cycles; Bonferroni over a fundamental cycle basis.

## 4. Orientation flip: a discrete margin bound

`det R̂_e = sign det(Û_aᵀÛ_b)`, and `det(U_aᵀU_b) = Π_i cos θ_{e,i}` has margin `m_e = Π cos θ_{e,i} > 0`. A flip on edge `e` requires the subspace perturbations to move a determinant by `m_e`, which requires `‖sinΘ‖`-level error `≳ m_e/2d`. Union-bounding the non-asymptotic tail over the `E` edges of the certificate:

    P(any edge orientation misread) ≤ E · exp( − c · n_min · m_min² / (d · γ_max (1 + P/n_min)) )

with explicit `c` from Gaussian concentration of the empirical covariance. Inverting gives the **seeder prescription**:

    n_patch ≥ (C/m²) · γ · ( d + log(E/α) + √(P·(d + log(E/α))) )

i.e. the certificate can *demand* patch occupancy before it signs. `AtlasOrientationEdge` (atlas_nerve.rs:254) should carry `(θ̂_e, m̂_e, n_a, n_b, γ̂_a, γ̂_b)` and the certificate a `flip_probability_bound: f64` — a certificate that states its own error rate instead of `sign: i8` alone.

## 5. Removing the ambient-P penalty (implementation win)

All statistics of an edge depend only on the relative geometry of two d-planes and their noise. Project the two patches' rows onto `span(Û_a^{(d+q)}, Û_b^{(d+q)})` (top `d+q` local PCs each, `q ≈ 3`) *before* the Procrustes step: the edge statistics are preserved to `O(‖sinΘ‖²)` while `P` in every variance and tail above is replaced by `2(d+q)`. For `P = 2048`, this is a variance reduction of ~two orders of magnitude in the second-order term and removes `√(P/n)` from the flip bound — patches of 50–100 rows become certifiably sufficient where the raw-P bound demands thousands. This is a ~20-line change at the single site that assembles `Û_aᵀÛ_b`.

## 6. Gauss–Bonnet χ with a confidence

The interior-χ readout sums angle defects: `2πχ̂ = Σ_v (2π − Σ_{t∋v} β̂_{v,t}) + (boundary terms)`. Each measured angle `β̂` is a smooth function of noisy landmark coordinates: `Var(β̂) ≈ σ²/(n_v ℓ̄²)`-scale with `ℓ̄` the local edge length — propagate per-vertex, sum (patches disjoint ⟹ independent up to shared boundary vertices, included in the plug-in). Since χ is an integer:

    P(round(χ̂) ≠ χ) ≤ 2 Φ̄( π / sd(2πχ̂) )

Report `χ` **with this confidence**. Combined with §4, the readout decision table (sphere/torus/Möbius/sheet — and Klein/RP² per the census issue) becomes a likelihood over discrete hypotheses with stated per-branch error, rather than a cascade of thresholds.

## Algorithm summary & complexity

Per edge: principal angles + plug-in variance, `O((d+q)³)` after §5 projection (`O(P d²)` to build the projection — already paid by PCA). Per cycle: sum + z-test, `O(L)`. Flip bound: closed form per certificate. No new solvers, no iteration; strictly additive fields on existing certificate structs (`atlas_nerve.rs:254–318`), one projection insertion, thresholds replaced by `(α, bound)` pairs.

## Validation plan

1. **Calibration under H₀**: flat sheet DGP, sweep (n_patch, σ, P, tilt): empirical rejection rate of test (i) vs nominal α on 10³ replicates; the plug-in τ̂_C within 15% of Monte-Carlo sd.
2. **Power**: cone-point and winding DGPs at controlled holonomy; power curve vs the derived noncentrality.
3. **Flip bound sanity**: Möbius band, shrink n_patch until flips appear; observed flip rate ≤ bound everywhere (bound may be loose; must never be violated).
4. **χ confidence**: sphere/torus/Klein DGPs; `round(χ̂)` correct whenever stated confidence ≥ 95%, and the failure cases concentrate where the confidence says they should.
5. **§5 projection**: identical decisions vs raw-P pipeline at equal seeds, variance ratio ≈ (d+q)/P.
6. Re-run the landed readout acceptance fixtures (sphere/torus/möbius/sheet) asserting the new certificates reproduce the old decisions with confidence ≥ 0.99 at current patch sizes — i.e. the theory certifies the readout we already trust.

## Relation to in-flight work

- #2280 end-state: this is the missing "(c) discrete topology readout with error rate"; the certificate structs it upgrades are exactly the ones the atlas promotion gate consumes.
- Census issue (Klein/RP²): §4+§6 provide the two extra decision-table rows those kinds need.
- #2233/MDL: a readout with stated error rate can be *priced* — a topology hypothesis at confidence `1−ε` adds `H(ε)` bits to the description length, making atlas→zoo promotion an honest MDL event instead of a hard switch.

### ISSUE #2312 [OPEN] — Outer REML ρ-geometry: per-mode decomposition, Sturm certificate for saddle count, exact global 1-D solves, explicit ARC Lipschitz constant
Author: SauersML   Created: 2026-07-13T05:17:21Z   Labels: 
Comments: 3
------------------------------------------------------------------------
BODY:
# Outer REML geometry: exact per-mode decomposition of V(ρ), a Sturm certificate for quasi-convexity / saddle count, exact global 1-D solves, and an explicit ARC Lipschitz constant

## Motivation

The E1 campaign established two outer-ρ failure classes empirically: interior saddle stalls and boundary (λ→0 / λ→∞) pathologies. Both are currently handled *reactively* (exact analytic outer HVP + ARC to cross saddles; boundary guards). This issue derives the exact 1-D structure of the REML/LAML criterion in ρ = log λ and turns it into: (1) a **computable a-priori certificate** for the number of stationary points along each ρ coordinate (quasi-convex? saddle? boundary attractor?) costing one generalized eigendecomposition we already compute; (2) an **exact global 1-D solve** per coordinate (root isolation of a polynomial), giving a coordinate-descent outer step that cannot stall at axis-visible saddles; (3) a **numerically uniform evaluation form** that is regular at both ρ → ±∞ (the λ→0 gradient non-finiteness is a parametrization artifact, not a property of the criterion); (4) an **explicit third-derivative Lipschitz constant** for the ARC cubic weight, replacing adaptive guessing on the first iterations. Everything below is exact for the Gaussian working model along one ρ coordinate with the other blocks frozen — which is precisely the object the outer optimizer differentiates at each step.

## 1. Per-mode decomposition

Single penalized block along coordinate `ρ = log λ`, other blocks folded into `H = XᵀWX + Σ_{j≠k} λ_j S_j` (fixed, PD on the relevant space). Generalized eigenvalues `s_i > 0` of `(S_k, H)`, `i = 1..m` (m = penalized rank), transformed responses `z_i` (units where H = I), `c_i = z_i²/(2σ²)`. The REML criterion (deviance + penalty + ½log|H+λS| − ½log|λS|_+, Wood-2011 form) decomposes exactly as

    V(ρ) = Σ_{i=1}^m f(u_i; c_i) + const,   u_i = ρ + log s_i
    f(u; c) = c·σ(u) + ½ log(1+e^u) − ½ u,   σ(u) = e^u/(1+e^u)

(The `c·σ(u)` term is the penalized-RSS contribution `z_i² λs_i/(1+λs_i)/(2σ²)`; the second and third give `½log((1+λs_i)/(λs_i))`.) Each mode is a **two-parameter scalar family**; every claim below is algebra on `f`.

Derivatives (all verified by direct differentiation, `σ' = σ(1−σ)`):

    f'(u; c)  = (1 − σ)(cσ − ½)
    f''(u; c) = σ(1−σ)·[c(1−2σ) + ½]
    f'''(u; c)= σ(1−σ)·{ (1−2σ)[c(1−2σ)+½] − 2cσ(1−σ) }

## 2. The phase portrait of one mode

- `u → −∞`: `f' → −½`. **Every mode pushes λ up out of the λ→0 boundary with slope exactly −m/2 in total** — the criterion is perfectly regular there. The λ→0 outer-gradient non-finiteness seen in the E1 fixtures is an artifact of assembling `½log|H+λS| − ½log|λS|_+` as two separately divergent terms; the per-mode form `½[log(1+e^u) − u]` is uniformly stable. Immediate recommendation: `rho_optimizer/objective.rs` should evaluate the log-det difference in this fused per-mode form whenever the diagonalization is available (it is — the same quantities feed the EDF).
- `u → +∞`: `f' ~ e^{−u}(c − ½)`.
- **Noise mode** (`c ≤ ½`): `f' ≤ 0` everywhere — monotone pull toward λ = ∞.
- **Signal mode** (`c > ½`): single sign change − → + at the *crossing* `σ(u*) = 1/(2c)`, i.e.

      ρ_i* = −log s_i − log(2c_i − 1)

So `V'` is a sum of m single-crossing/nonpositive terms: `V' < 0` for `ρ < min_i ρ_i*` always (left bracket is exact), and the sign at +∞ is that of `T = Σ_i (c_i − ½)/s_i`. `T ≤ 0` ⟹ the criterion decreases into the total-smoothing boundary (the λ→∞ attractor class); `T > 0` ⟹ at least one interior minimum exists.

## 3. The Sturm certificate: exact stationary-point count

Substituting `σ = λs/(1+λs)`:

    V'(λ) = Σ_i [ (c_i − ½) λ s_i − ½ ] / (1 + λ s_i)²

so `N(λ) := V'(λ)·Π_j (1+λs_j)²` is a **polynomial of degree ≤ 2m−1** with closed-form coefficients (`O(m²)` to assemble by incremental multiplication). Its positive real roots are exactly the interior stationary points of V. Therefore:

- **Root count by Sturm sequence** (or sign-change isolation on the crossing grid `{ρ_i*}` refined by bisection — the sum-of-sigmoids form of `V'` is the numerically stable evaluator; the polynomial is the exactness certificate): the number `S` of stationary points is *decided*, not guessed.
- `S = 1` ⟹ **V is strictly quasi-convex** on R (unique interior minimum; V′ < 0 before, > 0 after): any descent method converges globally; ARC needs no saddle logic on this coordinate.
- `S ≥ 3` (S is odd when `T > 0`) ⟹ multi-basin: the even-indexed roots are local maxima = **exact basin boundaries**. This is the a-priori detector for the E1 interior-stall class, available before the first outer iteration.
- All-noise (`∀i: c_i ≤ ½`) ⟹ `V' < 0` everywhere: short-circuit to the λ_max boundary with zero iterations, and *label* the block as evidence-free (this is diagnostic output the collapse/death machinery can consume).

Cost: the generalized eigendecomposition of `(S_k, H)` is already computed for EDF/log-det channels; the certificate adds `O(m²)` scalar work. m = penalized block rank (tens to a few hundred) — negligible.

## 4. Exact global 1-D solve and saddle-free coordinate descent

Given the roots, the global minimizer along ρ_k is `argmin` of V over ≤ m candidate minima (odd-indexed roots) + boundary behavior — an **exact global solve of the REML problem in one smoothing parameter**, replacing iteration entirely in the single-λ case.

Multi-λ: freeze `λ_{j≠k}`, and both log-det terms along λ_k are again `Σ log(1 + λ_k e_q)` over generalized eigenvalues (of `S_k` against `H_k` and against `A_k = Σ_{j≠k}λ_jS_j` on its range, the latter entering negatively), and the deviance term is again `Σ c σ`; so `V'_k × denominators` is again a polynomial and the same certificate + exact solve applies per coordinate. **Exact coordinate descent**: sweep k, each step a global 1-D minimization ⟹ V strictly decreases; accumulation points are coordinatewise-global minima. This escapes (i) every strict saddle with an axis-aligned descent direction and (ii) every point where a *distant* basin along some axis is lower — i.e. the stall class where line-search methods sit at tiny gradients in a shallow basin. Honest caveat: saddles whose negative curvature lives only in mixed directions survive coordinate descent; those remain ARC/HVP territory (task#7 PATH C). The two mechanisms are complementary, and the certificate tells you per coordinate which regime you are in.

Second caveat, stated plainly: for non-Gaussian families the inner solution moves with λ, so the decomposition is exact for the *working model* (PQL-fixed weights) at the current inner solve — the correct local model the outer step already uses. Use the exact solve as the trust-model step / seed, keep the existing acceptance test as arbiter. Nothing here weakens the #2253 stationary-only contract: the certificate and 1-D solves are performed on the same objective the contract owns; no FD, no alternative gradient path.

## 5. Seeding and the explicit ARC constant

- **Seed**: the global 1-D minimizer per block (from §4 with `H = XᵀWX` + current other blocks at their own seeds, one Gauss–Seidel pass). This strictly generalizes the landed closed-form DR ρ* seed — that seed is the one-mode moment-matched surrogate of this m-mode exact solve; when the eigendecomposition is in hand, use the exact one. Bracket for free: the global min lies in `[min_i ρ_i*, ρ_max-root]`.
- **ARC cubic weight**: from the `f'''` bound, `σ(1−σ) ≤ ¼`, `|1−2σ| ≤ 1`:

      |V'''(ρ)| ≤ Σ_i (3c_i + 1)/8 =: L₃

  along each coordinate (and the same bound holds for third directional derivatives of the multi-ρ criterion in the simultaneously-diagonalizable case; use it as the initialization scale otherwise). Cubic regularization with weight `M ≥ L₃` gives the standard global second-order convergence guarantee (Nesterov–Polyak / Cartis–Gould–Toint) with **no adaptive warm-up**, and combined with `S = 1` from the certificate, convergence to the global minimum from *any* seed — a provable basin statement: the basin is all of R when the certificate says quasi-convex, and is exactly the interval between adjacent even-indexed roots otherwise.

## 6. Algorithm summary

Per outer setup (and cheaply refreshable): for each penalized block k — (a) generalized eigens of `(S_k, H_k)` [already computed]; (b) `c_i` from transformed residuals; (c) assemble N(λ), Sturm count, isolate roots; (d) emit `RhoLandscapeCertificate { stationary_points, basins, tail_sign T, all_noise flag, L3 }`; (e) seed/step = global 1-D argmin. Complexity: `O(m²)` per block per refresh, zero extra factorizations.

## 7. Validation plan

1. **Exactness**: random `(H, S, z)` draws (m ≤ 200): root count equals sign changes of V′ on a 10⁶-point grid; global 1-D argmin matches grid argmin to 1e−10 in ρ. Property test over 10³ draws.
2. **Boundary regularity**: evaluate the fused per-mode form at ρ = ±40; assert finite value/gradient where the current two-term assembly overflows or cancels (reproduces then kills the λ→0 fixture failure mode).
3. **E1 interior fixtures**: assert the certificate reports `S ≥ 3` on the known saddle-stall fixtures and `S = 1` on the benign ones; exact coordinate descent reaches the profile global min on the fixtures where the current path stalls (StepSizeTooSmall class).
4. **All-noise short-circuit**: pure-noise block → certificate flags monotone, optimizer performs zero iterations on that coordinate, final λ at the boundary policy value.
5. **ARC constant**: with `M = L₃` fixed (no adaptation), iteration counts on the fixture set within 2× of the adaptive scheme, zero rejected steps (the theory says none can be rejected at `M ≥ L₃`).
6. **Non-Gaussian honesty**: binomial/Poisson fits — exact-1D step used as proposal only; assert monotone outer decrease and no acceptance-test regressions vs current path.

## File anchors

`crates/gam-solve/src/rho_optimizer/objective.rs` (fused per-mode evaluation, certificate emission), `rho_optimizer/seed_screening.rs` (exact seed replaces surrogate), `rho_optimizer/run.rs` / `capability.rs` (coordinate-exact step + ARC weight = L₃ wiring), `gaussian_reml.rs` (single-λ exact solve fast path). Read-only consumers: collapse/death diagnostics (all-noise flag), E1 fixture suite.

--- comment by SauersML at 2026-07-13T08:17:06Z ---
Source audit update for #2312 (implementation in progress, remote validation pending):

- The issue's proposed mode formula assumes a fixed sigma. Production Gaussian REML profiles dispersion at every rho: dp_j(rho) = y'Wy - sum_i c_ij^2/(1 + exp(rho) delta_i), so the fixed-sigma polynomial/Sturm roots are not roots of the fitted objective.
- The existing profiled enumerator had two concrete correctness holes: it returned a best candidate when non-monotone cells hit its rho resolution floor (the production callers discarded hit_resolution_floor), and it admitted the arbitrary init rho into the final argmin even when that seed was nonstationary.
- The multi-lambda "exact cyclic" route was also not exact for overlapping blocks: the coupled pseudo-determinant log|sum_j lambda_j S_j|_+ does not separate into per-block rank_j * rho_j terms. That route also skipped failed pencils and returned after 16 passes without a convergence certificate.

The source repair now keeps the actual profiled objective, evaluates every modal kernel in log-t space (finite even beyond exp range), uses conservative derivative/curvature enclosures with endpoint-jet checks, returns typed RemlDidNotConverge on unresolved structure, uses init only as a refinement hint, and removes the invalid coupled cyclic API/seed. Added analytic one-mode profiled-root, typed-refusal, and boundary-regularity tests; no grid oracle is used by the new tests.
